    　　○圣瑞

    　　仁祖先家于泗，后徙濠梁。所居密迩一兰若，与其主僧交颇厚，僧每钦服仁祖之纯诚。一夕，望其舍火光烛天，为之嗟惜曰：「朱公善人，天忍殃之乎！」弥月而仁祖至，僧唁之，答曰：「此夕妇生一男，恐有触污，故久不来践佛地，非有回禄之祸也。」男即高皇帝云。

    　　○太学

    　　相传高皇帝时，初起太学，上临视之，顾学制宏丽，圣情甚悦。行至广业堂前，偶发一言云：「天下有福儿郎，应得居此。」迄今百四十年来，学生居此堂者，往往占魁选，跻位通贵，他所不及也。又诸堂中都无蜘蛛，云上来时，见蛛布网屋隅，曰：「我纔建屋，尔輙据之耶？」顾叱之出，语讫而蛛遯，从兹遂绝。

    Explanation

    5

    Final Translation

    Yuanjiang Lin

    • Huán Lóng (Housing Dragons)
    • Yǎnzhōu Yù Miào (Temple of the Mountain God in Yǎnzhōu)
    • Wáng Quán
    • Guǐ Bīng (Army of Ghosts)
    • Shǒu Yín Quǎn (Guardian Silver Dog)
    • Cūn Mín Yùu Tǔdì (Villager Meets the Local Land God)
    • Zhú Pǔ Yìwù (Strange Things in a Bamboo Garden)
    • Kōngtóng Shānrén (Hermit of the Kunlun Mountains)
    • Zhāng Qiū Bó Jìn (Burning of Silk in Zhāng Qiū)
    • Wáng Gēng
    • Língzhī (Ginseng)
    • Mǎ Guǐ (Horse Ghost)
    • Sān Zú Biē (Three-Footed Turtle)

    ○ Divine Auspice

    The ancestor of Renzong (Zhu Yuanzhang) originally lived in Sui, later moving to Huaibei. His residence was close to a monastery, and he had a very close relationship with the abbot, who admired Renzong's sincerity. One night, he saw a fire in his house lighting up the sky and lamented, saying, "Mr. Zhu is a good man, how could heaven bring disaster upon him!" After a month, Renzong returned, and the abbot condoled him. Renzong replied, "Tonight, my wife gave birth to a boy, and I feared there might be some impurity, so I have not come to the Buddhist ground for a long time; it is not a disaster from the fire god." The boy is the High Emperor.

    ○ Imperial Academy

    It is said that during the reign of the High Emperor, the Imperial Academy was first established. The emperor visited it and was very pleased with the grandeur and beauty of the academy. As he walked to the Guangye Hall, he happened to say, "A fortunate young man should be able to live here." Since then, for over 140 years, students who have lived in this hall have often achieved top ranks, rising to high positions and great wealth, which others could not match. Additionally, there are no spiders in any of the halls. It is said that when the academy was built, the emperor saw a spider weaving a web in a corner of the house and said, "I just built this house, and you dare to occupy it?" He scolded the spider and it fled. From then on, spiders were completely gone.

    6

    ○贡院

    　　南京贡院，锦衣指挥纪纲宅也。纲有宠文皇帝朝，后坐不法伏诛，阖门受歼于是。 【 或云生瘗其下。】 至今每乡试时，举子入院，輙有声自地中起，历诸号房上，如万马腾踏者云。

    　　○平保儿

    　　都指挥平安，一名保儿。建文末为将，败北兵于小河。安单骑追蹑燕王，运槊将及之，忽空中有黑龙，舒爪掣其臂，安马跪于地。安知天命有在，叹息收兵而止。后兵败被擒，见王，问之曰：「小河之役，倘相及何如？」安应曰：「臣欲生致使长耳。 【 时国家沿元氏旧俗，诸皇子皆呼「使长」。】 不然，未可量也。」王劳而赦之，命掌北平都司事。后以旧人自疑，经死。

    Explanation

    6

    The Examination Hall

    The Nanjing Examination Hall was originally the residence of Jin Yi Commandant Ji Gang. Ji Gang was favored by the Hongwu Emperor during the Ming Dynasty, but later he was punished for illegal acts and executed, with his entire family being killed there. Some say they were buried alive there. To this day, every time the provincial examinations are held, when the candidates enter the hall, there is always a sound rising from the ground, passing over all the examination rooms, like the galloping of ten thousand horses, so it is said.

    Ping Bao'er

    General Ping An, also known as Ping Bao'er, served as a general at the end of the Jianwen era. He defeated the northern army at Xiao River. Ping An pursued the Prince of Yan on horseback alone, was about to catch up with him with his spear, when suddenly there was a black dragon in the sky, extended its claws and grabbed his arm, causing his horse to kneel on the ground. Ping An knew that fate was in play, sighed, gathered his troops, and stopped. Later, his army was defeated and he was captured. When he met the King, the King asked him, "What if I had caught up with you?" Ping An replied, "I wanted to capture you alive to serve as your attendant. At that time, the country followed the old customs of the Yuan dynasty, and all the princes called their attendants 'shizhang'. Otherwise, it would be hard to predict." The King rewarded and pardoned him, ordering him to take charge of the Beiping Commandery. Later, due to suspicion of his old connections, he was executed.

    7

    ○袁珙

    　　袁太常珙相术之妙，在胜国时已擅天下。洪武初，姚少师广孝为缁流，寓嵩山寺。珙一见即以匡辅器期之，曰：「公，刘秉忠之俦也。」后广孝以高僧选入燕邸，预密谋，言珙于王，王亦素闻其人，乃托以珙名隶尺籍，遣旗勾取。既至，未即得见，阴命选卫中长身多髯，貌与王类者九人，王杂其中，俱微服适市，拉珙入酒肆饮，王位列第三。珙遽前引其裾，俯伏呼殿下。众哂其妄，珙言愈切，王即起还宫，召珙入见。珙曰：「殿下千里召臣，而于酒肆相见乎？」问何以能识，对曰：「殿下入肆时，手操弓矢，臣望见知之，皮皱而瘦，龙掌无肉也。

    Explanation

    7

    Yuan Taichang Góng's skill in physiognomy was renowned throughout the previous dynasty. At the beginning of the Hongwu era, Yáo Shàoshī Guǎngxiào, a highly respected monk, resided at Songshan Temple. Upon first meeting Góng, he immediately recognized him as a person capable of assisting and supporting, saying, "You are comparable to Liu Bingzhong." Later, Yáo was selected as a high-ranking monk and brought into the Prince of Yan's residence, where he participated in secret planning. He spoke of Góng to the prince, who had also heard of him before. The prince then claimed that Góng was listed in the military register and sent a flag to summon him. After Góng arrived, he did not immediately meet the prince. Instead, the prince secretly ordered the selection of nine men from the guard who were tall, had beards, and resembled the prince in appearance. The prince mixed among them, all dressed in plain clothes and went to the market. They pulled Góng into a tavern for a drink, with the prince seated third. Góng suddenly approached and pulled at the prince's sleeve, bowing and calling him "Your Highness." The others laughed at his absurdity, but Góng spoke more insistently. The prince then stood up, returned to the palace, and summoned Góng to meet him. Góng said, "Your Highness summoned me from afar, yet we met in a tavern?" When asked how he recognized him, Góng replied, "When Your Highness entered the tavern, I saw him holding a bow and arrow. I recognized him by sight; his skin was wrinkled and thin, and his hand was like a dragon's, without flesh."

    8

    」 【 世所传「辨宰相于嵩山佛寺，识真王于长安酒家者」即此。】 更使详视，因极道天表之盛，曰：「年交四十，髯长过脐，当登大宝，必为二十年太平天子。」王悦，由此遂决大计。珙留燕城未久，遇列校散卒，多以公侯、大臣官许之，语往往流播。王恐有他虞，因遣还乡。其后渡江登极，驿召至京，拜太常丞，赐与甚厚。及议建储，上意有所属，迟回累年，使珙相仁宗，曰：「后代人主。」又相宣宗曰「万年天子」。于是国本始定。他日见仁宗于东宫，问曰：「吾寿得几何？」对曰：「过七七之年，天福无疆。」及乙巳鼎成，竟如此数云。子忠彻亦传其术，官至尚宝卿。

    Explanation

    8

    The world-famous story of "distinguishing the prime minister at a Buddhist temple on Mount Song and recognizing the true king at a tavern in Chang'an" refers to this event. Gong was then asked to examine the king closely, and he greatly praised the grandeur of his appearance, saying, "At the age of forty, he will have a beard that extends beyond his navel, and he will ascend to the throne, becoming a peaceful emperor for twenty years." The king was pleased, and thus he decided on a major plan. Gong stayed in Yan City for a short time, where he met officers and soldiers, promising many of them the titles of marquis, viscount, or high-ranking official. These promises often spread far and wide. Fearing other potential problems, the king sent Gong back to his hometown. Later, when the king crossed the river and ascended to the throne, Gong was summoned by imperial edict to the capital and appointed as the Grand Master of Rites, receiving generous gifts. When the matter of selecting a crown prince came up, the emperor had a particular preference, hesitating for many years. He sent Gong to assess Emperor Renzong, saying, "He will be the future emperor." Gong also assessed Emperor Xuanzong, saying, "He will be the emperor for a thousand years." Thus, the foundation of the state was finally established. One day, Gong met Emperor Renzong in the East Palace, where the emperor asked, "How long will my life be?" Gong replied, "Beyond the age of forty-nine, your blessings will be boundless." When the year Bihai (乙巳) came, it turned out exactly as predicted. Gong's son, Zhongche, also inherited his skill and reached the rank of Grand Master of the Imperial Seal.

    9

    ○登科先兆

    　　伯父工部公，在乡校累举不第，以贡入南雍。弘治戊午乡试，有别舍生徽人汪某者，梦与苏州监生陆某忿争相持，诉于祭酒，祭酒麾之出，曰：「陆某非此间人矣。」寤而莫测所以，盖汪与伯父平生无半面识也。间为苏士某言之，某来以告伯父 【 某来以告伯父　原本下无「伯父」两字，据说库本补。】 。既揭榜，伯父中选，汪竟无名。及会试至京，以岁旦往谒故吴文定公宽，公时佐吏部。适昆山毛宪清澄、朱懋忠希周二修撰皆在坐。三公皆吾乡殿魁也。俄有云南解元周文亦入谒，相见各道姓名。有顷辞出，伯父与周偕行，周意色惨沮，行且问曰：「君之先世 【 君之先世　原本作「君之相见」，据说库本改。】 ，得无有善事乎？」伯父唯唯未对。

    Explanation

    9

    Translation

    Omens of Passing the Imperial Examination

    My uncle, who served in the Ministry of Works, had failed repeatedly in the local exams but was admitted to the Imperial Academy in Nanjing through the imperial recommendation system. During the provincial exam of the Wuxu year of the Hongzhi era, a junior student from Huizhou named Wang had a dream in which he was fiercely arguing with a Suzhou scholar named Lu. They complained to the chief examiner, who dismissed them, saying, "Lu is not from here." Upon waking, Wang could not understand the meaning of the dream, as he and my uncle had never met before. Later, Wang told a Suzhou scholar about it, and the scholar came to inform my uncle. After the results were announced, my uncle was selected, while Wang did not make the list. When my uncle went to the capital for the metropolitan exam on New Year's Day, he visited the late Wu Wending, who was then serving as an assistant in the Ministry of Personnel. Coincidentally, Mao Qingshu from Kunshan and Zhu Maizhong and Zhou Xizhong, both scholars who held the rank of Xiu Zuan, were also present. The three officials were all top scholars from my hometown. Soon after, Zhou Wen, the top scholar from Yunnan, also paid a visit. They introduced themselves and exchanged names. After a while, they left, and my uncle walked with Zhou. Zhou looked gloomy and asked, "Have your ancestors done any good deeds?" My uncle nodded but did not answer.

    10

    周曰：「予此言有谓也。予丙辰岁尝梦至殿庭，方传唱进士名，予立庭下，自谓当在列。俄一物自空坠下，视之，乃金宫花一朵，欲取戴之。旁有人止之曰：『尔不得取，此苏州陆宣公子孙物也。彼家有阴德，当受此。』转顾则已为一人簪于首矣。予此来方物色其人，今遇君既苏人陆姓，且岁首遇三殿魁，又皆苏人，此殆君得隽之兆也。吾其终无成乎！」伯父唯唯而已。夜归邸中，向从者道之，且讶宣公之语。老仆许聪者忽应曰：「主忘之耶，吾家老官人非名『宣』乎！」盖先曾大父讳与宣同音而旁加王也，伯父乃悟而异之。既而果擢甲科。周讫不第，以选调得官。 【 伯父举进士时，梦乘肩舆八一佛庐，且梦草狱词。既乃得大理寺观政云。辛未附记。】

    Explanation

    10

    Zhou said, "These words of mine carry meaning. In the year of Bingchen, I once dreamed of arriving at the palace courtyard, where the names of the Jinshi (imperial scholars) were being announced. I stood at the foot of the courtyard, thinking I would be among them. Suddenly, an object fell from the sky. Upon seeing it, it was a golden palace flower. I wanted to take it and wear it. Someone nearby stopped me and said, 'You cannot take it; this is the property of the descendants of Lu Xuan Gong from Suzhou. Their family has accumulated good deeds, and they should receive this.' Turning around, I saw that it had already been placed on the head of someone else. Since then, I have been looking for this person. Now I have met you, who are a Lu from Suzhou, and you are the first to meet the top three in the palace examinations this year, and you are all from Suzhou. This is likely a sign of your success. Shall I never succeed?' My uncle nodded in agreement. At night, returning to the inn, I told my attendant about it, and I was surprised by the words of Xuan Gong. The old servant Xu Cong suddenly replied, 'Have you forgotten? Our old master's name was not "Xuan"?' It was my great-grandfather's name, which had the same pronunciation as 'Xuan' but added a 'wang' on the side. My uncle then understood and was surprised. Soon after, he was indeed selected as the top candidate. Zhou, however, never passed and obtained an official position through selection and appointment. [My uncle, when he took the Jinshi examination, dreamed of riding in a sedan chair to a Buddhist temple, and he also dreamed of drafting a legal document. Later, he obtained the position of Observing Affairs at the Imperial Court of Justice.] Recorded in the year Xinwei.

    11

    ○揣骨僧

    　　正统间，虎丘半塘寺有僧两目皆盲，善揣骨，言人贵贱祸福多奇中。粲之外大父胡公，年数岁时，家人携往求揣骨，僧云：「儿他日应得系金带，好自爱也。」后公举进士，累官至山西参议，致仕果终四品。里人石乙贫，为人佣织，以二子见僧，揣之，喜索厚谢，曰：「此两财主骨也。」谓石云：「勿轻视尔儿。」闻者初不信，二子长，果以赀雄于乡。龚大者家颇温裕，为人丰肥，腹脐间黑痣有毫长数寸，尝言其一生福皆在此。龚平日与人语，好大笑。一日在僧所，方笑未已，僧顾曰：「勿笑，明年尔腹间毛落死矣！」龚恶其语，不答。后偶就浴，摩挲间，毫忽落，又数日病死 【 又数日病死　原本作「又数日死」，据说库本补。】 。

    Explanation

    11

    Translation:

    The Bone-Reading Monk

    During the reign of Emperor Yingzong, there was a monk at the Half-Tank Temple in Tiger Hill who was blind in both eyes but skilled in bone-reading. He often predicted the fortunes and misfortunes of people with remarkable accuracy. When Càn’s great-grandfather, Hu Gong, was a child, his family took him to the monk for a bone reading. The monk said, “This child will one day hold a high official position, so take good care of him.” Later, Hu Gong passed the imperial examinations and rose through the ranks to become a Censorial Councillor of Shanxi Province, ultimately retiring as a Fourth-Rank official.

    In the same village, there was a man named Shi Yi, who was poor and worked as a hired weaver. He brought his two sons to the monk for a reading. The monk was pleased and asked for a generous reward, saying, “These two boys have the bones of wealthy men.” He advised Shi Yi, “Do not underestimate your sons.” At first, those who heard the prediction did not believe it, but as the boys grew older, they indeed became wealthy and influential in the village.

    Another man, Gong Dà, came from a relatively prosperous family. He was stout and had a black mole with a long hair several inches long on his navel. He once remarked that all his good fortune was concentrated in that mole. Gong was known for his hearty laughter and often laughed loudly when speaking to others. One day, while at the monk’s temple, he was still laughing when the monk looked at him and said, “Do not laugh! Next year, the hair on your navel will fall out, and you will die!” Gong was displeased with the monk’s words and did not respond. Later, when he was bathing and rubbing his navel, the hair suddenly fell out. A few days later, he fell ill and died.

    12

    ○沅江麟

    　　成化七年秋，常德沅江县之东田村民冯贵家牝牛，自孕而生一麟。生时云雾滃合，红光满室。其形畧如鹿，蹄及尾皆如牛，周身有麟，额上一骨锐坚，隐起肉间，盖其角也。初出胎跳跃，人不能制。民愚以为怪物，击之，伤右胁而死。后有识其为麟者，郡守杨宣令取其腊，藏库中。予外祖参议公佐郡日，常命取观，岁久骨肉已化，惟存空皮，麟亦间有脱落。诸姨及仆妾辈皆见之。

    Explanation

    12

    Qilin of the Yuan River

    In the autumn of the seventh year of the Chenghua era, a female cow belonging to a villager named Feng Gui in Dongtian Village, Dongyang County, Chenzhou Prefecture, gave birth to a Qilin. At the time of its birth, clouds and mist gathered, and the room was filled with a red light. Its shape was roughly like that of a deer, with hooves and a tail like those of a cow, covered in scales all over its body. On its forehead, there was a sharp and hard bone that protruded slightly from the flesh, which was actually its horn. As it emerged from the womb, it jumped vigorously, and people could not control it. The villagers, being foolish, considered it a monster and struck it, injuring its right side and causing it to die. Later, someone recognized it as a Qilin, and the prefecture governor Yang Xuan ordered the preservation of its body, storing it in the treasury. My maternal grandfather, who served as an advisor in the prefecture, often ordered it to be fetched and viewed. After many years, the bones and flesh had decayed, leaving only the empty skin, and the scales occasionally fell off. All my aunts and servants saw it.

    13

    ○豢龙

    　　计宗道惟中，柳州罗池人。自言其高祖 【 高祖　说库本作「曾祖」。】 在洪武中为巡检，居一山，号计家砦。尝出行，得一巨卵如升，持归，使鸡伏之。百余日，乃产一物，状类蛇，四足，苍色，鳞甲遍体，其长不盈尺，行则昂首竦身，殆若兽走。家人以米汁饮之。数月，渐大，好饮生血，每刲割羊豕，则取血啖之。久而益驯狎，计公行止，蛇常随之，至呼之出，蟠于榻旁。以手摩之，冷如冰铁。一家呼为小龙，传闻外间，多求观者。计心念曰：「是且致口语，为吾家祸矣。」乃放之廨后溪潭中，嘱曰：「汝毋忧饥，吾每日当遣人饲之，汝自今不得复出也。

    Explanation

    13

    A Man Who Raised a Dragon

    Ji Zong Dao Weizhong was from Luo Chi in Liuzhou. He claimed that his great-great-grandfather, during the reign of Emperor Hongwu, served as a local inspector and lived in a mountain area known as Ji Family Village. Once, while out, he found a huge egg the size of a winnowing basket. He brought it home and had a hen incubate it. After over a hundred days, the egg hatched, producing a creature that resembled a snake but had four legs, was blue-green in color, and had scales and armor covering its body. The creature was no longer than a foot long and moved by lifting its head and raising its body, almost like a beast running. The family fed it with rice water. After several months, the creature grew larger and developed a preference for raw blood. Whenever they slaughtered sheep and pigs, they would give it blood to drink. Over time, the creature became more tame and affectionate. Whenever Ji Zong Dao moved around, the creature followed him, and when he called it out, it would coil up beside his bed. When touched, it felt cold as ice and iron. The family named it "Little Dragon," and news of it spread outside, attracting many visitors who wanted to see it. Ji Zong Dao thought, "This will lead to gossip and bring trouble to our family." So, he released the creature into a stream in the courtyard behind the office, instructing it, "Do not worry about hunger; I will send someone every day to feed you. From now on, you must not come out again."

    14

    」还内，蛇已随至，计叱曰：「汝不听教令，斩汝矣！」蛇如解人意，俯首帖尾，即还潭中。自是常以血置潭口，辄奋起就食。岁久大且踰丈。一日有同官之子妇，汲于潭。妇衣红，蛇望见以为血也，卷而啮之至死。同官怒，声言：「尔畜妖物殃人，吾且以白上官，必破尔家。」计恐，哀祈之，且致厚馈，乃得解。由是恶蛇，欲斩之。持刃至潭，仍置血以诱其出，因投刃斫之，蛇惊而匿，仅断其尾尺余。自是不复出，亦不知其存亡。数年后，一夕风雷暴作，云雾中有苍龙自潭起，长数百丈，拏空而去。家人皆指云小龙化也。惟中，予家伯父同年进士 【 予家伯父同年进士　原本作「予家同年进士」，据说库本补。】 。

    Explanation

    14

    Upon returning home, the snake had already followed him, and Ji shouted at it, saying, "You did not obey my commands, I will kill you!" The snake seemed to understand human intentions, bowing its head and lying flat, then immediately returned to the pool. From then on, it would often place blood at the pool's mouth, springing up to eat whenever it was placed there. After many years, it grew to over ten feet long. One day, a colleague's wife went to the pool to draw water. The woman was dressed in red, and the snake, seeing her, mistook the color for blood, coiled around her and bit her to death. The colleague was furious and declared, "You are a monster that harms people, I will report this to the higher authorities, and I will destroy your family." Ji was afraid, begged for mercy, and offered a generous gift, and thus the conflict was resolved. Thereafter, he hated the snake and wanted to kill it. He took a knife to the pool, still placed blood to lure it out, and then threw the knife and struck it. The snake was startled and hid, only managing to cut off part of its tail. From then on, it no longer appeared, and no one knew whether it was alive or dead. Several years later, one night, a violent wind and thunderstorm arose, and a blue dragon emerged from the pool amidst the clouds and mist, hundreds of feet long, rose into the sky and flew away. The family all pointed and said it was a transformation of the small dragon. Only Zhong, my uncle's contemporary and fellow jinshi (imperial scholar), remains.

    15

    ○兖州岳庙

    　　兖州府岳庙素着灵迹。弘治中，吾苏龚元之知府事，尝于中夜闻有鞭扑声，以问左右，左右有知者，具言庙之神异，元之弗信也。凌晨往谒庙，无所覩，召言者责之。其人言：「但须至诚，乃得进见。」明日斋沐更衣，以夜往，祭祷良久，门启而入。见五人冕服如王者出迎，延坐宾位。元之辞让，王者曰：「公阳官，予阴官也，于职事无统摄，请坐。」已而进茶，元之未敢饮，神曰：「此斋筵中茶也，饮之无害。」元之请曰：「闻有十王，彼五位安在？」曰：「已赴斋矣。」求观狱，辞曰：「狱禁严，不得入，有一事当以奉观耳。」命舁一僧至，炽炭炙其背，曰：「是此地某寺僧也，平日募缘所得，皆供酒食费，不修殿宇，故受罚如此。」问曰：「犹有解乎？」曰：「今改过则可免也。」遂辞出。既归，使人密访，其僧正患背疽且死。告以所见，僧悔惧，倾赀修建，病即愈。

    Explanation

    15

    The Temple of Mount Tai in Yanzhou Prefecture

    The Temple of Mount Tai in Yanzhou Prefecture has long been renowned for its miraculous phenomena. During the Hongzhi period, Gong Yuanzhi, the governor of Suzhou, once heard the sound of whips and beatings in the middle of the night. He asked those around him, and those who knew about it spoke of the temple's divine wonders, but Gong Yuanzhi did not believe them. At dawn, he went to visit the temple, but saw nothing, and summoned the person who had spoken to reprimand him. The person said, "Only if you are sincere can you gain access." The next day, after bathing and changing clothes, he went at night, prayed for a long time, and the temple gates opened for him to enter. He saw five figures dressed in crowns and robes like kings, who came out to greet him and invited him to sit in the guest seat. Gong Yuanzhi declined, and the king said, "You are an official of the sun, and I am an official of the moon; in matters of duty, we have no authority over each other, so please sit." Soon after, tea was served, and Gong Yuanzhi hesitated to drink it. The deity said, "This is tea from a ceremonial banquet; it is harmless to drink." Gong Yuanzhi then asked, "I have heard of the Ten Kings; where are the other five?" The deity replied, "They have already gone to the ceremonial banquet." He then asked to see the prison, and the deity said, "The prison is strictly guarded, and I cannot let you in, but there is one thing I must show you." The deity ordered a monk to be brought, and heated coals were used to roast his back, saying, "He is a monk from a certain temple in this area. His daily alms were used for food and drink, not for repairing the temple buildings, so he is punished in this way." Gong Yuanzhi asked, "Is there still a way to be spared?" The deity replied, "If he repents, he can be spared." He then bid farewell and left. After returning, he sent someone to secretly investigate, and found that the monk was suffering from a back abscess and was about to die. When the monk was told what he had seen, he repented in fear, spent all his money to repair the temple, and his illness was immediately cured.

    16

    ○王全

    　　嘉定娄塘镇人王全，家饶于赀。为人伟躯大腹，饮啖兼数人。行则蹒跚，不能疾趋。每浴时，则令人以物覆己，妻子婢仆皆不得在旁，且戒勿妄开。一日入浴，久无水声，家人怪之，揭视，但见一虾蟆大如斗，伏其中，惊而复覆之。已而全出，恍惚若有所失，是夕死。 【 右二事徐氏姨所说。】

    　　○鬼兵

    　　陆容居吴之娄门外。正德丙寅春，一日薄暮，容倚门独立，闻隔岸汹汹，若有兵甲声。已而，有数千百人，自腰以上不可见，腰以下可见，皆花缯缴股，其行甚疾。容大惊呼，其家男女老幼毕出，皆见之。踰时，过始尽。是岁崇明海寇钮东山作乱，奏调京军及诸卫军讨之，兵岁余乃罢，官帑为之一空。容所见，盖兵象也。

    Explanation

    16

    Wáng Quán

    Jiading Lou Tang Town resident Wáng Quán was wealthy. He had a large, robust body and a voracious appetite, eating and drinking as much as several people. He walked with a slow, unsteady gait, unable to walk quickly. Every time he bathed, he would have someone cover him with a cloth, and his wife, children, maidservants, and servants were not allowed to be near, and he forbade them from opening the cloth without permission. One day, while bathing, there was no sound of water for a long time, which surprised the family. They lifted the cloth to look, and they saw a toad as big as a basket, lying inside. Surprised, they covered him again. Later, Wáng Quán emerged, feeling dazed and as if something was lost, and he died that night. [The two stories above were told by my aunt Xu.]

    Ghost Soldiers

    Lu Róng lived outside the Lou Gate in Wu. In the spring of the year 1506 (丙寅年) during the Zhengde era of the Ming dynasty, one evening near dusk, Lu Róng stood alone by the door and heard a loud noise coming from the other side of the river, as if it were the sound of weapons and armor. Soon after, thousands of people appeared, but only from the waist down could they be seen; above the waist, they could not be seen. They were all decorated with colorful silk and bows, and they moved very quickly. Lu Róng was greatly startled and shouted. His family, including men, women, and children, all came out, and they all saw them. After some time, they passed by completely. That year, the pirate Niudongshan of Chongming caused chaos, and an imperial decree was issued to mobilize the capital troops and various guard troops to suppress them. The military campaign lasted for over a year and was finally disbanded, and the state treasury was depleted. What Lu Róng saw was likely a military omen.

    17

    ○守银犬

    　　家君说：阊门一民家，忘记姓名，以开行为业。家蓄一犬，甚徤，日卧一槛旁，顷刻不离。人有至其所者，輙噬之。家人相戒，莫敢犯。有商人至门，不知而近之，犬噬其股流血。商号呼骂其主，其主亦恶犬，谢曰：「君姑勿怒，明日当烹之共食耳。」商归邸中，夜梦若有告之者，曰：「吾乃主人之父也，死若干年矣，有银数百两埋槛下，生时不及语吾子，子不知也。一念不忘，复生为犬，所以朝夕不去者，盖前此冥数，未可传于子，故守以待之耳 【 故守以待之耳　说库本作「故守之以待耳」。】 ，不意误犯君。今子欲烹我，我欲告以故，彼必不见信，君幸往见之，令不吾杀也。」商竦然惊觉，即起奔诣其家，扣门，主出迎，商问：「犬安在？」则已被烹且熟矣。商人惋恨，具语以所梦，其主犹未信。商请验之，撤槛，果得一瓦b，盛银四百余两。痛悔无及，乃哀其犬而瘗之。

    Explanation

    17

    The Guardian Dog of Silver

    My father recounted: In a household in the Chuan Gate, whose name I have forgotten, the family made a living from trade. They kept a dog, which was very strong, and it would lie beside a cage all day, never leaving for a moment. Whenever someone came to its place, it would bite them. The family warned each other not to approach it. One day, a merchant arrived at the door, unaware of the dog, and approached it. The dog bit his thigh, causing blood to flow. The merchant shouted and cursed at the owner, who also disliked the dog, and apologized, saying, "Please don't be angry, I will cook it and eat it tomorrow." The merchant returned to his inn that night and had a dream in which someone told him, "I am the father of the owner, who has been dead for several years. I buried hundreds of taels of silver beneath the cage, but I did not have the chance to tell my son about it before I died. I remembered it so clearly that I was reborn as a dog, and that is why I stayed there day and night, waiting for someone to discover the silver. I did not expect to mistakenly bite you. Now, your son wants to cook me, and I want to tell him the reason, but he will not believe me. Please go to see him and tell him not to kill me." The merchant was startled awake and immediately went to the house, knocking on the door. The owner came out to greet him, and the merchant asked, "Where is the dog?" The owner replied that it had already been cooked and was almost done. The merchant was filled with regret and told the owner about his dream. The owner still did not believe him. The merchant then asked to check, and they removed the cage, finding a clay vessel containing over four hundred taels of silver. The owner deeply regretted his actions and mourned the dog, burying it.

    18

    ○村民遇土地

    　　家君又说：乡中小民于某，尝出行，遇一老人自称土地，呼于名曰：「汝将死矣，我特来报汝。」于曰：「我方壮年，无疾病，何为而死？」不顾而行，老人忽不见。数日他出，仍遇之，又谓曰：「汝必将死矣 【 汝必将死矣　原本作「汝必死矣」，据说库本补。】 。」于曰：「我死何如？」老人曰：「汝当落水死。」于强辞拒之，而意甚恐。居无何，邻村有与于同姓名者，以他事赴水死，而于竟无恙。岂鬼神亦有误耶，抑聊戱之也？

    Explanation

    18

    My father again said: In a small village, there was a villager named Yu, who once went out and met an old man who called himself the land god. The old man called out Yu's name and said, "You will die. I have come especially to inform you." Yu replied, "I am still in my prime, without any illness, why should I die?" He walked away without looking back, and the old man suddenly disappeared. After several days, when he went out again, he encountered him once more, and the old man said to him, "You will certainly die." Yu asked, "What will happen if I die?" The old man replied, "You will die by drowning." Yu refused it with strong words, but he was very afraid. Not long after, there was someone in a neighboring village with the same name as him, who died by drowning due to some other matter, but Yu was unharmed. Could it be that the gods and spirits also make mistakes, or were they just playing a joke?

    19

    ○竹圃异物

    　　友人徐鹏之妇家朱氏，居沙湖。数年前，其家后圃竹间，忽生物如人，形体差具，其首如戴席帽，断之微有血，不知何怪也。

    　　○空同山人

    　　蜀人卢川，弘治初领乡荐，卒业太学，质美而贫，与吾乡程贡士遵相友善。有道士不知何许人，自云姓达，号空同山人，与川同邸，交尤稔密。其人身颀然长形，状秀伟，而落魄善饮，日行歌于市，暮归携钱满袖，尽以与川。川赖以给，周旋岁余。一旦，欲辞还山，川来语程，共治具送之。川时患疮徧体，久不瘥，求道士治，曰：「易耳。」出药少许，和酒与服，烧炕极热，令卧其上，重被覆之，取所佩小葫芦镇其角。

    Explanation

    19

    Final Translation

    Strange Creature in the Bamboo Garden

    A friend of mine, whose wife's family name is Zhu, resides near Sha Lake. Several years ago, in the bamboo grove behind his house, something resembling a human suddenly appeared. It had a partially formed body, with a head that looked like it was wearing a straw hat. When it was cut, there was a slight amount of blood, but it was unknown what kind of monster it was.

    The Recluse of Mount Kongtong

    Lu Chuan, a man from Sichuan, passed the local examination at the beginning of the Hongzhi era and graduated from the Imperial Academy. He was of noble character but poor. He befriended Cheng Gongshi, a scholar from my hometown. There was a Taoist whose origins were unknown; he introduced himself as surnamed Da and nicknamed himself the Recluse of Mount Kongtong. He lived in the same lodging as Lu Chuan and had a particularly close relationship with him. The Taoist was tall and slender, with a handsome and distinguished appearance, but he was dissolute and fond of drinking. He sang in the market every day and returned home at dusk with his pockets full of money, giving it all to Lu Chuan. Lu Chuan relied on him for support and spent over a year with him. One day, the Taoist wanted to leave and return to the mountains. Lu Chuan came to tell Cheng about it, and they prepared a feast to send him off. At that time, Lu Chuan was suffering from boils all over his body, which had not improved for a long time. He asked the Taoist to treat him, and the Taoist said, "It's easy." He took out a small amount of medicine, mixed it with wine, and gave it to Lu Chuan to drink. He heated the kang to extreme heat, made Lu Chuan lie on it, covered him with a thick blanket, and placed the small gourd he wore at the corner.

    20

    川如为所压，不能兴，出汗淋漓，被尽沾湿。道士徐揭被，呼之起，则疮尽脱去，肤莹如玉矣。顾川曰：「乍别，客中真大寂寞，且忧子贫无以赡。予有丹能点铜为白银 【 能点铜为白银　原本作「能点铜为白金」，据说库本改。】 ，今相分与，他日聊试之，或能充数月费耳。」倾瓢中药一匕授川，酒尽别去。无何，川值乏资，程请出其丹试之。觅铜杓重四两，炽火镕之，投丹其中，少顷五色焰起，铿然有声，已成雪白银，而锱铢无所耗，于是相顾惊叹。程乞其少许，至今藏之。

    　　○张秋帛烬

    　　弘治壬子，河决张秋之沙湾，勅右副都御史华容刘公大夏往治，而以太监李兴、平江伯陈锐俱董其役。方祭神焚帛，帛烬俨成一人，面目手足皆具，俄焂然而起，自烟中入空而灭。时兴、锐多方扰民，山东按察副使杨茂元上疏论之，亦及此事。杨公坐贬官。 【 外舅盛公说。】

    Explanation

    20

    Chuanru was crushed and could not rise, breaking out in a sweat that soaked his robe completely. The Taoist priest slowly lifted the robe and called him to rise. As he rose, all the sores fell off, and his skin became as clear as jade. The Taoist priest looked at Chuanru and said, "Just parted, truly very lonely in a foreign place, and also worried about your poverty, unable to sustain yourself. I have a pill that can turn copper into silver, now I will share it with you. One day, try it out, perhaps it can suffice for several months. He poured out a small amount of medicine, a ladleful, and gave it to Chuanru. After the wine was finished, he left. Shortly afterward, Chuanru found himself short of funds, and Cheng asked to take out the pill to test it. They found a copper ladle weighing four ounces, melted it over a burning fire, and threw the pill into it. A short while later, five-colored flames rose, with a clanging sound, and it had already become pure silver, not losing a single bit. They looked at each other in amazement. Cheng asked for a small portion, and has kept it ever since.

    ○ Zhangqiu Silk Burn

    During the reign of Hongzhi in the year Renzi, the Yellow River broke through the sandbank at Zhangqiu. The emperor ordered the Right Deputy Censor of the Ministry of Justice, Mr. Liu Daxia of Huacr, to go and manage the situation, and appointed the eunuch Li Xing and the Pingjiang Prince Chen Rui to oversee the work. During the ritual of burning silk to worship the gods, the silk ashes formed a complete figure, with a face, hands, and feet. Suddenly, the figure rose from the smoke and disappeared into the air. At that time, Li Xing and Chen Rui were causing much trouble for the people. The Deputy Censor of Shandong, Yang Maoyuan, submitted a memorial criticizing them, which also mentioned this incident. Yang was subsequently demoted. [This was told by my father-in-law, Mr. Sheng.]

    21

    ○王絙

    　　长洲学生王絙，弘治己酉初应乡试。时有校官托所亲鬻举于苏，适无愿者，亟欲贱售焉。同学生奚纯来招絙共图之，事滨就矣。一夕，絙梦身中乡试六十七名 【 梦身中乡试六十七名　原本阙「六」、「七」二字，据说库本补。】 。甫中试而父死，妻继死，妻之父亦死，俄而身亦死。及觉，心怪之，且往见纯，秘不言梦，但托以年幼学踈，不欲暴得名第，辞不就。纯怒，责以重利轻名，曰：「我即自为之，计所费不过数十金。」已而果中式，名次正如所梦。絙方以为异，既而其父与妻之父相继皆死，絙益异之。居无何，纯竟死。絙乃以所梦告人曰：「使当时我为之，今已入鬼录矣。」科名之不可以侥幸得也如此。

    Explanation

    21

    A Student Named Wang Xing

    Wang Xing, a student from Changzhou, took the provincial examination in the early years of the Jiyao period during the reign of Emperor Xiaozong of the Ming Dynasty. At the time, an educational official entrusted a close relative to sell an examination pass in Suzhou, but there were no takers, so he immediately wanted to sell it cheaply. A fellow student named Xi Xuan came to recruit Wang Xing to help him, and the matter was almost completed. One night, Wang Xing dreamed that he passed the provincial examination as the 67th candidate. Just as he passed the exam, his father died, followed by his wife, then his wife's father, and soon after, he himself died. Upon waking, he found it strange and went to see Xuan, keeping the dream secret. He excused himself by saying he was young and not well-versed, did not want to gain fame suddenly, and refused to accept. Xuan became angry, rebuking him for valuing profit over reputation, saying, "I will do it myself, and it will cost only a few dozen gold coins." Soon enough, he indeed passed the exam, and the rank matched his dream exactly. Wang Xing thought it strange, and soon after, his father and his wife's father both died, which made him find it even more strange. Not long after, Xuan eventually died. Wang Xing then told others about his dream, saying, "If I had done it then, I would already be in the Book of the Dead." The fact that one cannot obtain a degree by chance is evident in this case.

    22

    ○灵芝

    　　弘治癸亥，予里人陆忠家墙下产灵芝。明年，连产九本，亦有重台者，五彩烂然，后皆拔去。予曾得其一枯茎藏之。

    　　○马鬼

    　　母党有阙翁者，言其邻人有良马牧于沙湖塘，失足坠水死。自后，每风雨阴晦之日，常有一马奔驰塘上，毛色宛然如生，逼视之，辄不见。人皆谓：此马之鬼也。

    　　○三足鳖

    　　庚午夏 【 庚午夏　原本作「今年夏」，据说库本改。】 ，太仓州有百姓道见渔者，持一鳖而三足，买归令妇炰之。既熟，呼妇共飡，妇不欲食，出坐门外。久之不闻其夫声，入视已失所在，地上止存发一缕，衣服冠履，事事皆在，如蜕形者。惊怖号唤，里中闻之，以妇为谋杀夫而诈谖也，录之官。知州莆田黄廷宣鞫之，得其情，以为异物理或当有，归妇于狱。召渔者，立限令捕三足鳖来。数日，得之以献。

    Explanation

    22

    Translation:

    Lingzhi

    In the year 1493 of the Hongzhi era, a lingzhi mushroom grew at the base of the wall of my fellow villager Lu Zhong's house. The following year, it continued to grow nine more, some with double-layered structures, all brightly colored, but they were all later removed. I once obtained one dried stem and kept it.

    Horse Ghost

    Among my maternal relatives, there was an elder named Que who said that a neighbor had a good horse grazing at Shahu Lake. The horse fell into the water and died. Afterward, every rainy, stormy, or overcast day, a horse would often be seen galloping on the lake's surface, its fur color vividly alive. When looked at closely, it would disappear immediately. People all said: "This is the ghost of the horse."

    Three-Legged Turtle

    In the summer of 1490, a villager from Taicang saw a fisherman holding a turtle with three legs. The villager bought it and had his wife cook it. After it was cooked, he called his wife to eat it together. The wife did not want to eat it and sat outside. After a long time, he did not hear his wife's voice and went inside to find that she had disappeared. On the ground, only a single strand of hair remained, and her clothes, hat, and shoes were all present, as if she had shed her form. Frightened, she screamed, and the villagers heard her. They suspected that the wife had killed her husband and lied about it, and took her to the authorities. The magistrate of Taicang, Huang Tingxuan from Putian, investigated the matter and found the truth, believing that such a physical anomaly might exist. He released the wife from prison. He summoned the fisherman and ordered him to catch the three-legged turtle within a set time. After several days, the turtle was caught and presented.

    23

    即于官厅召此妇依前烹治，而出重囚令食之，食毕引入狱，及门已化尽矣，所存衣发皆与百姓同。乃原妇罪。羣渔云：初被命，网于川，举网惊其太重，及岸视之，乃一肉块如人形，五官俱具而无手足，闭目蠢动。渔大惊怕，掷之水中，又别网一所，得物状亦如之。羣渔惧，共买牲酒祭水神，祷曰：「我辈奉命于官，寻三足鳖，乃连得怪物，如违限，必获罪矣。惟神佑之。」祷毕而网，乃得鳖焉。竟不知前二物为何也。按尔雅曰：「鳖三足为能。」注云：「今阳羡君山上有池，中出三足鳖。」又山海经曰：「从山多三足鳖。」是物世宜有，但人食而化，传记所无。然一举而得二异，尤前所未闻也。

    Explanation

    23

    In the government office, the woman was summoned and cooked as before, and a serious prisoner was released and ordered to eat her. After he finished eating, he was led back into prison, but by the time they reached the gate, she had completely transformed. The remaining clothes and hair were the same as those of ordinary people. The woman's crime was then pardoned. The fishermen said: "At first, we were ordered to fish in the river. When we lifted the net, we were surprised by its great weight. When we reached the shore and looked at it, it was a meat block shaped like a human, with all five senses present but no hands or feet, and with closed eyes, moving clumsily. The fishermen were greatly frightened and threw it back into the water. Then, in another net, they caught something similar. The fishermen were afraid and collectively bought sacrificial meat and wine to offer to the water god. They prayed, saying, 'We have been ordered by the government to find a three-legged turtle, but instead, we have caught monsters. If we fail to meet the deadline, we will surely be punished. Only the gods can help us.' After finishing their prayer and casting the net again, they finally caught the turtle. They still did not know what the previous two things were. According to the Er Ya (Dictionary of Ancient Terms), it says: 'A three-legged turtle is called "Neng." The commentary says: 'Now, in the pool on Jun Mountain in Yangxian, there are three-legged turtles.' The Shan Hai Jing (Classic of Mountains and Seas) says: 'The Congshan (Mount Cong) has many three-legged turtles.' This thing should exist in the world, but when eaten by humans, it transforms, and there are no records of this in history. However, catching two such anomalies at once is particularly unprecedented."

    　　○洞箫记

    　　徐鏊字朝揖，长洲人，家东城下。为人美丰仪，好修饰，而尤善音律。虽居廛陌，雅有士人风度。弘治辛酉，年十九矣。其舅氏张镇者，富人也，延鏊主解库，以堂东小厢为之卧室。是岁七夕，月明如昼，鏊吹箫以自娱，入二皷，拥衾榻上，呜呜未伏。忽闻异香酷烈，双扉无故自开，有巨犬突入，项缀金铃，绕室一周而去。鏊方讶之，闻庭中人语切切，有女郎携梅花灯循阶而上，分两行，凡十六辈。最后一美人，年可十八九，瑶冠凤履，文犀带，着方锦纱袍 【 着方锦纱袍　原本作「着方空纱袍」，据说库本改。】 ，袖广几二尺，若世所图宫妆之状，而玉色莹然，与月光交映，真天人也。

    Second Volume of the Gengsi Bian

    The Flute Record

    Xu Ao, courtesy name Chaoyi, was from Changzhou, living in a house at the eastern city gate. He was handsome and well-mannered, with a particular aptitude for music and melody. Despite living in the marketplace, he had the refined demeanor of a scholar. In the year Xinyou of the Hongzhi era, he was nineteen years old. His uncle, Zhang Zhen, was a wealthy man who invited Xu Ao to manage his money house, and he provided a small room to the east of the hall as Xu Ao's bedroom. That year, on the seventh day of the seventh month, the moon shone brightly like daylight. Xu Ao played the flute to entertain himself, and as the second drum strike approached, he lay on his bed with a quilt, still playing softly. Suddenly, he smelled a strong, unusual fragrance. The double doors of the room opened on their own, and a large dog with a golden bell around its neck suddenly entered, circling the room once before leaving. Xu Ao was startled by this, and he heard soft voices in the courtyard. A young lady appeared, carrying a plum blossom lamp and ascending the stairs. She was followed by sixteen others, arranged in two rows. The last was a beautiful woman, about eighteen or nineteen years old, wearing a jade crown, phoenix-shaped shoes, and a decorated rhinoceros belt. She wore a square-sleeved brocade robe, with sleeves nearly two feet wide, resembling the attire of a palace lady. Her skin was as smooth as jade, and her beauty shone in the moonlight, truly a heavenly being.

    25

    诸侍女服饰畧同，而形制差小，其貌亦非寻常所见。入门，各出笼中红烛，插银台上，一室朗然，四壁顿觉宏敞。鏊股栗不知所为。美人徐步就榻坐，引手入衾，抚鏊体殆遍。良久趋出，不交一言。诸侍女导从而去，香烛一时俱灭。鏊惊怪，志意惶惑者累日。越三夕，月色愈明，鏊将寝，又觉香气非常，心念昨者佳丽，得无又至乎？逡巡间 【 逡巡间　原本「逡巡」下无「间」字，据说库本补。】 ，侍女复拥美人来室中，罗设酒肴，若几席柂架之属，不见有携之者，而无不毕具。美人南乡坐，顾盼左右，光彩烨如也。使侍女唤鏊，鏊整衣冠起揖之，美人顾使坐其右。侍女捧玉杯进酒，酒味醇冽异常，而肴极精腆，水陆诸品，不可名状。美人谓鏊曰：「卿莫疑讶，身非相祸者。

    Explanation

    25

    The maidservants' attire was largely the same, but their shapes were slightly smaller, and their appearance was not ordinary. Upon entering, each brought out red candles from their cages and placed them on silver stands, and the room became bright, and the four walls suddenly felt spacious. Ao Gu's knees trembled, and he did not know what to do. The beautiful woman slowly walked to the bed and sat down, extending her hand into the quilt and caressing Ao Gu's body almost entirely. After a long time, she left hurriedly without speaking a word. The maidservants followed her out, and the incense and candles all went out at once. Ao Gu was surprised and confused, and his thoughts and intentions were in turmoil for several days. After three nights, the moonlight became even brighter, and as Ao Gu was about to sleep, he again sensed an unusual fragrance. He thought of the beautiful woman from the previous night and wondered if she might come again. After hesitating for a moment, the maidservants brought the beautiful woman into the room, setting up a feast of wine and delicacies, as if the tables, chairs, and racks had appeared by themselves, though no one was seen carrying them, and everything was fully prepared. The beautiful woman sat facing south, looking around, and her radiance was dazzling. She had the maidservants call Ao Gu, and Ao Gu straightened his clothes and stood up to bow to her. The beautiful woman then gestured for him to sit beside her. The maidservants presented jade cups of wine, which had an exceptionally strong and pure flavor, and the dishes were extremely refined and exquisite, with a variety of land and sea delicacies that were indescribable. The beautiful woman said to Ao Gu, "Do not doubt or be surprised, I am not here to harm you."

    26

    与卿夙缘，应得谐合，虽不能大有补益，然能令卿资用无乏，饮食常可得，远味珍错，缯素絁锦，亦复都有，世间可欲之物，卿要即不难致，但忧卿福薄耳。」复亲酌劝鏊，稍前促坐欢笑，辞致温婉。鏊唯唯不能出一言，饮食而已。美人曰：「昨听得箫声，知卿兴致非浅，身亦薄晓丝竹，愿一闻之。」顾侍女取箫授鏊，吹罢，美人继奏一曲，音调清越，鏊不能解也 【 鏊不能解也　原本作「鏊不能按也」，据说库本改。】 。且笑曰：「秦家女儿纔吹得世间下俚调，如何解引得凤凰来？令渠箫生在，应不羞为徐郎作奴。」逡巡遂去 【 逡巡遂去　原本「逡巡」下无「遂去」二字，据说库本补。】 。

    Explanation

    26

    The predestined bond between us, I believe, should lead to harmony. Though I may not be able to greatly benefit you, I can ensure that your resources are never in short supply, and that food and drink are always available. You will also have access to exotic delicacies, fine fabrics such as silk and brocade, and all the desirable things of the world. If you desire something, it will not be difficult to obtain, but I worry that your fate may be thin.

    I then personally offered you a toast, inviting you to sit closer and join in the laughter. My words were warm and gentle. You could only nod in agreement, unable to speak, and focused on eating and drinking. The lady said, "I heard the sound of a flute yesterday and knew your interest in music was not shallow. I myself have a slight understanding of stringed and wind instruments, and I would like to hear you play." She asked her servant to fetch a flute and handed it to you. After you finished playing, the lady followed with a piece of her own, her melody clear and resonant. However, you could not comprehend it.

    She then smiled and said, "A woman from the Qin family can only play the simple tunes of the world. How could she attract a phoenix? If that flute player were here, he should not be ashamed to serve as a servant to Mr. Xu." With that, she left quickly.

    27

    越明夕，又至，饮酒阑，侍女报曰：「夜向深矣。」因拂榻促眠，美人低回微笑，良久，乃相携登榻。帐帏裀藉，穷极瑰丽，非复鏊向时所眠也。鏊心念：「我试诈跌入地，观其何为。」念方起，榻下已徧铺锦褥，殆无隙地。美人解衣，独輙红绡裹肚一事，相与就枕交会，已而流丹浃藉，宛转恇难胜。鏊于斯时，情志飞荡，颠倒若狂矣，然竟莫能一言。天且明，美人先起揭帐，侍女十余奉匜沃盥。良久妆讫言别，谓鏊曰：「感时追运，偎得相从，良非容易。从兹之后，欢好当复无间，卿举一念，身即却来，但忧卿此心，还易翻覆耳。且多言可畏，身此来，诚不欲令世间俗子辈得知，须卿牢为秘密。」已而遂去。鏊恍然自失，徘徊凝睇者久之。昼出，人觉其衣上香酷冽异常，多怪之者。

    Explanation

    27

    The next evening, she arrived again. As the drinking feast neared its end, a maidservant reported, "The night is deep." She then swept the bed and urged him to sleep. The woman smiled hesitantly and lingered for a long time before they ascended the bed together. The curtains and bedding were of the utmost beauty and splendor, far more luxurious than what he had slept on before. The protagonist thought, "I will try to fall to the ground as a test, to see what she will do." As he thought this, the floor below the bed was already covered with brocade rugs, leaving almost no empty space. The woman undressed, wearing only a red silk wrap around her waist. They lay down together and met, and soon their passion was intense, with sweat and exertion making them turn and twist, unable to bear it. At this moment, the protagonist's emotions and thoughts were flying wildly, and he was almost crazed, yet he could not utter a word. As dawn approached, the woman rose first and lifted the curtain. More than ten maidservants brought water and washed his hands and face. After a long time, she finished dressing and said goodbye, telling the protagonist, "Grateful for the time and circumstances, we are able to be together, which is truly not easy. From now on, our joy and affection will be without interruption. If you have a thought, I will come back immediately. But I worry about your heart, it is easy to change your mind. And many words are to be feared. I truly do not want to let the common people know. You must keep it a secret." She then departed. The protagonist was suddenly lost in thought, lingering and gazing for a long time. During the day, people noticed the unusual strong and cool fragrance on his clothes, and many found it strange.

    28

    自是每一举念，则香骤发，美人輙来，来则携酒相与欢宴，频频向鏊说天上事及诸仙人变化，其言奇妙，非世所闻。鏊心欲质问其居止所向，而相见輙吶于辞，乃书小札问之，终不答，曰：「卿得好妇，适意便足，何烦穷问！」间自言：「吾从九江来，闻苏杭名郡多胜景，故尔暂游，此世中处处是吾家耳。」美人虽柔和自喜，而御下极严，诸侍女在左右，惴惴跪拜惟谨，使事鏊必如事己。一人以汤进，微偃蹇，輙摘其耳，使跪谢乃已。鏊时有所须，应心而至。一日出行，见道傍柑子，意甚欲之。及夕，美人袖出数百颗遗焉。市物有不得者，必为委曲，多方致之。鏊有隹布数端，或剪六尺藏焉，鏊方勤觅，美人来，语其处，令收之。

    Explanation

    28

    From then on, every time he thought of her, a sudden fragrance would appear, and the beautiful lady would come. When she arrived, she would bring wine and they would enjoy a feast together. She frequently told him about celestial matters and the transformations of various immortals, her words were wonderful and not heard in the world. He wanted to ask her directly about where she lived, but whenever he saw her, he would stammer in words. So he wrote a short note to ask her, but she never answered, saying, "You have a good wife, if you are content, why bother to ask further?" She occasionally said, "I came from Jiuhu, I heard that Suzhou and Hangzhou are famous prefectures with many beautiful sights, so I am temporarily traveling. In this world, everywhere is my home." Although she was gentle and self-satisfied, she ruled her subordinates very strictly. The attendants around her trembled and bowed with utmost respect, and she made them serve him as if they served themselves. One attendant served soup, slightly hesitating, and she immediately pulled her ear, making her kneel and apologize until it was over. Whenever he needed something, it would arrive as desired. One day, when he went out, he saw oranges by the roadside and very much wanted them. By evening, the beautiful lady took out hundreds of them and left them. If something was not obtained in the market, she would certainly go to great lengths to obtain it. He had several pieces of fine cloth, sometimes cutting six feet and hiding them. He was just diligently searching for them when the beautiful lady came, told him where they were, and ordered him to collect them.

    29

    解库中失金首饰，美人指令于城西黄牛坊钱肆中寻之，盗者以易钱若干去矣。诘朝往访焉，物宛然在，径取以归，主人者徒瞪目视而已。鏊尝与人有争，稍不胜，其人或无故僵仆，或以他事横被折辱，美人輙告云：「奴辈无礼，已为卿报之矣。」如此往还数月，外间或微闻之。有爱鏊者疑其妖，劝使勿近，美人已知之，见鏊曰：「痴奴妄言，世宁有妖如我者乎？」鏊尝以事出，微疾病邸中，美人歘来坐于旁，时时会合如常。其眠处人甚多，了不觉也。数戒鏊曰：「勿轻向人道，恐不为卿福。」而鏊不能忍口，时复宣泄，传闻浸广，或潜相窥伺，美人始愠。会鏊母闻其事，使召鏊归，谋为娶妻以绝之，鏊不能违。美人一夕见曰：「郎有外心矣，吾不敢复相从。」遂绝不复来。鏊虽念之，终莫能致也。

    Explanation

    29

    Lost gold jewelry was found missing in the pawnshop, and the beauty ordered a search for it in the money shop on the west side of the Yellow Ox Lane. The thief had exchanged it for some amount of money and left. The next day, they went to visit the shop, and the object was still there. They took it directly and returned, and the owner just stared blankly. Ao often had disputes with others, and when he was slightly defeated, the other person either fell down inexplicably or was unjustly humiliated for other reasons. The beauty would then tell him, "These servants are rude; I have already reported it for you." This went on for several months, and outside, people sometimes heard about it. Those who loved Ao suspected that she was a demon and advised him not to get close. The beauty already knew this and said to Ao, "You foolish servant is speaking nonsense; how could there be a demon like me in the world?" Ao once went out on business and fell slightly ill in the inn. The beauty suddenly came and sat beside him, meeting with him as usual. There were many people sleeping there, but she was completely unaware of it. She repeatedly warned Ao, "Do not casually tell others about it, for it might not be a blessing for you." But Ao could not keep quiet and often leaked out the information, causing the rumors to spread widely. Some secretly watched and waited, and the beauty became angry. Coincidentally, Ao's mother heard about the matter and sent for Ao to return home, planning to marry him off to cut ties with her. Ao could not disobey. One night, the beauty appeared and said, "You have an outside heart now; I dare not follow you anymore." She then stopped coming altogether. Ao missed her, but in the end, he could not bring her back.

    30

    至十一月望后，一日，鏊夜梦四卒来呼，过所居萧家巷，立土地祠外，一卒入呼土神，神出，方巾白袍老人也，同行曰：「夫人召。」鏊随之出胥门，履水而渡，到大第院，墙里外乔木数百章，蔽翳天日。历三重门，门尽朱漆兽环，金浮沤钉，有人守之。进到堂下，堂可高八九仞，陛数十重，下有鹤屈颈卧焉，彩绣朱碧，上下焕映。小青衣遥见鏊，奔入报云：「薄情郎来矣。」堂内女儿捧香者、调鹦鹉者、弄琵琶者、歌者、舞者，不知几辈，更迭从窓隙看鏊，亦有旧识相呼者、微谇骂者。 【 微谇骂者　原本作「微言骂者」，据说库本改。】 俄闻佩声泠然， 【 俄闻佩声泠然　原本作「俄闻佩声泠然」，据说库本改。】 香烟如云，堂内递相报云：「夫人来。

    Explanation

    30

    On the day after the full moon of the eleventh month, Zhuo dreamed at night that four soldiers came to call him. They passed by the alley where he lived, standing outside the land temple. One soldier went in to call the land god, who emerged as an old man in a square cap and white robe. Another soldier said, "The lady has summoned you." Zhuo followed them out of the city gate, walking on water to cross, and arrived at a grand mansion. The walls were surrounded by hundreds of tall trees that shaded the sky and sun. They passed through three sets of gates, each painted red with animal rings and golden nails, guarded by people. They entered the hall, which was about eight or nine ren high, with steps leading up in dozens of layers. Below, a crane was resting with its neck bent, its colorful embroidery and vermilion and green colors shining brightly. A young girl in green clothes saw Zhuo from afar and ran in to report, saying, "The unfeeling husband has come." Inside the hall, there were many women holding incense, playing with parrots, playing the pipa, singing, and dancing, too many to count, taking turns looking at Zhuo through the window cracks. Some were old acquaintances who called out to him, while others muttered insults. Soon, the sound of jade pendants tinkling and the fragrance of incense rising like clouds filled the air. Inside the hall, they reported one after one, "The lady has arrived."

    31

    」老人牵鏊使跪，窥帘中有大金地炉燃兽炭，美人拥炉坐，自提筯挟火，时时长叹云：「我曾道渠无福，果不错。」少时，闻呼卷帘，美人见鏊数之曰：「卿大负心，昔语卿云何，而辄背之！今日相见愧未？」因欷歔泣下曰：「与卿本期始终，何图乃尔。」诸姬左右侍者或进曰：「夫人无自苦，个儿郎无义，便当杀却，何复云云。」颐指羣卒以大杖击鏊，至八十，鏊呼曰：「夫人，吾诚负心，念尝蒙顾覆，情分不薄，彼洞箫犹在，何无香火情耶！」美人因呼停杖曰：「实欲杀卿，感念畴昔，今贳卿死。」鏊起匍匐拜谢，因放出。老人仍送还，登桥失足，遂觉。两股创甚，卧不能起。又五六夕，复见美人来，将鏊责之如前话，云：「卿自无福，非关身事。」既去创即差。后诣胥门，踪迹其境，杳不可得，竟莫测为何等人也。予少闻鏊事，尝面质之，得其首末如此，为之叙次，作洞箫记。

    31

    The old man led Aò to kneel, peering through the curtain to see a large golden hearth burning animal charcoal. A beautiful woman sat by the hearth, holding a fork and stoking the fire, often sighing and saying, "I always said he had no luck, and it's true." After a while, she called for the curtain to be drawn back. The woman saw Aò and reproached him, saying, "You are very unfaithful. What did I tell you before, and yet you have betrayed me! Today, what shame do you feel?" She then wept and said, "We were supposed to be together forever, who would have thought it would end like this?" Some of the women and attendants around her said, "Lady, do not harm yourself. This man is unrighteous, and he should be killed. Why are you still talking about it?" She gestured to the guards to beat Aò with a large stick, up to eighty blows. Aò cried out, "Lady, I truly am unfaithful, but I remember your kindness and the deep feelings we shared. That flute is still there, why no affection?" The woman then called for the beating to stop and said, "I really wanted to kill you, but remembering our past, I will spare your life today." Aò rose and prostrated himself in gratitude, and she let him go. The old man still escorted him back, and as they climbed the bridge, Aò lost his footing and woke up. His thighs were severely injured, and he could not get up. A few days later, he saw the woman again, who reproached him as before, saying, "It's your own bad luck, not my fault." After she left, his injuries began to heal. Later, he visited the place near the bridge, but could not find any trace of her. Finally, it remained unknown what kind of person she was. I heard about Aò's story when I was young and once confronted him directly, learning the full details. I wrote this account, calling it the "Flute Record."

    ○普光伽蓝

    　　史鉴公甫与予家同里居。未达时 【 未达时　纪录汇编本作「未逢时」，据说库本改。】 ，与数友读书城东普光寺。尝昼假寐，恍惚若有呼之者，曰：「速起读书，子御史也，努力自爱。」遂惺然寤，忆所见者类寺门伽蓝，即往默祝曰：「他日得如神言，当令神像宇一新。」自是每晨入暮归，过必一揖。诸友相目笑之，鉴不恤也。遇朔望日，觇诸友俱出，独携一麸往祭，极冗不辍。弘治己未，鉴登进士，授今官，归往设斋以谢，建小殿奉之。

    Explanation

    32

    The Temple of Pu Guang

    Mr. Shi Jian Gongfu and I lived in the same village. When he was not yet successful, he studied with several friends at Pu Guang Temple in the east of the city. Once, during the day, he took a nap and felt as if someone was calling him. The voice said, "Hurry up and read; you will become a censor, so work hard and take care of yourself." He then awakened with clarity, remembering that what he had seen resembled the statue of the temple guardian. He went to the temple and silently prayed, "If I achieve what the divine has said, I will have the temple and its statues renewed." From then on, every morning when entering and every evening when returning, he would bow every time passing by. His friends would look at him and laugh, but Jian did not care. On the first and fifteenth days of the month, when all his friends had left, he would carry a small offering alone to pay respects, continuing tirelessly despite great busyness. In the year 1499 of the Hongzhi era, Jian passed the imperial examination and became a jinshi, being appointed to his current position. Upon returning home, he set up a vegetarian meal to express gratitude and built a small hall to honor the temple guardian.

    33

    ○方学

    　　无锡方学，少时豫选为诸生。其夜，梦一人持一桃一梨授之，曰：「二人之命，悬于君手。」觉而异焉，心识之。后领乡书，弘治己未，会试礼部。时江阴士人徐经于主文者有夤缘，为华给事中昶所奏，下制狱验问。华以学同乡且素厚，援以为证，将引入廷鞫，道遇乡人贡主事安甫遗以桃李各一，曰：「事之虚实，待君一言，彼二人之命，皆在君手矣。」学骤忆前梦，为之竦然。独安甫所遗，而梦中为梨，似若少差，然亦神矣。学证狱事，人多知之，此不复列。 【 尤四绍熊说。】

    Explanation

    33

    Translation

    Fang Xue

    Fang Xue of Wuxi was pre-selected as a student when he was young. One night, he dreamed of a person who gave him a peach and a pear, saying, "The fate of two people hangs on your hands." He woke up feeling strange and remembered the dream. Later, he passed the provincial examination in the year 1509 and took the imperial examination at the Ministry of Rites. At that time, Jiangyin scholar Xu Jing had a close relationship with the chief examiner, and he was reported by Hua Chang, a censor, who had him sent to the imperial prison for investigation. Hua, being from the same hometown as Fang Xue and having a close relationship with him, cited Fang Xue as evidence and intended to bring him to the imperial court for trial. On the way, Fang Xue met a fellow townsman, the official Gong Anfu, who gave him one peach and one plum each, saying, "The truth or falsehood of the matter depends on your words; the fate of those two people is in your hands." Fang Xue suddenly remembered his earlier dream and was deeply shaken. The peach and plum given by Gong Anfu matched the dream, except that the dream had a pear instead of a plum, but it was still remarkable. Fang Xue testified in the legal case, and many people knew about it, but this account is not detailed here. [Provided by You Si Shao Xiong.]

    34

    ○七总管部使

    　　成化间，苏人张文宝者，有子壮年夭没。他日，其友人有遇之于途者，忘其死也，拉归家，升楼呼家人治具共饮。家人怪入门时无客，视楼上了无所见，而其主语言揖逊如对人者，惊而噀之，遂不见，友乃悟其已死。又数日，以事出齐门，复遇之，谢曰：「君家何乃尔，吾岂祸君者，吾今在七总管部下，庙宇去此不远，君能垂访乎？」即与俱至庙中，入庑间一室，坐谈久之，因告曰：「某所某家人有疾，彼多行禳谢无益也。」指堂上曰：「此正欠我家主翁一陌纸耳，君为语之，了此自无事矣。」友归，往告其家，如言祭祷，即愈。七总管者，郡人姓金氏名元，七里俗所私祀。 【 毛师】

    Explanation

    34

    Translation

    The Seven Generals' Attendant

    During the Chenghua period, there was a man named Zhang Wenbao from Suzhou who had a son who died prematurely at a young age. One day, a friend of Zhang encountered his son on the road and, unaware that he was dead, brought him back home. They climbed the stairs, called the family to prepare a feast, and invited them to drink together. The family was surprised to see no guest when they entered, and upon looking upstairs, they saw nothing, but the son spoke and bowed as if talking to someone. Startled, they spat at him, and then he vanished. The friend realized that he had already died. A few days later, when the friend left through the Qi Gate on some errand, he met the son again. The son said, "Why have you become so harsh? I am not one who would bring harm to you. I am now under the command of the Seven Generals, and the temple is not far from here. Could you visit me?" The friend then accompanied him to the temple, where they entered a room in the side hall and sat to talk for a long time. The son then said, "There is a family in a certain place who is ill, and their many rituals and offerings are of no use." Pointing to the hall, he said, "This is just lacking one sheet of paper for my master. You should tell them this, and the matter will be resolved." The friend returned home and informed the family as instructed. They performed the sacrifice as directed, and the illness was cured. The Seven Generals were a local figure named Jin Yuan, worshipped privately by the people of the seven towns.

    35

    ○周岐凤

    　　周岐凤，初名凤，江阴之青阳人。性敏绝伦，身兼百艺，诗文笔札亦可观。平生所服用皆自制，尝与其仆各市一帽，既而曰：「吾帽竟与尔无别乎？」即瓜分之，仆有所如，少顷却回，岐凤已缕金缝而戴之矣，其巧捷类此。然阴险狡狯，挟邪术肆为奸淫，以故不齿于人。寓宿富家，与主人剧饮，就寝。主妇中夜展转不寐，若闻有相唤者，启门欲出，迟回自疑，蹵其夫起，告其故，夫往觇之，岐凤方裸体散发，跳踯为厌胜。执而痛棰之，几死。

    Explanation

    35

    ○Zhou Qifeng

    　　Zhou Qifeng, originally named Feng, was from Qingyang, Jiangyin. He was exceptionally intelligent, unparalleled in his abilities, and possessed a hundred skills; his poetry, prose, and calligraphy were also noteworthy. Throughout his life, everything he used was made by himself. Once, he and his servant each bought a hat. Later, he said, "Is my hat really no different from yours?" He then divided it, and the servant went somewhere. A short while later, the servant returned, but Zhou Qifeng had already sewn gold thread into it and was wearing it. His dexterity and ingenuity were of this kind. However, he was cunning and deceitful, using evil arts to commit immoral acts, and thus was disgraced among people. He stayed at a wealthy family's home, drinking heavily with the host, and went to bed. In the middle of the night, the hostess was restless and unable to sleep, as if she heard someone calling. She opened the door to go out, hesitated and doubted herself, woke her husband up, and told him the reason. The husband went to investigate and found Zhou Qifeng naked and disheveled, jumping and dancing in a ritual. He grabbed and beat him severely, nearly killing him.

    The magistrate prayed for rain in the temple. Feng Qi, dressed in Daoist robes with a braided bun and carrying a sword, went to pay respects. The magistrate did not recognize him. They spoke, and Feng Qi gradually became more intimate. Soon, he threw his sword, stepped, and flew into the air. The magistrate was greatly surprised, thinking a true immortal had arrived. Feng Qi later became a guest at the Lu family in Xintang. The Lu brothers were named Ji Fang and Ji Yuan. When he reached Jiangyin, He listed Ji Fang's illegal actions and went to the water's edge to appeal. Xiong Gai did not accept it, and He jumped into the water. Xiong Gai then accepted it.

    37

    Ji Fang, fearing for his safety, entrusted ten taels of gold to Qi Feng to resolve matters in the capital. Qi Feng squandered it almost entirely, and Lu Shu was ultimately seized and confiscated. Resenting this deeply, he implicated Qi Feng in his accusations. After Ji Fang was already punished by law, Qi Feng changed his name and hid in the rivers and lakes, having no fixed residence, living on a boat, and indulging in extreme luxury, with all his tableware made of gold. Once he arrived in Suzhou, a Suzhou man named Qian Ye sent him a poem saying, "Hearing that you are talented but have not yet met, where have you been these years, seeking your whereabouts? A guest in a foreign land like Zhang Jiean, who in the world is like Kong Rong? In the marketplace, under the spring blossoms and singing birds, drinking wine; at the river bridge, in the wind and rain at night, pushing open the door. All schemes are left to the east-flowing river, returning to the dream of my homeland." Qi Feng was deeply moved upon receiving the poem. Later, he went to the capital to clear his name, but ultimately died of illness in a guesthouse. Liu, an official, bought a coffin and buried him. After his death, in the Three Wu regions, there were those who summoned him as a spirit, and when Qi Feng appeared, his writings often resembled his works in life, and his predictions were often remarkably accurate. One day, he wrote a poem: "The moon over Chang'an, a thousand miles away, the spring at Du Ling in the third month."

    38

    With one cup of tea and the scent of incense, the gentle breeze brings an old friend. It also says, "A solitary journey abroad, the meeting of influential people in the autumn of life. I will carry spiritual virtue to the afterlife, causing even ghosts and gods to be troubled." He wrote after the poem, "If you set up tea and incense and recite this poem, I will come." Later, when they tried it, it proved true. The governor of Songjiang lost some gold jewelry in his office and consulted a spirit. The spirit wrote four lines: "Finding relief after a long drought, meeting an old friend in a foreign land. The night of marriage, passing an exam and being listed on the imperial register." When asked to explain the meaning, the spirit did not respond. When asked to write his name, it wrote, "Zhou Qifeng." The governor was displeased, thinking that the ghost's words were not reliable. He mentioned this to a scholar, who replied, "This is the four-joy poem that people commonly talk about." The governor was surprised and said, "I have a female servant named Si Xi (Four Joys), could that be the case?" He arrested and questioned her, and indeed, the stolen items were found, still hidden in the ashes behind the office building. He then understood the previous statement. My great-grandfather also knew Qi Feng, but he disliked his character and would send him to a summer house whenever he came, not allowing him to visit the main house.

    39

    ○柴驿丞

    　　吴江盛昶允高，景泰庚午举乡试北上，偕常熟章参议表大、理格兄弟及他同年二人，行达山东一驿，章等先至，昶独后。驿丞柴某出迎，目诸人久之，问曰：「公等五人来，其一安在？」众对曰：「在后且至。」丞又问曰：「彼非衣绿乎？」众怪之，诘其所自知，丞曰：「予昨夜梦一白须老人云：『明日有五举人至此，中一绿衣者是汝异日恩人，慎毋慢之。』予是以不无少望耳。」少选昶至，丞意甚喜，留五人宿，供帐极丰。亲为昶执奴隶役，勤渠百端，众窃笑之。及上京，昶竟擢第。寻以监察御史俵马山东。至其地时，丞适被讼于巡按御史，下狱，当黜为民矣。昶因造谒，为之缓颊，不从。索狱词至，手裂碎之，因取笔别为具案，尽雪其罪。御史不得已听之，丞遂得释。恩人之梦，至是不诬矣。

    Explanation

    39

    ○柴驿丞

    In the year Jingtai, during the reign of Emperor Jingtai, Sheng Chang of Wujiang passed the provincial examination and traveled north with Chang Biaoda, a senior official from Changshu, his brother Li Ge, and two other scholars. They reached a post station in Shandong, where Chang and his companions arrived first, leaving Sheng Chang slightly behind. The postmaster, Mr. Chai, came out to greet them and stared at the group for a long time before asking, "Where is the fifth person among you?" The others replied, "He is coming soon." The postmaster then asked, "Is he not wearing green?" The others were surprised and asked how he knew. The postmaster said, "Last night, I had a dream of an old man with a white beard who said, 'Tomorrow, five scholars will come here, and one of them wearing green will be your future benefactor. Do not treat him rudely.' That is why I had a slight hope." A short while later, Sheng Chang arrived, and the postmaster was very happy. He invited the five to stay and provided them with very rich accommodations. He personally performed menial tasks for Sheng Chang, working diligently in many ways, which made the others smile secretly.

    Upon reaching the capital, Sheng Chang was eventually selected. Soon after, he became a censor and was sent to distribute horses in Shandong. When he arrived, the postmaster was just being sued by the circuit inspector and was about to be demoted to commoner status. Sheng Chang went to visit him and pleaded on his behalf, but the circuit inspector did not listen. When Sheng Chang got the court documents, he tore them up by hand and then took a pen to write a separate case, completely clearing the postmaster's guilt. The circuit inspector could not help but accept it, and the postmaster was released. The dream of the benefactor was not false after all.

    40

    ○罗江神祠

    　　昶自御史谪官福之古田，寻以霈恩改知罗江县。公署后有土地祠，前令所立，颇着灵异，令有事必祷焉，祭享无虚月，自昶莅任不复然。一日，私廨失所畜鸡，寻之乃在神前，舒翼伏地如被钉者。以问舆皂辈，皆言神以久不祭，故见谴耳。昶怒，至神祠斥数其神，因举意欲毁之。是夜梦中见神来，谢罪恳曰：「予血食于此者累年，不敢为过。昨日鸡被钉，乃鬼卒辈苦饥，故为之，非予敢然也。公幸怜之勿毁。」昶不许，明旦遂撤去之。其前令者既秩满，即留家于县署后，夜梦神来诉乞立庙，诘之曰：「何不更诉新令？」神蹙额曰：「须公自为之耳，彼盛公威严，不敢干也。」令乃即所居旁建祠祀之。

    Explanation

    40

    罗江神祠

    Chang, who was demoted from the position of censor to an official in Gǔtián, soon after received imperial favor and was appointed to govern Luojiang County. Behind the government office, there was a local shrine dedicated to the land god, established by the previous magistrate. It was very famous for its miraculous nature, and the magistrate would always pray there for important matters, holding worship and offerings without fail every month. Since Chang took office, this practice no longer continued. One day, the chicken kept in his private residence went missing, and upon searching, it was found in front of the shrine, with its wings spread and head down as if nailed to the ground. When he asked the servants, they all said the deity was punishing the shrine because it had not been worshipped for a long time. Chang became angry and went to the shrine to scold the deity, expressing his intention to destroy it. That night, he dreamed that the deity came to him, apologizing sincerely and saying, "I have been worshipped here for many years and have never done anything wrong. Yesterday, the chicken was nailed down because the ghost soldiers were suffering from hunger, so they did it. It was not I who dared to do such a thing. Please have mercy and do not destroy it." Chang did not agree and dismantled the shrine the next morning. The former magistrate, whose term had ended, immediately moved his family behind the county office. That night, he dreamed that the deity came to him, pleading for a new shrine to be built. He questioned the deity, saying, "Why didn't you appeal to the new magistrate?" The deity frowned and said, "It must be done by you. Magistrate Sheng is strict and authoritative, and we dare not interfere." The magistrate then built a shrine near his residence to worship the deity.

    41

    ○戚编修

    　　余姚戚澜，少时尝得危疾，息已绝，踰时复苏。自言被人执至一官府，有贵人坐堂上，引见，问乡里、姓名、年几何，具以对。贵人曰：「非也，追误矣。」顾吏令释之，得出。还至中途遇雨，憩佛寺，步入一室中，满地皆纱帽楦也，以手扳举之不动。旁有人谓曰：「此非君物也，君所有者在此。」指一架令取之，随手而得，视其内有字曰「七品」。后澜果以进士终翰林编修。

    Explanation

    41

    ○Qī Biānxiū

    During his youth, Qī Lán from Yúyáo suffered a serious illness, his breath had ceased, and after some time he revived. He claimed that he was taken by someone to an official place, where a noble person sat on the dais, introduced him, and asked about his hometown, name, and age. Qī answered thoroughly. The noble person said, "It is not so, you have made a mistake." He looked at the official and ordered him to release him, and Qī was released. Returning to the halfway point, he encountered rain and rested in a temple. Entering a room, he found the floor full of hat forms, which he tried to lift with his hand but could not. A person nearby said to him, "These are not your possessions, what you have is here." Pointing to a rack, he ordered Qī to take it, and Qī took it easily, seeing that it had the word 'seven' written on it. Later, Qī indeed became a Jinshi and ended his career as a Hanlin Academy editor.

    42

    ○临江狐

    　　临江富人陈崇古，所居后有菓园，委一人守之，贩鬻利息皆由其手。其人年可四十许，颇修整，不类庸下人，独居园中小屋间。一夕，有美姬来就之，自言能饮，索酒共酌，且求欢。其人疑之，扣其居止姓名，终不答，曰：「与君有夙缘，故相从，无问也。」遂与狎。自是每夜辄至，日久情密如伉俪，亦不复扣其所从来也。比舍人怪园中常有人语声，窥见之，以告主人。主人为其费财也，召责之，其人初抵讳，因请主人覆视记识，曾无亏漏。更加研问，乃吐实，主亦任之。

    Explanation

    42

    A Fox from Linjiang

    A wealthy man named Chen Chonggu from Linjiang had an orchard behind his residence, and he entrusted one person to guard it, handling all profits from selling and buying. The man was around forty years old, well-groomed, and did not look like an ordinary person; he lived alone in a small house in the garden. One night, a beautiful woman came to him, saying she could drink, asked for wine to drink together, and sought pleasure. The man doubted her, asked about her residence and name, but she never answered, saying, "I have a predestined relationship with you, so I follow you; don't ask." So they became intimate. From then on, she came every night, and after a long time, their relationship became as close as husband and wife, and he no longer asked about where she came from. The neighbors were surprised by the frequent sounds of voices in the garden and saw it, reporting it to the owner. The owner was concerned because he was spending money, called him to account, and the man initially denied it. Then he asked the owner to check and verify, and there was no loss or damage. The owner asked more deeply, and the man then revealed the truth, and the owner also accepted it.

    43

    是夜姬来云：「而主谓吾诱汝财耶？」因从容言：「吾非祸君者，此世界内如吾者无虑千数，皆修仙道，吾事将就，特借君阳气助耳。更几日数足，吾亦不复留此，于君无损也。」他日来，剧饮沉醉，谈谑益欵，其人试挑之曰：「子于世间亦有畏乎？」姬以醉忘情，且恃交稔，无复防虞，直答曰：「吾无所畏。吾睡时则有光旋绕身畔，人欲不利于我者，一蹑此光，吾已惊觉，终不能有所加也。所最恶者，人能远立以口承其光而徐吸之，则彼得寿而吾祸矣。」其人唯唯。俟其去，目逆而送之，遥见其狼跄仆田中，往看姬寐正熟，有光照地如月，依言吸之，觉胸臆隐隐热下，光尽敛，乃归。明日复至其所，有老狐死焉。景泰中，盛允高莅盐课扬州，陈氏有商于扬者道其事，云此人尚在，年九十余矣。 【 右四事允高之子壅说。】

    Explanation

    43

    That night, the lady came and said, "Your master accuses me of luring you to steal your wealth?" She then spoke calmly, "I am not one who brings disaster to you. In this world, there are countless beings like me, all cultivating the Tao of immortality. My task is nearly complete, and I am only borrowing your yang energy to aid me. In a few more days, when the count is complete, I will no longer stay here, and it will cause no harm to you." On another day, she came again, and they drank heavily, becoming intoxicated. They engaged in more intimate conversation and jesting. The man tried to test her by asking, "Do you have any fears in this world?" The lady, drunk and forgetful of her emotions, and relying on their long acquaintance, no longer felt any apprehension. She answered straightforwardly, "I have no fears. When I sleep, there is a light swirling around my body. If someone intends to harm me and steps on this light, I will already be awakened, and they will ultimately be unable to harm me. What I detest most is if someone stands far away and slowly inhales the light through their mouth; then they will gain longevity while I will suffer." The man nodded in agreement. After she left, he watched her until she was out of sight, seeing her fall into the field in a drunken state. He went to check and found the lady asleep soundly, with a light illuminating the ground like the moon. Following her words, he inhaled the light, feeling a warm sensation in his chest. The light completely disappeared, and he returned home. The next day, he returned to the place, and there was an old fox found dead there. During the Jingtai era, Sheng Yun Gao, the salt tax commissioner in Yangzhou, heard a merchant from the Chen family in Yangzhou tell this story. The man said he was still alive, over ninety years old. [These four stories were told by Sheng Yun Gao's son, Yong.]

    ○果报

    　　吴人盛侗行第九，平昔以智干武断乡曲。有里人于英者，妾与奴通，事泄，英杀奴，密令其家干人常熟顾某载尸他所焚之。顾潜瘗之城下，绐英云：「已烧却矣。」后顾复以事忤英，虑得祸，将发奴尸以胁之，谋于侗。侗以为奇货，阳许之而微泄其事于英。英惧，致厚赂焉。授以计，杀顾，焚其尸，事秘莫能知者。后数年，侗与英俱感疾，英病昏恍惚，若有所见，因备述前事，言「今为顾某所讼，必与九老官人俱去。」两人竟同日死。侗疾亟，连呼索马，时所乘马方纵牧邻僧庵中，比侗气绝，马忽数跃而毙。英且死，呼家人曰：「九老官人去未？」答曰：「死矣。」乃曰：「如此，我亦当去。」遂瞑目。 【 郁箎说。】

    Explanation

    44

    Fruit and Retribution

    Sheng Dong of Wu, the ninth of his name, had long been known for his intelligence and authoritarian rule in his village. There was a man named Yu Ying from the same village, whose concubine had an illicit relationship with a slave. When the affair was discovered, Yu Ying killed the slave and secretly ordered a man from Changshu named Gu to transport the body elsewhere and burn it. Instead, Gu secretly buried the body beneath the city walls and deceived Yu Ying, saying, "I have already burned it." Later, Gu offended Yu Ying in some matter, fearing punishment, and planned to exhume the slave's body to threaten him. He consulted Sheng Dong about this. Sheng Dong saw this as a valuable opportunity and pretended to agree, but secretly revealed the matter to Yu Ying. Yu Ying, fearing retribution, offered a substantial bribe to Sheng Dong. Sheng Dong then devised a plan, had Gu killed, and burned his body. The matter remained secret, and no one knew what had transpired.

    Several years later, both Sheng Dong and Yu Ying fell ill. Yu Ying, delirious and seemingly seeing something, recounted the earlier events and said, "Now I am being sued by Gu, and I will surely go with the Nine Old Men." Both men died on the same day. Sheng Dong's illness worsened, and he repeatedly called for his horse. At the time, the horse he rode was being grazed at a nearby temple. When Sheng Dong's spirit departed, the horse suddenly leaped and died. As Yu Ying was dying, he called to his family, "Has the Nine Old Men gone?" They replied, "He has died." Yu Ying then said, "In that case, I shall go as well," and closed his eyes. [Reported by Yu Chui.]

    ○鸡变

    　　辛未， 【 辛未　原本作「是岁」，据说库本改。】 予家一母鸡已伏卵数过，忽冠赤尾长，能鼓翼高鸣，且与他牝相尾。未几，家大疾病，盖咎征也。

    　　○剑池

    　　虎丘剑池水清冽，虽经旱不少减。辛未十二月二十日，无故忽涸见底。八、九十老人云：「所未尝闻也。」池不甚深，傍崖处露一洞，可容数人立，其中亦无所有，但累石数层，若横板而已。

    Chicken Transformation

    In the year 辛未 (1621), one of my hens, which had already incubated eggs multiple times, suddenly developed a red crest and a long tail. It could flap its wings and crow loudly, and it also interacted with other hens. Soon after, there was a serious illness in my family, which seemed to be a sign of impending misfortune.

    Sword Pond

    The water in the Sword Pond at Tiger Hill is clear and cold, and even during drought, it does not decrease much. On 辛未 (1621) December 20th, the pond suddenly dried up, revealing the bottom. Elderly people in their eighties and nineties said, "We have never heard of such an event." The pond is not very deep, and a cave is exposed at the side of the cliff, which can accommodate several people standing. There is nothing of significance inside the cave; it just has several layers of piled stones, looking like a horizontal board.

    Conclusion

    This translation aims to faithfully convey the original text's meaning, cultural context, and historical significance while ensuring clarity and readability in English.

    　　○西山狐

    　　范益者，精于脉药，仕元，至正间为大都医官，年七十矣。尝有老妪诣其门曰：「家有二女属病，欲请公往治之。」问其家所在，曰：「西山。」益惮途远，以老辞，曰：「必不得已，可携来就诊耳。」妪去良久，携女至，皆少艾。益诊之愕然，曰：「何以俱非人脉，必异类也。」因谓妪：「尔无隐，当实告我。」妪惶恐跪诉曰：「妾实非人，乃西山老狐也。知公神术，能生吾女，故来投恳。今已觉露，幸仁者怜而容之。」益曰：「济物吾心也，固不尔拒。然此禁城中帝王所在，万神诃护，尔丑类何得至此？」妪曰：「真天子自在濠州，城隍社令皆移守于彼，此间空虚，故吾辈不妨出入耳。」益异其言，授以药，妪及二女拜谢而去。是时高皇帝龙潜淮右云。益，吾乡刘原博先生之外祖也。刘之祖能道其事。
