    ○ The Fox of the Western Mountains

    Fan Yi, an expert in pulse diagnosis and medicine, served as a medical officer in the Yuan Dynasty during the reign of Emperor Taiding, and was seventy years old. Once, an old woman came to his door and said, "My two daughters are ill, and I wish to ask you to come and treat them." When asked where her home was, she replied, "The Western Mountains." Fan Yi was hesitant due to the long distance and his age, and he declined, saying, "If it is absolutely necessary, you may bring them here for treatment." The woman left and returned after a long time, bringing the two girls with her. Both were young and beautiful. Fan Yi was startled upon examining them, saying, "How can both of them have the pulse of non-humans? They must be of a different kind." He then said to the woman, "Do not hide anything from me; you should tell me the truth." The woman, trembling with fear, knelt and confessed, "I am not human; I am an old fox from the Western Mountains. I heard of your divine skills and your ability to heal my daughters, so I came to seek your help. Now that I have revealed myself, I hope the kind-hearted will show mercy and accept me." Fan Yi said, "It is my wish to help all beings, so I would not refuse you. However, this is the imperial city where the emperor resides, and it is guarded by myriad spirits. How could you, an ugly creature, come here?" The woman replied, "The true emperor is currently in Huaizhou, and the city deities and local officials have all moved there. This place is now empty, so we can come and go without hindrance." Fan Yi was surprised by her words and gave her medicine. The woman and her two daughters bowed in gratitude and left. At that time, the Hongwu Emperor was still in hiding in the Huai River region. Fan Yi was the maternal grandfather of Liu Yuanbo, a scholar from my hometown. Liu's ancestor was able to recount this story.

    47

    ○程学士降笔

    　　弘治己未，篁墩程先生主考会试，以言者去国，未几发背卒。是年京师有雪夜祈仙者，先生至，降笔云：「夜偕东坡游，闻有请仙者，予亦谪仙之流也，事之不偶，殆有甚焉者，诗以纪之。」因书一绝云：「江山何日许重来，白骨青林事可哀。吾党莫怜清梦远，海东东去是蓬莱。 【 海东东去是蓬莱　原本作「海东东去去蓬莱」，据说库本改。】 」又二律云：「紫阁勋名近已休，文章空自压儒流。孤舟敢许悬天日，浩气还应射斗牛。苏子蛰松遭众谤，杜陵荒草唤穷愁。乾坤不尽江流意，回首青山一故丘。」「斯文今古一堪哀，吾道真传己作灰。鸿雁未高罗网合，麒麟偶见信时猜。迅雷不起金縢策，紫电谁知武库才。此气那同芳草合，浑沦来往共盈亏。」读者悲之，玩其气格，盖彷佛先生平昔云。

    Explanation

    47

    Master Cheng's Descent to Write

    In the year 1499 during the reign of the Ming Dynasty Emperor Zhengde, Master Cheng of Huangduan, a prominent scholar, served as the chief examiner for the imperial examination. Due to his remonstrations, he was dismissed from his post and not long after, he died of an illness on his back. That same year, there were those in the capital who sought the company of immortals on a snowy night. Master Cheng appeared and wrote down the following: "At night, I traveled with Su Dongpo, and heard that there were those who sought the company of immortals. I too am of the same ilk as exiled immortals, and my misfortunes have been great. I shall record this in verse." He then wrote a quatrain: "When will I return to these mountains and rivers? The white bones and green forests are a matter of sorrow. My comrades do not pity my distant clear dreams, but the eastern sea leads to the mythical island of Penglai. [The original text reads '海东东去去蓬莱,' but it is said that the library edition reads '海东东去是蓬莱.']" He also wrote two couplets: "The glory of the purple hall has nearly faded, and my writings alone dominate the scholarly world. A lone boat dares to hang the sun in the sky, and my noble spirit should still reach the stars. Su Shi, like a pine tree in hibernation, suffered many slanders, and Du Fu, in the wilderness, called out in despair. The vast heavens and earth cannot contain the meaning of the flowing river, and turning back, I see a solitary hill of green." "The literati of the past and present are all worthy of pity, and my true teachings have turned to ashes. The wild geese have not yet risen high enough to escape the nets, and the qilin is occasionally seen but often misunderstood. The swift thunder does not arise from the golden seal, and who knows the purple lightning is the talent of the military arsenal. This spirit cannot be compared to the fragrance of grass, and the cyclical nature of life and death." Readers were moved by these verses, and considering the spirit and style, they seemed to reflect Master Cheng's character and disposition.

    ○蒋生

    　　蒋生者，名焕，吴人也，少年美姿容，而性质温雅。弘治辛酉，以县学生领乡荐，会试北上，道出临清，日暮憩止道旁民家，爱其门户潇洒。延竚移时，堂中有女郎，映方窗 【 映方窗　似为「方映窗」之误。】 ，悄悄独立，覩生风仪，注目情动，呼青衣邀入中堂。女郎更衣出拜，韶颜稚齿，殆若天仙，生一见为之心醉。逡巡设酒肴，延坐，谈谑稍狎，抵夜同入小阁，遂偕缱绻。时其父适以他往，经三日归，为家人所白，翁闻之怒甚，将执焉。既而沉思久之，顾生曰：「汝良家子，俊士也，吾一女素钟爱，今一旦至此，已无可奈何。

    Explanation

    48

    Mr. Jiang

    Mr. Jiang, whose given name is Huan, was a native of Wu. He was a handsome young man with a gentle and refined nature. In the year Xinyou of the Hongzhi era (1501 AD), he passed the county examination as a student and was recommended for the provincial examination. On his way north to take the metropolitan examination, he traveled through Linqing. At dusk, he rested at a civilian's house by the roadside and admired the elegant appearance of the house. He lingered for a while, and in the hall, he saw a young lady reflected in a square window. She quietly stood alone, noticing Jiang's demeanor, and her emotions stirred. She called a servant to invite him into the main hall. The young lady changed her clothes and came out to bow. She had a beautiful face and youthful teeth, almost like a celestial being. Jiang was immediately captivated by her. They hesitated before setting up wine and food, inviting him to sit, and their conversation became slightly intimate. Until nightfall, they entered a small pavilion together, and they became intimately entangled. At the time, his father was away on other business, and after three days, he returned and was informed by the family. The father heard this and was very angry, intending to apprehend them. After thinking for a long time, he looked at Jiang and said, "You are a fine young man from a good family. My daughter, whom I have always cherished, has now come to this situation, and there is nothing we can do about it."

    49

    虽甘心于子，不足赎吾耻，顾吾女犹未有家，子能为吾壻乎？不则吾将执汝送县官矣。」生唯唯从命，遂偕伉俪，留连越旬。俄迫试期，遂辞行登途，临别相顾，凄断雨泣，升车而去。抵京入试，下第，还到翁家。翁哭而迎曰：「自子行迈，吾女朝夕悲思，因而成疾，今死矣。」引示以女衬，生潸然泣下， 【 潸然泣下　原本作「悚然汗下」，据说库本改。】 仆地欲绝，是夕设祭号恸。辞翁登舟，女已先在矣。从此舟行月余，常觉其在旁，抵家已复在室中。自是动息不离，至啜茶亦于杯中见之。生迷罔憔悴，遂成瘵疾。家人研问，始具述其事。疾益甚，乃徙城中寓所，女复随至，不久竟死，时年二十有三而已。予姊之夫于生有亲，能道其事。

    Explanation

    49

    The husband said, "Even if I am willing to sacrifice myself for you, it is not enough to redeem my shame. But my daughter still has no husband. Can you marry her? Otherwise, I will take you to the authorities." The man obediently agreed, and they lived together as husband and wife, staying for over ten days. Soon the exam date approached, so he bid farewell and set off on his journey. As they parted, they looked at each other with tears streaming down their faces, got on the carriage, and left. Upon arriving in the capital to take the exam, he failed, and returned to the father-in-law's house. The father-in-law wept as he welcomed him, saying, "Since you left, my daughter grieved day and night, fell ill, and has now died." He showed him the daughter's bedding, and the husband's tears welled up in his eyes; he fainted to the ground. That night, he set up an altar and wept loudly. He said goodbye to the father-in-law and boarded the boat, and the daughter was already there. From then on, they traveled by boat for over a month, often feeling her presence nearby. When they arrived home, she was already in the room. From then on, they never parted, even when drinking tea, he saw her in the cup. The husband became bewildered, disoriented, and emaciated, and fell ill with a wasting disease. Family members questioned him, and he began to recount the events. His illness worsened, so he moved to a rented house in the city, and the daughter followed him again. Soon after, she died, and she was only twenty-three years old. My sister's husband is related to the husband and can tell the story.

    ○盛氏怪

    　　郡医官盛早被檄摄狱事，有数囚死，不以理。壬申夏四月， 【 壬申夏四月　原本作「今年夏四月」，据说库本改。】 盛罢摄，携狱中刑具数事归家，囚凭而为厉。初有犬自外衔一死狐而入，置之地，狐忽跃起，犬亦人立与之相搏。家人击逐之，即不见。从此妖变百出：器案互相击撞，床席自移，尝觉有青衣女儿在室，忽钻于榻下，查不可寻。一男子着单衣往来庑间，俄变成大猪，瞥然遂灭。诸妇尝夜坐，见窗外立异物如人，长丈许，皆奔避。怪入，举手撼灯，其影蔽一室。端午日，有医生馈猪头，置肉杌上，连作声长鸣，剖为四悬之，鸣如故。又有馈斋馒头者，方持之，内有声如鬼。如此数月，多方禳之不效。为徙居城中，乃稍稍止。后盛三男相继夭，家人亦皆患病，死丧狼藉，久而洎安。

    Explanation

    50

    The Strange Phenomenon of the Sheng Family

    The county physician, Sheng Zao, was summoned to oversee prison affairs. Several prisoners died in ways that defied logic. In the fourth month of summer in the year Ren Shen, Sheng ceased his duties and brought several prison instruments home with him. The prisoners, relying on these instruments, transformed into spirits that plagued the household.

    At first, a dog brought a dead fox into the house from outside, placing it on the ground. The fox suddenly leaped up, and the dog stood on its hind legs to fight it. The family struck and chased the creatures away, and they immediately disappeared. From then on, strange phenomena began to occur: objects and tables hit each other, beds and mats moved by themselves, and a girl dressed in green was often felt in the room, only to suddenly burrow under the bed and vanish. A man wearing a single garment was seen going back and forth in the corridor, and suddenly turned into a large pig, disappearing in an instant. The women often sat at night and saw a strange object standing outside the window, about a zhang tall, and they all fled in fear. The ghost entered, raised its hand and shook the lamp, its shadow covering the entire room.

    On the Dragon Boat Festival, a doctor gave a pig's head as a gift, which was placed on a meat stand. It made a continuous, long cry, and when cut into four parts and hung, it continued to cry. Another gift of vegetarian steamed buns was brought, and as it was held, a sound like a ghost was heard inside. Such events continued for several months, and despite many attempts to ward them off, they were ineffective. The family moved to the city, and the strange phenomena gradually ceased. However, afterward, Sheng's three sons died one after another, and the family members also fell ill, leading to a disarray of deaths and illnesses. Eventually, peace was restored.

    51

    ○人为牛

    　　苏城大鹿巷唐豆腐家，以磨面为生。其子妇陆氏有弟，死四年矣。唐之季子尝昼假寐，梦陆子来语之曰：「予不幸死，被罚为牛，今卖于君家。君以亲故，幸善遇我，视眼上有白翳者，乃我也。」惊觉，问之其家佣工，两日前正买二牛，一小者目果有白翳。后卖者来，说此牛适四岁矣。陆子平日与唐交易，负其直，不时输，尝誓云：「我若欠钱，应作畜生偿汝。」至是人以为果报云。

    Explanation

    51

    A Human Turned into a Cow

    In the Da Lushan Alley of Suzhou, there was a family of tofu makers named Tang who made a living by grinding flour. His wife, Lu, had a younger brother who had died four years ago. One day, the youngest son of the Tang family took a nap during the day and dreamed that his brother-in-law came to him and said, "I was unfortunate to die and was punished by being turned into a cow. Now I am sold to your household. Since we are related by marriage, please treat me kindly. Look for the one with a white film over the eye; that will be me." He awoke in alarm and asked his household workers. They told him that two days ago, they had exactly bought two cows, and the smaller one indeed had a white film over the eye. Later, the seller came and said this cow was exactly four years old. It was known that Lu usually traded with Tang, owing him money, not paying on time, and once swore, saying, "If I owe money, I should be reborn as an animal to repay you." Thus, people believed this was a case of karma.

    52

    又嘉定富人王全者，尝梦其亡父曰：「吾生时欠江阴某甲钱，今托生其家为牛以偿，且满矣。尔往赎吾归，诸牛惟吾身白，善记之，慎无论价。」全寻到其家，视栏内果有一白牛，求市之，其家惜此牛徤而善运，不许，倍价乃得载归。覆以帷幙，择刍豆精好者饲之，数岁死。

    　　○袁尚宝

    　　鄞人袁尚宝忠彻，得其父太常珙之传，以相术妙天下。尝道吾苏，过阊门沈氏。沈一子方周岁，抱之求观，尚宝笑且抚其首曰：「切头，切头。」更无他言，沈以为戏弄耳。其子长，名洪，凶很不肖，竟坐重辟，是岁录囚，止此一人。吴谚至今有「沈洪出阊门独杀」之语。又尝入南濠徐生药家，生子适三日，方浴而啼，尚宝及堂闻其声曰：「是一强盗耳。」徐闻而怒，几欲捶之。子后亦以探丸论死。古有视熊状而知灭族，闻豺声而识丧宗者，袁术视之，殆不多让也。

    Explanation

    52

    Wang Quan of Jia Ding

    Wang Quan, a wealthy man from Jia Ding, once dreamed that his deceased father said: "When I was alive, I owed money to someone named Jiang Yin. Now I have been reborn into their family as a cow to repay the debt, and it is almost complete. You should redeem me back. Among all the cows, only my body is white. Remember this well, and do not mention the price." Wang Quan went to the family and found that there was indeed a white cow in the pen. He asked to buy it, but the family cherished the cow because it was strong and good at carrying loads, so they did not agree. Only by offering double the price could he bring it back. He covered it with a canopy and fed it the best fodder and beans. After several years, the cow died.

    Yuan Shangbao

    Yuan Shangbao, a native of Yin, inherited his father's legacy and was skilled in physiognomy. Once, he traveled through Wu and passed by the house of Shen at Chang Gate. Shen had a son who was just one year old, and Wang Quan carried him to be examined. Yuan Shangbao smiled and patted his head, saying: "Cut head, cut head." He said no more, and Shen thought it was a joke. The son grew up and became a nameless Shen Hong, who was cruel and unscrupulous, and eventually faced a serious crime. That year, the prison records showed only this one person. The Wu proverb still has the saying "Shen Hong exits Chang Gate alone and kills."

    Yuan Shangbao once entered the home of Xu Shengyao in Nan Hao. Xu's son was just three days old and was crying while being bathed. Yuan Shangbao and the others heard the cry and said: "This is a bandit." Xu heard and became angry, almost wanting to beat him. The child later died due to a ball game incident. In ancient times, there were those who could tell of clan destruction by looking at a bear's appearance and recognize the loss of their clan by hearing a jackal's cry. Yuan Shangbao's ability is not far behind.

    ○还金童子

    　　袁尚宝忠彻居乡时，其友人家一童子，姿貌韶秀，且性机警，尚宝相之，以为不利于主，使逐焉。友虽素神其术，然意不忍也，数言之，不得已而听之。童竟去，无所归，往来寄食于人。一夕宿古庙中，久不寐，见墙角一破衲中裹黄白约数百两，欲取之，忽自叹曰：「我以命薄不得主意，横被遣逐。今更掩有此物，则是不义，天益不容矣，当守之以待失主。」至旦，遂住庙中不去。已而闻哭声，见一妇人掩涕而来，四顾彷徨，问之，答曰：「吾夫，军也，以事系狱应死，指挥某者当治之。

    Explanation

    ○ The Child Who Returns Gold

    When Yuan Shangbao Zhongche lived in his hometown, there was a young boy at his friend's house who was both handsome and shrewd. Shangbao observed the boy and thought he might be a threat to his master, so he ordered him to be expelled. Although the friend had always been in awe of Shangbao's skills, he felt pity and repeatedly advised him, but finally, he reluctantly agreed. The boy was eventually sent away and had no place to go, so he wandered from place to place, eating at others' homes. One night, he stayed in an ancient temple and could not sleep for a long time. He saw a bundle of gold and silver, wrapped in a tattered robe, in the corner of the wall, and was tempted to take it. Suddenly, he sighed and said, "I am unfortunate and cannot please my master. I was unjustly sent away. Now, if I were to take this treasure, it would be unjust, and the heavens would not tolerate it even more. I should guard it until the rightful owner returns." By dawn, he stayed in the temple without leaving. Soon after, he heard crying and saw a woman come, wiping her tears. She looked around hesitantly. He asked her, and she replied, "My husband is a soldier. He was imprisoned for a matter and should be sentenced to death. The commander, someone, should deal with it."

    54

    妾卖家产及假贷，通得金银若干，将以献彼，因裹着破衲中，挈之过庙少憩，不觉遗下，今追寻无得，吾夫分死矣！」童历问其锭数多少，皆合，即举以还之。妇感激，欲分以谢，不受，遂携去，夫因得释。念童之德，徧以语人。指挥者闻而异焉，令人访致之，育于家，年老无子，悦其美慧，遂子之。又数年致仕。此子遂袭职，归而告拜故主，主叹曰：「袁君之术，乃疎如此乎！」留之迟袁至，使仍故服捧茶而出，袁见之，惊起曰：「此故某人耶？何以至是。」主谬云逐出无归，今又来矣。袁笑曰：「君无戏我，今非君仆矣，三品一武官也，形神顿异畴昔，岂尝有善事以致兹乎！」此子为备述前故，友乃叹袁术之神焉。

    Explanation

    54

    A woman, in dire straits, sold her property and borrowed money, collecting a certain amount of gold and silver, which she intended to offer to him. She wrapped the money in a tattered robe and carried it to a temple for a brief rest, but unconsciously left it behind. Unable to find it, she exclaimed, "My husband will surely die!" The child carefully counted the number of ingots, and they all matched, so he immediately returned it to her. Grateful, the woman wanted to share some as thanks, but he refused and took it away. The husband was thus released, and remembering the child's virtue, she told everyone about it. The commander heard about it and was amazed, so he ordered someone to find and bring him home to raise. As he grew older without children, he liked the child's beauty and wisdom, and adopted him. After several more years, he retired. This adopted son then inherited the position, returned home, and paid respects to his former master. The master sighed and said, "Was Master Yuan's method so careless?" He kept him waiting until Master Yuan arrived, and had him return in his old clothes, serving tea. Master Yuan saw him, jumped up in surprise, and said, "Is this the same person? How could this be?" The master falsely claimed that he had been expelled and had no place to go, and now he had returned. Master Yuan laughed and said, "You are not joking with me; I am no longer your servant. I am a third-rank military official now, and my appearance and spirit have changed greatly from before. How could I have done good deeds to reach this point?" This adopted son recounted the previous events, and his friend then marveled at Master Yuan's skill.

    ○户婚亲中司

    　　苏州府学生吴照，仪质瑰伟，音吐洪亮。尝夜梦駃卒捧一牌，其上署朱字数行，跪于前曰：「奉命请相公作户婚亲中司官，愿速行。」照梦中不暇详问，觉而恶之。他日游水仙庙，偶忆前梦，问道士：「道书中有所谓户婚亲中司者乎？」对曰：「有之，在某书中。」照闻之益不乐，居无何感疾，疾革，发言如对下人有所处分者，竟死。疑其遂赴此职也。

    　　○古铜鸭盆

    　　门村朱常家之右室， 【 门村朱常家之右室　原本作「门材朱家常之古室」，据说库本改。】 旧蓄一古铜盆，中有鸭形隐然，初亦不以为异。他日，有农垦土田间，获一铜鸭，农不识，贱价售于朱，以合盆影，不差毫发，注水盆中，鸭辄自浮而浴，遂以为奇宝。后其家被焚，遂付煨烬。 【 右三事徐二元录说。】

    Explanation

    55

    The Official of Household, Marriage, and Kinship

    In Suzhou Prefecture, there was a student named Wu Zhao. He was magnificent in appearance and had a loud, clear voice. One night, he dreamed that swift messengers presented him with a tablet, upon which were inscribed several lines of red characters. They knelt before him and said, "We are commanded to invite you to serve as an official of household, marriage, and kinship disputes. Please proceed quickly." Wu Zhao did not have time to ask detailed questions in his dream, but upon waking, he found the dream repulsive. Later, while visiting the Temple of the Water God, he recalled his dream and asked a Taoist priest, "Are there any references to an official of household, marriage, and kinship disputes in Daoist texts?" The priest replied, "Yes, it is mentioned in a certain book." Upon hearing this, Wu Zhao became even less happy. Shortly after, he fell ill, and his condition worsened. He spoke as if giving orders to subordinates, and eventually died. It is suspected that he took up this post in the afterlife.

    The Ancient Bronze Basin with a Duck

    In the right chamber of Zhu Chang's house in Men Village, there was an ancient bronze basin. Inside, the shape of a duck was faintly visible, and initially, it was not considered unusual. One day, a farmer plowed the fields and found a bronze duck. Not recognizing it, the farmer sold it at a low price to Zhu. When the duck was placed in the basin, it perfectly matched the shadow inside, without a hair's breadth difference. When water was poured into the basin, the duck immediately floated and bathed itself. Zhu then considered it a rare treasure. Later, Zhu's house was burned down, and the basin was reduced to ashes. [These three stories were recorded by Xu Er Yuan.]

    ○侍女峯

    　　里中医师朱玑作池岛，买石西山。掘地，有峯卧土中，工运锹而断焉。植而观之，其首若妇人鬟，两肩以下若袖之垂腰，左右小支若飘带然，俨一图画中侍女凝立也。扣之，声清越如玉磬，惜其已断，徒叹咤置之。

    　　○蛇癫

    　　嘉定有王某者，家颇丰，年四十许，得癫疾。尝号其家人曰：「我腰间沉重，何不为我解却？」积数年不愈。他日，王有甥来省视，怜其病态，因请与俱归，使游衍自适。留数日，病如故，甥常使人随之。一日，王散步后圃，圃中畜鹤一羣，悉奔遶之，争啄其腰下。会从者至，麾其鹤去。王戄然汗下，觉病如失，还语甥曰：「吾瘳矣。吾适遭羣鹤。一惊，觉腰间顿轻，甚快也。」甥喜，往视后圃，见一蛇大如椽，死竹间，犹带血。王从是平复。疑其疾是蛇所为，盖鹤羣啄蛇也。 【 吴越说。】

    Explanation

    56

    Stone Figure of a Standing Attendant

    A local physician named Zhu Ji was constructing a garden island and purchased stones from the western mountains. While digging, they discovered a stone lying in the earth. The workers broke it off with shovels. When planted and observed, the top of the stone resembled a woman's bun, the lower part below the shoulders looked like sleeves hanging down to the waist, and the smaller parts on the sides resembled flowing ribbons. It appeared as if a standing attendant from a painting. When struck, it produced a clear and resonant sound like a jade chime. Unfortunately, it had already been broken, and they merely sighed and placed it aside.

    Madness Caused by a Snake

    In Jiading, there was a man named Wang, whose family was quite wealthy and who was around forty years old. He contracted a form of madness. He once shouted at his family, saying, "My waist feels heavy; why don't you take it off?" The condition lasted for several years without improvement. One day, Wang's nephew came to visit and pitied his condition. He asked to go back with him to let him wander and enjoy himself. They stayed for several days, but his illness remained the same. The nephew often had someone accompany him. One day, Wang was strolling in the backyard, where a flock of cranes was kept. The cranes rushed around him, pecking at his waist. Just then, the attendant arrived and drove the cranes away. Wang broke out in a sweat and felt the illness disappear. He returned to tell his nephew, "I am cured. I just encountered a flock of cranes. A sudden shock made me feel my waist suddenly lighten, and it felt very good." The nephew was delighted and went to check the backyard, where he saw a snake as big as a beam, dead in the bamboo grove, still with blood on it. From then on, Wang recovered. He suspected that the illness was caused by the snake, as the cranes had been pecking it. [According to Wu Yue's account.]

    57

    ○苟毕元帅

    　　玄妙观道士郭渊静，宦族子，道业颇精。饮马桥居人李旭遘疫，延渊静建醮。至昏时，渊静握剑及水盂辟除于旭寝所。既出，旭问其妻曰：「适为何人？」曰：「郭老师也。」旭讶曰：「我适见一人披发而束额，左绾索，右挈槌，状如神人，此何也？」妻以为谵语，不省。旭疾顿瘳，诣渊静具说所见，渊静曰：「吾心将雷霆苟毕元帅也。」旭乃悟，为扣头谢。

    　　○顾镇

    　　正德辛未夏，疫疠盛行。葑门■〈王〈爫曼〉〉姬墩西居民顾镇家，老幼皆染疾，因祈于神，誓合家茹素以禳灾。适巡抚开仓赈济，镇入城关领米， 【 镇入城关领米　「米」字原无，据说库本补。】 偶忘其誓，于肆中买鱼三尾，酒一壶，饮啖毕，附舟而归，不以语家人也。是日感疾，不食顷而终。家人见三小鳑魮蛰其背，及殓，又见三鱼跃入棺中，索之则不复有矣。问之同入城者，乃知镇前所食正此物也，神盖以示警云。

    Explanation

    57

    ○苟毕元帅

    A Taoist priest named Guo Yuansheng, a descendant of a noble family, was highly skilled in Taoist practices. A resident of Yimaqiao named Li Xu contracted an illness and invited Guo to perform a ritual. At dusk, Guo held a sword and a water basin to ward off evil spirits at Li's sleeping quarters. Afterward, Li asked his wife, "Who was that person?" She replied, "It was Master Guo." Li was surprised and said, "I just saw a man with long hair tied on his forehead, with a rope on his left and a mallet on his right, resembling a divine being. Who is he?" His wife thought he was delirious and did not understand. Li's illness suddenly disappeared, and he went to Guo to describe what he had seen. Guo said, "I invoked the Thunder and Lightning God, Spoiled General, in my heart." Li then realized and bowed deeply in gratitude.

    ○顾镇

    In the summer of 1511 during the Ming Dynasty, an epidemic spread widely. The family of Gu Zhen, a resident of the western part of Fongmen, were all infected with the disease. They prayed to the gods and vowed to eat only vegetarian food to ward off the disaster. Just as the governor opened the granaries to distribute relief, Gu entered the city gate to collect rice. He accidentally forgot his vow and bought three fish and a pot of wine at a shop, drank and ate them, and returned by boat without telling his family. That day, he fell ill and died shortly after. His family saw three small fish on his back, and when they prepared the coffin, they saw the three fish jump into the coffin. When they searched for them, they were no longer there. They asked others who had entered the city with him and learned that the fish he had eaten were the same ones. The gods must have used this to warn him.

    58

    ○王栾

    　　葑门人王栾，以辛未冬至日诣玄妙观高真殿烧香，途中见渔者持一鳖甚肥大，栾素所嗜，令从者买之，先归烹炮。既入庙，一念在是，殊不诚恪。归而食罢，至暮，其阴侧忽肿一块，痛不可忍，数日几死，医祷百方不效。延巫者周道虎附乩召将，判云：「温元帅下报坛。申时玄天亲降东南方，黑云为验。」至时，黑云起于巽偶，隐隐见披发仗剑者立云际，满堂中檀麝香气氤氲。须臾，乩大发，入栾寝所，判令其妻掖病者以汤洗肿处，肿破出一骨，首尾形状宛如一鳖，创合而愈。自是其家奉真武甚虔恪。 【 右三事道士陈然裔说。】

    　　○猪犬生儿

    　　壬申春， 【 壬申春　原本作「今年春」，据说库本改。】 长洲阳城湖旁民家母猪产一雏，猪头而人手足。十二月十六日，嘉定二十二都民家犬生一儿，形状皆人，但足根短，背微有毛。或以人与畜交而生，理或然也。

    Explanation

    58

    王栾

    葑门人王栾，于辛未年冬至日前往玄妙观的高真殿烧香。途中见到渔夫手持一只非常肥大的鳖，王栾平素就喜欢这种食物，便命令随从买下它，先回家烹制。进入庙中后，他心中只想着那只鳖，丝毫没有虔诚恭敬之心。回家吃完饭后，到了傍晚，他的阴部一侧突然肿起一块，疼痛难忍，几天后几乎丧命，尽管医生和祈祷者尝试了各种方法都未能奏效。于是请来巫师周道虎附乩召将，判词说：“温元帅降临报坛。申时玄天亲自降于东南方，以黑云为证。”到了约定的时间，黑云从西南方向升起，隐约可见一位披发持剑的人站在云际，整个殿堂中弥漫着檀香和麝香的香气。不久，乩板剧烈移动，进入王栾的卧室，判词命令他的妻子扶着病人用热水清洗肿处，肿块破裂后露出一根骨头，首尾形状宛如一只鳖，伤口愈合后痊愈。从此，王栾一家对真武非常虔诚恭敬。【以上三事由道士陈然裔讲述。】

    猪犬生儿

    壬申年春天，【原本作“今年春”，据说库本改为“壬申春”。】 长洲阳城湖旁的一户人家的母猪生下一只幼崽，长着猪头和人的手足。十二月十六日，嘉定二十二都的一户人家的狗生下一只幼崽，形状完全像人，只是脚跟较短，背上有些许毛发。有人认为可能是人与动物交配所生，这种说法或许有道理。

    59

    ○梓潼神

    　　陈僖敏公镒父孟玉，为人愿悫，乡闾称善士。尝出行登厕，见锅底饭一块在厕旁，拾取于水中涤而食之，其平居不欲暴殄率如此。是夜，梦神人告之曰：「翁好善如此，当获福报。吾梓潼神也，将降生以大而门。吾在胥门线香桥人家楼上，其家不知奉事，翁今速往迎归尔。」既觉，语其妻，则妻梦亦如之。即访至其家，主妇出，延之登楼，壁挂神像尘埃脱落，因乞以归，加装饰，奉事甚虔。未几有姙，生僖敏，仕至太子太保、左都御史，累赠翁如其官，母为一品夫人云。以予观之，如僖敏公之硕德伟度，功在西土，民皆尸而祝之，为一时名臣，殆所谓其生有自来者耶。 【 僖敏从孙汴为吴翁说。】

    　　○妇人生须

    　　弘治末，随州应山县女子生髭，长三寸余，见于邸报。予里人卓四者，往年商于郑阳，见人家一妇美色，颔下生须三缭，约数十茎，长可数寸，人目为三须娘云。

    Explanation

    59

    The God of Zitong

    Chen Ximin Gong Yi's father, Meng Yu, was a simple and honest man, well-regarded in his village. Once, while traveling and using the restroom, he saw a piece of leftover rice at the bottom of a pot near the latrine. He picked it up, washed it in water, and ate it, demonstrating his usual frugality in daily life. That night, he dreamed of a divine being who told him, "Your kindness is so great, you will receive blessings. I am the God of Zitong, and I will be born to greatly benefit your family. I am currently residing in a house on the upper floor of Xianxiang Bridge in Xumen, but the family there does not know how to worship me. Go quickly and bring me back." Upon waking, he told his wife about the dream, and she had had the same dream. They immediately went to the house, and the lady of the house invited them up to the floor. There was a dusty and detached deity image hanging on the wall, so they asked for it and took it home, decorating it and worshipping it with great reverence. Soon after, his wife became pregnant and gave birth to Ximin, who rose to the position of Grand Tutor and Left Censor-in-Chief, and was posthumously honored with the same rank as his official position, with his mother being ennobled as a First-Rank Lady. From my perspective, Ximin Gong's great virtue and remarkable achievements, his contributions to the western lands, and the people's worship of him as a deity, make him a renowned statesman of his time. It seems that his birth was predestined. [This was told by Ximin Gong's cousin Bian to Wu翁.]

    A Woman with a Beard

    At the end of the Hongzhi era, a woman from Yingshan County in Suizhou grew a beard that was over three inches long, which was reported in the official gazette. One of my fellow villagers, Zhuo Si, who was a merchant in Zhengyang, once saw a beautiful woman with three twists of beard under her chin, about several dozen strands long, each about an inch, and she was called the Three-Beard Lady.

    60

    ○黑眚

    　　壬申岁，北方顺德、涿州、河间有物青赤色黑，或如犬，或如猫。其行如风，夜空中飞下，或爪人面额，或啮人手足，逐之不见踪迹，盖黑眚类也。

    　　○火灾

    　　三月， 【 三月　说库本作「二月」。】 山东秦始皇庙钟皷，夜无故自鸣。火起桑上，被燔而枝叶无损，庙宇荡毁，而神像在火中都不焦灼。是月，江西余干之仙居寨，夜大雷电，西北风，有流火如箭坠旗竿上，如灯笼光照四野。戍卒或撼其旗，火直飞上竿首，卒因发炮冲之，其火四散，阖寨鎗首皆有光如星，须臾而灭。五月，广西方春北寨各鎗上亦有光 【 广西方春北寨　说库本作「广西万春北寨」。】 。并邸报云。

    Translation

    Black Omens

    In the year of the Water Monkey, there were creatures in Shunde, Zhuozhou, and Hejian in the north. These creatures were a mix of green, red, and black, sometimes appearing like dogs, other times like cats. They moved as swiftly as the wind, descending from the night sky. Some clawed at people's faces and foreheads, others bit their hands and feet. When pursued, they left no trace, being of the nature of black omens.

    Fire Incidents

    In March, at the Qin Shi Huang Temple in Shandong, the bells and drums rang spontaneously at night without any apparent cause. A fire broke out on a mulberry tree, burning the trunk but leaving the branches and leaves unharmed. The temple was completely destroyed by the fire, but the statues of the gods remained unscathed. In the same month, at the Xianju Camp in Yudan, Jiangxi, there was a severe thunderstorm with a northwest wind. A streak of fire fell like an arrow onto a flagpole, illuminating the surrounding area like a lantern. A soldier shook the flag, and the fire flew straight to the top of the pole. The soldier then fired a cannon to extinguish the fire, causing it to scatter in all directions. The muzzles of all the guns in the camp glowed like stars, and the phenomenon disappeared shortly after. In May, similar glowing phenomena were observed on the muzzles of the guns at the Fangchun North Camp in Guangxi. These events were also reported in the official bulletins.

    　　○王士能

    　　济宁有王士能者，故海州人，生元至正甲辰，入国朝成化癸卯，已一百二十岁，其寓济宁亦六十年矣。自其少时，志慕养生，辞家走四方，求名师无所遇。入蜀，闻雪山有异人，往投之，见老人披毡衣，卧深洞中石床上，其长三尺余，五官、手足皆如婴儿。士能拜之，不答，因为之执役左右。老人不饮食，坐侧一囊，所盛类干面，时取啖之，或掬饮涧水一二升。士能留数日，所赍米尽，跪而乞食，老人分囊中物与之，苦涩不能下咽，乃拾山菓野菜以充腹。居三年，勤苦不懈，老人怜之，一旦谓曰：「子可以语道矣，然子得之当出山，他日非其人勿轻授也。」遂示以摄形炼气之要，学成，辞出。又久之，乃来居济宁。日常不火食，惟啖枣数枚，或菜数茎，饮水少许而已。白发被颔，肌肤如童子少妇。其初人不识，后乃稍稍异之。

    ○ Wang Shen Neng

    In Jining, there was a man named Wang Shen Neng, originally from Haizhou. Born in the year Jia Chen of the Zhizheng era of the Yuan dynasty (1354), he entered the country's official calendar in the Gui Mao year of the Chenghua era of the Ming dynasty (1473), having reached the age of one hundred and twenty. He had resided in Jining for sixty years. From his youth, he aspired to the art of longevity and left home to wander the world, seeking a master but finding none. He traveled to Sichuan and heard that there was an extraordinary person on the Snowy Mountains, so he went to seek him out. He saw an old man wearing a felt robe, lying on a stone bed in a deep cave, measuring over three feet in length, with all his senses, hands, and feet resembling those of an infant. Shen Neng bowed to him, but the old man did not respond, so Shen Neng served him on his left and right. The old man did not eat or drink, but he had a bag beside him, which contained something like dry flour, and he would occasionally take some to eat, or scoop up a few liters of spring water to drink. Shen Neng stayed for several days, and the rice he had brought was all gone. He knelt and begged for food, and the old man gave him some of the contents of his bag, which was bitter and hard to swallow. Shen Neng then gathered wild fruits and vegetables to fill his stomach. After three years of diligent and tireless effort, the old man pitied him and one day said to him, "You can now be told the way, but when you have learned it, you must leave the mountains, and in the future, do not lightly impart it to others." He then taught Shen Neng the essentials of shaping his form and refining his energy. After mastering the teachings, Shen Neng bid farewell and left. After a long time, he returned to reside in Jining. His daily diet consisted of eating a few dates, or a few stems of vegetables, and drinking a little water. He had white hair covering his chin, and his skin was like that of a young boy or young woman. At first, people did not recognize him, but later, they began to see him as somewhat unusual.

    62

    济宁指挥王宣亦海州人，往见，问姓名大惊，曰：「闻吾祖言，吾上世有叔祖，实名士能，好道出家，不知所终，翁是乎？」问以家事，所言皆合，于是日往候之。州人闻而有所馈者，士能皆辞不受。宣有同官往，欲受其术，士能望见曰：「尔声妓满前，日事妄作，非吾徒也。」谢之。其人大惭，乃上疏言状。朝廷下山东守臣，俾乘安车入京，得见上，赐宝镪遣归。士能被召时，篁墩程先生适道其地，闻州人说其履历如此，因往谒焉。

    Explanation

    62

    Commander Wang Xuan of Jining was also from Haizhou. Upon meeting, he asked about his name and was greatly surprised, saying, "I have heard from my ancestors that in my distant past, there was an uncle who was a true scholar named Shi Neng, who liked the Dao and left home, and no one knows what happened to him. Are you him?" He asked about family matters, and everything he said matched. Thus, Wang Xuan visited him daily. People in the state heard and brought gifts, but Shi Neng refused all of them. Wang Xuan had a colleague who went to see him, wanting to learn his techniques. Shi Neng saw him and said, "You have music and entertainers all around, and daily engage in frivolous activities. You are not one of us." The colleague apologized to him. The person was greatly ashamed and then submitted a memorial detailing the situation. The court ordered the governor of Shandong, and he was to ride a sedan chair to the capital to meet the emperor, who granted him treasures and sent him back. When Shi Neng was summoned, Mr. Cheng from Huangdun happened to be passing through the area. He heard the people in the state describe his background like this and then went to pay him a visit.

    63

    士能所居城东僻处，老木深巷，败屋数间，屋中卧榻外无长物。与客言，多静坐寡欲之说，坐久瞑目闭息曰：「老仆无能为，朝廷过听而召之。仆岂知道，但习静日久，近日乃与人接，大败吾事矣。」问以元末国初事，曰：「一身之外皆非所知也。」后三年丙午，吾苏杨南峯先生以使事过济宁，微服访之，见士能着白禅衣坐木榻上 【 见士能着白禅衣坐木榻上　「白禅衣」说库本作「白单衣」。】 ，扣其所以致寿，曰：「无他术也，但平生不茹荤，不娶妻，不识数，不争气耳。」先生为之叹息而返。要之其人，盖有道之士云。

    Explanation

    63

    The recluse, known as Shiren, lived in a secluded part of the city east of the walls, in a deep alley lined with old trees and surrounded by a few dilapidated houses. Inside, his dwelling contained only a sleeping area and nothing else of value. When speaking with guests, he often discussed the virtues of stillness and minimal desires, and after sitting for a long time, he would close his eyes and hold his breath, saying, "An old servant like me has no great accomplishments; the court summoned me through excessive listening. How could I know anything? I have only practiced stillness for a long time. Recently, I have begun to interact with others, and this has greatly disrupted my affairs." When asked about events from the late Yuan and early Ming dynasties, he replied, "I know nothing beyond myself." Three years later, in the year of Bingwu, Yang Nanfeng, a scholar from Suzhou, traveled to Jining on official business and, disguised, sought out Shiren. He found Shiren sitting on a wooden bench, wearing a white robe [which some editions refer to as a "white single-layered robe"]. Yang asked him about the secret to his longevity, and Shiren responded, "There is no other method. I simply do not eat meat, do not marry, do not count or calculate, and do not strive for success." Yang sighed and returned. In summary, Shiren was a person of virtue, a sage.

    ○王主簿

    　　张氏据苏日，胥门有王主簿者，故元官也，平日所积俸赀颇厚。主簿感伤寒七日死，既葬，二子析产，求其赀不得，疑母匿之，以咎母，母无以自明，终日喧竞。主簿对门有徐姓者，商于远方，归至金山，泊舟五圣庙下。黎明时起，见一舟上五人冠带坐，皆衣白，中一人则主簿也。徐故与王通家，主簿其父行也。未知其死，揖而问曰：「丈何缘来此？」主簿前曰：「君来甚善，吾正欲有所恳也。

    Explanation

    64

    ○Wang, the Clerk

    During the time when Zhang held power in Suzhou, there was a clerk named Wang who lived opposite the city gate. He was an official from the Yuan dynasty and had accumulated a considerable amount of salary and wealth over the years. Wang died of a severe cold after seven days. After his burial, his two sons divided the estate. They could not find the wealth and suspected that their mother had hidden it, blaming her for it. The mother could not prove her innocence and they argued and quarreled all day.

    Opposite the Wang household lived a man named Xu, a merchant who traveled far away. He returned to Jinshan and moored his boat at the foot of the Wu Saints Temple. At dawn, he woke up and saw five men in official attire sitting on a boat, all dressed in white. One of them was Wang, the clerk. Xu was acquainted with Wang's family, and Wang was like a father figure to Xu. Xu did not know that Wang had died. He bowed and asked, "Why are you here?" Wang stepped forward and said, "It is good that you have come. I have something I wish to ask of you."

    65

    吾在此数日矣，来时匆遽，不及处分家事。吾有薄赀若干，藏卧榻中板下，二子不知，乃与母竞。又有分书一纸，藏匣中，置房门帘楹上，君为我语之。」又密谓曰：「君归告吾家人，早晚有大兵到吴城，城中人当大半死，宜急移居杭州可免也。」徐唯唯，恍然登舟而别。归到主薄家，见其妻说曾相见状，妻怒以为妄语。徐具道所以，二子闻之，发地板果得白金八百两，视帘楹匣子亦如所言，家人神之。因与徐俱挈家迁于杭。不两月，而天兵围吴矣。 【 家君说。】

    Explanation

    65

    I have been here for several days, arriving in haste and not having time to settle family affairs. I have some meager wealth hidden under the board of my bed, and my two sons do not know about it, so they are competing with the mother. There is also a letter of division hidden in a box, placed on the door curtain and lintel, which you should tell them for me. He then secretly told, "When you return, tell my family that there will be a large army coming to Wu City soon, and most of the people in the city will die. It is advisable to quickly move to Hangzhou to avoid it." Xu nodded and then suddenly boarded the boat and left. Upon returning to the household of the county magistrate, Xu met his wife and told her about the previous encounter. The wife was angry and thought it was nonsense. Xu explained the reason in detail. When the floorboard was removed, eight hundred taels of silver were indeed found, and the box on the door curtain and lintel was also as he said. The family was amazed. Therefore, they all moved their families to Hangzhou together. Within two months, the heavenly army surrounded Wu. [As told by my father.]

    ○人魂出游

    　　葑门有百姓为里长，以索役钱，适齐门钱万李桥 【 适齐门钱万李桥　说库本作「适齐门万里桥」。】 ，暑月从一童奴早行，少憩人家檐前。奴坐阶下，有顷便熟寐，主亦颇思睡，朦胧间见一小儿戏舞于奴身，俄下地，从一板过隔溪菜畦中。良久，主蹵奴不起，至溪边掣其板，儿还不能渡，临水彷徨，仍置板原所，乃得过，复还上奴体而没，遂醒。主诘之，云：「适梦乘桥入一苑中，乔木千章，戏游甚适，及归，被人掣桥板，几不得渡。」主方悟所见小儿是其魂也。

    Explanation

    66

    Human Soul's Journey

    In the district of Fong Gate, there was a commoner who served as the village headman, tasked with collecting labor fees. He headed towards the Qimen Bridge at Qianwan Li Bridge [Note: The library edition reads "Qimen Ten Thousand Li Bridge"]. During the hot summer months, he set out early in the morning accompanied by a young servant. They took a brief rest under the eaves of a house. The servant sat on the steps and soon fell into a deep sleep. The master also felt drowsy and, in a half-asleep state, saw a small child playing and dancing on the servant's body. The child then descended to the ground and crossed the stream to a vegetable plot using a board. After a long while, the master kicked the servant, who did not wake up. He reached the stream and pulled the board away. The child was unable to cross back and stood by the water, hesitating. The child then placed the board back in its original place and crossed. The child returned to the servant's body and disappeared, causing the servant to wake up. The master questioned the servant, who said, "I just had a dream where I crossed a bridge into a garden filled with tall trees and enjoyed playing. When I tried to return, someone pulled the bridge away, and I almost couldn't cross." The master then realized that the child he saw was the servant's soul.

    67

    又嘉定有士人尝访一僧，值其方睡，因坐榻前待之，忽见一小蛇自僧鼻窍中出，蜿蜒至地。其人异之，取几上小刀插地，蛇至其侧，如有所畏者，俟拔起，乃复行。其人唾地，蛇餂食之，出户外水潭中，偃仰久之，冉冉过花药栏，仍寻旧路登榻，自鼻窍而入。僧睡觉，为其人言：「适梦出行，遇盗植刃道上，几不能免。见道旁水如甘露，食之甚美，浴于海中，乐甚，乃入花园，游适而返，不知何所感也。」其人唯唯，竟不告以所见而罢。尝闻人魂能出游，以此二事验之，信然。

    Explanation

    67

    During the reign of Emperor Ling, there was a scholar in Jiading who once visited a monk. When he happened to be sleeping, the scholar sat in front of the monk's bed and waited for him. Suddenly, he saw a small snake emerge from the monk's nostril and slither to the ground. The scholar was surprised and took a small knife from the table and stuck it in the ground. When the snake reached its side, it seemed to be afraid. When the scholar pulled the knife up, the snake continued its way. The scholar spat on the ground, and the snake licked it up. It then went out to the outdoor water pool, lay and stretched out for a long time, and slowly passed by the flower and medicine stand. It returned to its original path and climbed back onto the bed, entering through the monk's nostril. The monk woke up and spoke to the scholar, saying, "I just dreamed of going out and encountered a thief who planted a blade on the road, almost unable to escape. I saw water by the roadside that tasted like nectar, drank it and found it very delicious, bathed in the sea, and was very happy. I then entered a garden, wandered around, and returned, not knowing what I was feeling." The scholar nodded in agreement but finally did not tell him what he had seen and left. He had heard that human souls could leave the body, and these two events confirmed this belief, indeed.

    68

    ○肉芝

    　　癸酉春 【 癸酉春　原本作「今年春」，据说库本改。】 ，长洲漕湖之滨，有农妇治田，见湖滩一物，白如雪，趋视之，乃一小儿手也，连臂约长尺许，其下作声唧唧。惊走报其夫，夫往看亦甚疑怪，掘之，其根不可穷，乃折而弃之湖。尝读神仙感遇传云：「兰陵萧静之掘地得物，类如人手，肥润而红，烹而食之，踰月发再生，力壮貌少。复值道士顾静之曰：『神气若是，必尝仙药。』指其脉曰：『所食者肉芝也，寿等龟鹤矣。』」然则漕湖之物，正此类耳，乃不幸弃乎愚夫之手，惜哉！

    Explanation

    68

    Translation:

    Meat Fungus

    In the spring of the year Gengyou (or Kuiyou, depending on the calendar system), by the shore of Cao Lake in Changzhou, a peasant woman was tending her fields when she saw an object on the lakebank, white as snow. She hurried to examine it and found it to be a child's hand, with arms connected, about a foot long, and making a chirping sound from below. Alarmed, she ran to tell her husband, who also went to look at it and was greatly puzzled. They dug into the ground, but its root could not be traced, so they broke it off and threw it into the lake.

    I once read in the Records of Immortals and Their Encounters that in the time of Xiao Jingzhi of Lanling, a man unearthed an object while digging, which resembled a human hand, was fleshy, moist, and red. After cooking and eating it, he regained his hair after a month, became strong, and appeared youthful. Later, he met a Taoist named Gu Jingzhi, who said, "With such spirit and energy, you must have taken elixir of immortality." The Taoist pointed to his pulse and said, "What you ate was meat fungus, which grants a lifespan as long as that of turtles and cranes."

    Thus, the object from Cao Lake was indeed of this kind, but it was unfortunately discarded by the hands of a foolish man. How regrettable!

    69

    ○郑灏

    　　里人郑灏，尝娶后妻，设席既罢，失去一银杯，重数两。其家织帛工及挽丝佣各数十人，欲自明其非盗也，相率列名书状为誓，投之城隍神祠。灏止之不得，亦不复觅杯。一日，灏倚门立，少时入内，忽仆地，家人掖以登榻，四肢已冷，独心下微暖，环守之，至半夜乃醒，问所以死，摇手不对。天明乃言：「初在门见一皂自西奔驰而来，势甚猛恶，吾意官府有所追摄也，将入避之，皂及门，径前捽吾曰：『奉命勾汝。』便以索缚吾颈，驱出行数百步，抵城隍庙。有白衣老人立门外，见呼吾名，皂令老人相守，先驰入报，复出引入，跪于庭。

    Explanation

    ○ Zheng Hao

    There was a man named Zheng Hao in the village who had once married a second wife. After a banquet, he lost a silver cup weighing several taels. His family included dozens of silk weavers and silk-drawing servants who wanted to prove their innocence, so they wrote a statement as an oath and threw it into the city god temple. Zheng Hao could not stop them and no longer searched for the cup. One day, Zheng Hao stood at the door, and after a short while, he entered the house. Suddenly, he fell to the ground. His family members supported him onto a bed. His limbs were cold, but his heart was slightly warm. They surrounded and guarded him until midnight when he woke up. He asked why he thought he had died, shaking his head and not answering. At dawn, he spoke: "At first, I saw a black-clad person rushing from the west, looking very fierce and evil. I thought the officials were pursuing someone, so I intended to enter and avoid them. The black-clad person reached the door, grabbed me, and said, 'I am here by order to summon you.' He then tied a rope around my neck and dragged me for several hundred steps to the city god temple. There was an elderly man in white clothes standing outside the door. He saw me and called my name. The black-clad person ordered the elderly man to guard me, rushed in to report, and then came out again to lead me inside. I knelt in the courtyard."

    70

    神坐殿上，厉声叱问以投誓之故。顿首谢不知，神愈怒，曰：『忆失银杯事乎？此杯是汝孙盗耳，如何诬妄他人，致其干扰官府！』吾再拜，具陈非己意，神呼之前曰：『汝孙盗杯以质钱于汝家之东银匠铺中，今犹置架上，尔欲见之乎？』顾一卒，令取杯示之，真吾家物也。良久，神怒稍解，曰：『今姑放汝，至二十六日行牌提此一干人鞫之。』吾但拜不已，俄又闻殿上传言曰：『既人众，且不推究，但要汝去与众人说，令他知过。』因放出门，乃得活。」即遣人到银匠家访之，杯果在架上，其孙所质也。诸人闻而怖畏，亟诣庙陈谢，犹惴惴，弥月乃得自安。 【 徐说。】

    Explanation

    70

    The god sat on the throne and sternly scolded and questioned me about the reason for the vow. I kowtowed and apologized, saying I did not know, but the god became even angrier and said, "Do you remember the matter of the lost silver cup? This cup was stolen by your grandson. How can you falsely accuse others, causing interference with the government?" I bowed twice and fully stated that it was not my own intention. The god called me forward and said, "Your grandson stole the cup to pawn for money at the silver shop east of your house. It is still placed on the shelf. Do you want to see it?" He looked at a soldier and ordered him to fetch the cup and show it to me. It was indeed a household item. After a long time, the god's anger slightly subsided and said, "I will temporarily release you. On the 26th day, I will issue an order to bring these people for interrogation." I continued to bow without stopping. Suddenly, I heard a voice from the hall saying, "Since there are many people, and we won't investigate further, just go and tell the others, so they know they have made a mistake." Therefore, I let you out, and you were saved. Immediately, someone was sent to the silversmith's house to check, and the cup was indeed on the shelf, pawned by his grandson. The others heard and were terrified, quickly going to the temple to apologize. They still felt anxious, and it took a month to feel secure. [Xu said.]

    ○蒋子修

    　　南京监察御史蒋钦，字子修，有刚直名。正德初元，偕同官十三人上疏论时事。方夜属草灯下，闻筐箧间鬼声戢戢 【 闻筐箧间鬼声戢戢　「鬼声」原本作「鬼神」，据说库本改。】 。子修自念此疏一上，且掇奇祸，彼鸣者将非吾先人之灵覆念后胤，欲以尼吾事乎？因起视曰：「倘是吾祖宗，何不厉声告我。」言未毕，声四振于壁。子修叹曰：「吾业已委身，义不得顾私，使缄默负国为先人羞，亦均于不孝矣。」因奋笔曰：「死耳，不可易也。」声遂止。疏上，与同官皆坐逮，被杖创甚。诸人或迎医饮药，子修独曰：「吾得死所矣。」竟不疗治而卒，天下伤之。子修，吾苏之常熟人，弘治丙辰进士。

    71

    Chiang Chih-hsiu

    Chiang Chin, a censor in the capital Nanjing, was known for his integrity and courage. During the early years of the Zhengde era, he joined thirteen other officials in submitting a memorial to the emperor regarding current affairs. Late at night, as he was drafting the document by the lamp, he heard a rustling sound in the bamboo basket, which he interpreted as a ghostly presence. Chiang Chin thought to himself, "If I submit this memorial, I will likely bring about a great disaster. Could the one making this sound be the spirit of my ancestors, warning me to reconsider my actions?" He stood up and said, "If it is indeed my ancestors, why don't you speak up and warn me more clearly?" Before he finished speaking, the sound echoed through the walls. Chiang Chin sighed and said, "I have already committed myself to this cause. I cannot prioritize personal safety over my duty to the country. To remain silent and betray the nation would be a dishonor to my ancestors and a form of filial impiety." With determination, he wrote, "It's death, and nothing can change that." The sound then ceased. The memorial was submitted, and Chiang Chin and his colleagues were all arrested and subjected to severe punishment. While others sought medical treatment and care, Chiang Chin alone said, "I have found my place of death." He refused treatment and died as a result. The whole country mourned his death. Chiang Chin was from Changshu in the region of Wu and passed the imperial examination in 1496 during the Hongzhi era.

    ○黑鱼

    　　相城刘浩尝昼寝，梦一黑衣人前立，白衣者数人随之，拜诉曰：「吾辈居此四五十年矣，今为君家所获，幸垂仁相舍。」惊觉，甚疑之。是夕，家奴网鱼者获大黑鱼重数十斤，又有数白鱼差小，以献浩，浩悟前梦，即以足蹵诸水中放之。

    Explanation

    72

    A Black Fish

    Liu Hao from Xiangcheng once took a daytime nap and dreamed of a black-clothed figure standing before him, followed by several white-clothed figures. They bowed and said, "We have lived here for forty or fifty years, but now we are captured by your family. Please show mercy and let us go." Awakening in shock, Liu Hao doubted the dream greatly. That night, a household servant who was fishing caught a large black fish weighing several dozen pounds, along with several smaller white fish, and presented them to Liu Hao. Realizing his previous dream, Liu Hao immediately kicked the fish into the water and released them.

    ○青虎

    　　刘瀚者，浩弟也，平生未尝素食。尝夜梦一虎，毛色深青，来逐己，被啮腰间，痛而寤，汗流徧体。及明，视腰间有五齿痕，青肿，出血成疮。因持斋设醮三年，乃瘥。 【 右二事瀚之子楷说。】

    　　○黄长子

    　　长洲十四都小民黄长子者，患膈气，不能饮食，亦不知饥，积数年益甚。一日，入齐门访医，行至吊桥少憇。有道人亦来坐桥上。民因惫呕吐狼藉，道人怜之，问所苦，具言疾状，道人曰：「我能医尔疾。」倾葫芦中红药一丸，如大芥子，令吞之。少顷，民觉胸膈甚快，分所携器中数饼为谢，道人受之。因以手抚其背，复吐前药，仍纳葫芦中，循桥侧而去。民至医家觉饥甚，索食，视器中则其饼故在，大异之。自此宿疾顿平。意道人为仙，不然亦一奇术士也。 【 顾秀才桧说。】

    Explanation

    Translation

    Blue Tiger

    Liu Han, the younger brother of Liu Hao, had never eaten vegetarian food in his life. One night, he dreamed of a tiger with deep blue fur that came to chase him. It bit him on the waist, causing him pain, and he woke up drenched in sweat. By morning, he saw five tooth marks on his waist, which were blue and swollen, and had bled, forming a wound. He then observed vegetarianism and performed rituals for three years, and his condition improved. [The above two stories are told by Liu Han's son Kai.]

    Yellow Longzi

    A small person from the fourteenth district of Changzhou named Huang Changzi suffered from a disease of the diaphragm. He could not eat or drink and did not feel hungry, and the condition worsened over several years. One day, he went to the Qi Gate to seek a doctor. On his way, he rested briefly at a suspension bridge. A hermit also came and sat on the bridge. The man, exhausted, vomited messily. The hermit pitied him and asked about his illness. The man described his condition, and the hermit said, "I can cure your illness." He poured a red pill from a gourd, as large as a mustard seed, and ordered the man to swallow it. A short while later, the man felt his chest and diaphragm very comfortable. He divided several cakes from the container he carried to thank the hermit, who accepted them. The hermit then patted the man's back, causing him to vomit the medicine again, which the hermit put back into the gourd and went away along the side of the bridge. When the man reached the doctor's house, he felt very hungry and asked for food. He looked into the container and saw that the cakes were still there, greatly surprised. From then on, his chronic illness suddenly improved. He thought the hermit was a deity, or at least a remarkable sorcerer. [The above story is told by the scholar Gu.]

    　　○鸡精

    ○雄鸡卵

    In the city of Jiading, a commoner named Chen Chang's rooster laid an egg, as large as a sparrow's egg. Chen Chang considered it very ominous, but there was no further incident.

    ○沈镗

    Shen Tang, a person from Jiangdong, during his final illness, a person emerged from behind his buttocks, about an inch long, with both eyes, hands, feet, and limbs fully formed. A few days later, Shen Tang died.

    ○鸡精

    Chen Yuan Shan, a resident of Suzhou's Loumen district, was a person of broad-minded character and had a particular interest in Daoist practices. He often engaged in rituals such as summoning spirits and was known by his Daoist name, Dongzhen. He frequently traveled to Jiading, where he was well-acquainted with the children of prominent families.

    Once, Chen Yuan Shan stayed at the home of the Tan family. They had a rooster that had lived for eighteen years. While talking with the host, the rooster flew from the courtyard to in front of Chen Yuan Shan, spread its wings and stretched its neck, and then died on the ground.

    One night, Chen Yuan Shan was staying in the study when a woman knocked on the door, smiled, and entered. She claimed to be the host's daughter and admired his broad-mindedness, so she came to be with him. Chen Yuan Shan saw that she was exquisitely beautiful. When he asked her age, she replied, "Eighteen years old." He then kept her with him for intimacy.

    From then on, the woman came to him every morning and left in the evening, and this continued for nearly a year. She occasionally mentioned that her life was associated with the rooster. Whenever she came, Chen Yuan Shan felt drowsy and dreamlike, but felt refreshed upon her departure.

    He told the Tan family about this, and the host was shocked and said, "My family has no such daughter, nor does any neighboring household. This must be a spirit or ghost."

    且彼云年十八而属鸡，以今岁计之，生肖不合，独吾家所畜鸡，其年正如此数，将无是乎？」陈用其技，书符咒水，欲以辟之，女来如故。或密藏符于怀袖间，女辄知之，怒曰：「尔乃疑我！」以手挟而反复扑之，俟符坠地，则夺去。或教其以周易一册置裹肚中，女至，扑之再三，终不坠，乃舍去。一夕，与数友同宿王槚所，相戒无睡，以觇其来。夜中，众闻元善叱骂声，起视，见其身凭于床 【 见其身凭于床　原本作「见其身凭于床」，据说库本改。】 ，类交合之状，已而遗精在席上。元善如梦觉，众大噪逐之，见帐顶一黑团作鸡声，飞出窓外。乃相与延术士结坛，召将吏遣之。女见元善谢曰：「无逐我，我数日将往无锡托生矣。汝送我不可至井亭，惧为井神所收，当送我于野地耳。」如其言，以符水、祭物送城外数里荒僻处，自是遂绝。

    Moreover, he said that she is eighteen years old and belongs to the Year of the Rooster. Someone secretly hid the talisman in their sleeves, and the woman always knew about it. She became angry and said, "You are doubting me!" She grabbed it with her hand and repeatedly hit it.     ○如公

    　　嘉定僧如公者，尝昼假寐，梦至苏城枫桥北里许，渡板桥入一家，瓦屋三间，饮馔满案，己据中坐。 【 己据中坐　原本作「已据中坐」，据说库本改。】 有妇人前立，年可四十许，展拜垂泣，少者数人侍立于后。有顷进馄饨，妇人取案上纸钱焚之地。及醒，乃觉饱且喉中有馄饨气，怪之。后以事至枫桥，顺途访之。到一处宛如梦中所见，入门，几案陈设皆梦中也。有少年出迎之，扣其家事，云：「父死矣。」其死忌之日，正僧得梦日也，乃知是时其家设祭耳。 【 右四事姨兄徐来凤说 【 姨兄　原本作「姨见」，误。】 。】

    A Monk Named Ru Gong

    A monk from Jia Ding named Ru Gong once took a nap during the day and had a dream in which he arrived at a place about a mile north of Suzhou's Fengqiao Bridge. He crossed a wooden bridge and entered a house. The house had three tiled rooms, and the table was filled with food and drink. He sat in the middle seat. In front of him stood a woman, about forty years old, who bowed and wept. A few young people stood behind her. After a while, dumplings were brought in, and the woman took some paper money from the table and burned it on the ground. When he woke up, he felt full and had the smell of dumplings in his throat, finding it strange. Later, when he went to Fengqiao for business, he visited the place along the way. Upon arriving, he found that it was just as he had seen in his dream. Entering the house, the tables and chairs were arranged exactly as in his dream. A young man came out to greet him. When he inquired about the family matters, the young man said, "The father has died." The day of the father's death was the same day the monk had his dream. Thus, he realized that it was the time when the family was holding a memorial service. [The above four stories were told by my aunt's brother Xu Laifeng.]

    77

    ○戴妇见死儿

    　　长洲陆墓人戴客，以鬻瓦器为业，颇足衣食，止生一子，极爱之，衣裘饮博，恣其所需。子年十六，得疾，卧床褥者半年，医药祷祠，百方不效，子竟死。夫妇痛惜，厚加殓葬，诵经建醮，费又不赀，家具为之一空，犹念其子不已，终日哭泣。一日，有妪拏舟舣岸，欵门而入，不忍其夫妇之悲哽，因进曰：「死生常理，何悲如此。然翁姥爱深难割，今念令嗣者，亦欲一见之否耶？」夫妇掩涕谢曰：「长逝之人，永沉冥漠，幽明隔越，安有见期？如妪之言，非所敢望也。」妪曰：「若然，亦易事耳。」惊喜扣其说，妪曰：「吾将引到一处，即当见之。然翁姥不须俱行，以一人往可也。」戴喜，即令其妻偕入舟，妪戒不得妄窥。

    77

    The Wife of Dai Sees the Dead Child

    A man named Dai, a traveler from the village of Lu Mu in Changzhou, made a living by selling pottery. He was well-off enough to support himself and his family, but he only had one son, whom he loved deeply. He indulged the boy with fine clothing and lavish feasts, fulfilling all his desires. When the son was sixteen, he fell ill and lay bedridden for half a year. Despite medical treatments and prayers, all efforts to cure him were in vain, and the boy eventually died. The parents were heartbroken and lavishly buried their son, reciting scriptures and holding rituals. The expenses were enormous, depleting all their household belongings. They still thought of their son incessantly and cried all day long. One day, an old woman arrived by boat, tied it to the shore, and knocked on the door. Unable to bear the couple's sorrow, she said, "Life and death are natural laws; why grieve so much? However, your deep love for your son is hard to part with. If you think of your son, would you also want to see him again?" The couple, tears streaming down their faces, replied, "The departed person is forever lost in the darkness, and the boundary between the living and the dead is vast. How can there be a time to see him again? As you say, it is not what we dare to hope for." The old woman said, "If so, it is an easy matter." Surprised, the couple asked about her words. The old woman said, "I will lead you to a place where you will see him. You do not need to both go; one person can go." Dai was happy and immediately sent his wife to go with him. The old woman warned not to look around casually.

    78

    鼓棹如飞，食顷到一处，市廛中居民稠密，妪导以登，遥见其子立米铺中，方持槩为人量米。望见母来，即趋出拜母，喜可知也。子言：「见今为此家开铺，正念母，欲一见。母姑留此，吾入报主家，令相迎也。」即奔入，妪招母入舟，以箬蓬密覆，漾舟中流，使潜窥之。其子少选便出，装饰大畏，俨一牛头野叉也 【 俨一牛头夜叉也　原本「夜叉」作「夜乂」，据说库本改。】 ，四顾骂曰：「老畜安在？渠少我债二十年，尚欠四年未满，今来，我正欲报人执之，恨少迟，令得走却。」含怒而入 【 含怒而入　原本作「抝而入」，据说库本改。】 。母伏舟中不敢喘，妪谓曰：「已见之乎？」放舟复还故处，述所见于其夫，自是悲念始息。寻妪舟亦不复见矣。 【 温陵说。】

    Explanation

    78

    Rowing like the wind, they arrived in a short while at a bustling market where the residents were densely packed. The old woman guided her to climb up, and she saw her son standing in a rice shop, just using a measure to weigh rice for others. Seeing his mother come, he immediately rushed out to greet her, clearly very happy. The son said, "I am currently running this family's shop. I have been thinking of you and wanted to see you. Please stay here, mother. I will go inform the master of the house to come and greet you." He immediately rushed in, and the old woman invited the mother into the boat, covering it with a thick layer of bamboo matting. They drifted the boat in the middle of the stream, allowing the mother to secretly observe. Soon, the son came out, dressed in a frightening manner, looking like a fearsome bull-headed demon. He looked around and shouted, "Where is the old beast? He owes me a debt of twenty years, still owes me four years. Now that he's here, I'm just about to have someone arrest him. I regret not acting sooner, letting him escape." Entering with anger, the mother crouched in the boat, too afraid to breathe. The old woman asked, "Have you seen him?" They released the boat and returned to their original spot, where the mother described what she saw to her husband. From then on, her sorrow and longing subsided. Soon, the old woman's boat was also nowhere to be found. [This is the story from Wenling.]

    79

    ○玄坛黑虎

    　　吴俗喜鬬蟋蟀，多以决赌财物。予里人张廷芳者好此戏，为之辄败，至鬻家具以偿焉，岁岁复然，遂荡其产。素敬事玄坛神，乃以诚祷，诉其困苦。夜梦神曰：「尔勿忧，吾遣黑虎助尔。今化身在天妃宫东南角树下，汝往取之。」张往，掘土获一蟋蟀，深黑色而甚大。用以鬬，无弗胜者，旬日间获利如所丧者加倍。至冬，促织死，张痛哭，以银作棺葬之。

    Explanation

    79

    The Black Tiger of the Dark Altar

    In the Wu region, there is a custom of enjoying cricket fighting, often deciding to gamble on property. A man named Zhang Tingfang from my village was fond of this pastime, but always lost, to the point of selling his furniture to repay his debts. This happened year after year, and he eventually squandered all his possessions. He had always respectfully served the dark altar god, so he prayed sincerely, recounting his hardships. That night, he dreamed that the god said to him, "Do not worry; I will send a black tiger to help you. It has now transformed into a form under the tree at the southeast corner of the Tianfei Palace. Go and retrieve it." Zhang went there, dug the soil, and obtained a cricket that was very dark and very large. Using it to fight, he never lost, and within ten days, he gained profits double what he had lost. By winter, the cricket died, and Zhang cried bitterly, making a silver coffin to bury it.

    80

    ○钱蛇

    　　酆都熊存为予弟子远说：其乡一村落中，有蛇出为患，不知所从来，其大如盌，长数丈，惟以啮鸡雏、窃饮食而不伤人。人求而杀之，不可得。村中僧寺有隙地，一人赁而艺为圃有年矣。一旦，执锄耘草，见巨蛇蜿蜒而至，亟运锄斫之，蛇钻入穴中，仅伤其尾，而铿然如击铜铁声，就视之，乃散钱数千布穴口 【 乃散钱数千布穴口　原本「穴口」作「穴中」，据说库本改。】 。其人疑蛇为钱所化也，呼妻及弟并力掘之，深丈许，得钱一缸，约数十万，悉担归于家，顿成富人。蛇自是不复见矣。

    　　说妖
    　　芭蕉女子
    　　巨蚌

    Explanation

    ○Money Snake

    Fengdu's Xiong Cun, my disciple far away, told me: In his village, there was a snake that appeared as a pest, no one knew where it came from, it was as big as a bowl, several zhang long, only biting young chickens and stealing food without harming people. People sought to kill it but could not. There was a vacant plot of land in a village temple, one person rented and cultivated it as a garden for many years. One day, while wielding a hoe to weed, he saw a huge snake winding its way, quickly swung the hoe to chop at it, the snake burrowed into a hole, only injuring its tail, and made a clanging sound like striking metal. Looking closely, there were thousands of scattered coins at the entrance of the hole. The person suspected that the snake had been transformed into money, called his wife and brother to dig together, about one zhang deep, found a vat of money, about several tens of thousands, carried it all back home, suddenly became a wealthy person. Since then, it was never seen again.

    　　○说妖

    　　吴俗所奉妖神，号曰五圣，又曰五显灵公，乡村中呼为五郎神，盖深山老魅、山萧木客之类也。 【 夷坚志云：一名独脚五通。予谓即传所谓「夔一足」者也。他郡所事者曰「萧公」，正取山萧义。】 五魅皆称侯王，其牝称夫人，母称太夫人，又曰太妈。民畏之甚，家家置庙庄严，设五人冠服如王者，夫人为后妃饰。贫者绘像于板事之，曰「圣板」。祭则杂以观音、城隍、土地之神，别祭马下，谓是其从官。每一举则击牲设乐，巫者叹歌，辞皆道神之出处，云神听之则乐，谓之「茶筵」。尤盛者曰「烧纸」 【 尤盛者曰烧纸　说库本作「尤盛者曰烧大纸」。】 。虽士大夫家皆然，小民竭产以从事，至称贷为之。一切事必祷，祷则许茶筵，以祈阴佑，偶获佑则归功于神，祸则自咎不诚，竟死不敢出一言怨讪。
