    　　刘公望气

    　　○铁冠道人

    　　铁冠道人张景和者，江右之方士也。道术甚高，人不能测。太祖皇帝初驻滁阳，道人诣军门谒，言于上曰：「天下淆乱，非命世之主，未易安也，以今观之，其在明公乎！」上问其说，对曰：「明公龙瞳凤目，状貌非常，贵不可言。若神采焕发，如风扫阴翳，即受命之日也。」上奇之，留于幕下，屡从征伐。上与陈氏相持，每令望气以决休咎，言出必验。鄱阳之战，友谅中流矢死，两军皆未知觉。道人望气知之，密奏曰：「友谅死矣，然其下未知，犹为之力战。请为文以祭，使死囚持往哭之，则彼众气夺，而吾事济矣。」上从其言，汉兵遂大溃。后上定鼎金陵，凡诸营建，必令道人相其地，大见信用。

    Explanation

    116

    The Taoist priest with the iron crown, Zhang Jinghe, was a sorcerer from Jiangxi. His Taoist skills were highly advanced, beyond human understanding. When Emperor Taizu of the Ming Dynasty first stationed himself in Chuzhou, the Taoist priest visited the military camp to pay respects and spoke to the emperor, saying: "The world is in chaos, and it is not easy to establish peace without a ruler destined to save the world. From what I see now, it might be in Your Excellency!" The emperor asked him to explain his reasoning, and he replied: "Your Excellency has dragon eyes and phoenix eyes, an extraordinary appearance, and a preciousness too great to describe. If your divine spirit is radiant, like the wind sweeping away clouds, then it is the day of receiving the mandate." The emperor found his words remarkable and kept him in his entourage, frequently accompanying him on military campaigns. When the emperor faced off against Chen Sheng, he often ordered the Taoist priest to observe the atmosphere to predict good or bad omens, and what he said always came true. During the Battle of Poyang Lake, Liu Xiong was hit by an arrow and died, but both armies were unaware. The Taoist priest observed the atmosphere and knew of this, secretly reporting to the emperor: "Liu Xiong is dead, but his subordinates do not know, and they continue to fight fiercely. Please write an eulogy to commemorate him and send a condemned prisoner to go and cry out, then their morale will be broken, and our cause will succeed." The emperor followed his advice, and the Han forces were completely defeated. Afterward, when the emperor established his capital in Nanjing, all construction projects always had the Taoist priest choose the sites, and he was greatly trusted and relied upon.

    117

    尝游鸡鸣山寺，时上以剎宇高瞰大内，欲毁而更置之，犹未言也，道人忽谓寺僧曰：「圣上有意毁汝寺，来日当临幸，汝等于中道遮诉之，庶可免也。」僧素神其术，明旦相率燃香出山数里以候，驾至，僧拜恳不已。上讶曰：「我无此心，若辈何以妄诉？」僧曰：「此铁冠道人教臣等耳。」上异之，遂止不毁。初，徐武宁王为列将时，道人谓之曰：「公两颧赤色，目光如火，官至极品，所惜者仅得中寿耳。」后果以五十四而薨。

    Explanation

    117

    Once, I visited the Jīmíng Temple on the mountain. At that time, the emperor intended to destroy and rebuild the temple because its high vantage point overlooked the imperial palace. He had not yet spoken of this plan when a Taoist monk suddenly said to the temple monk, "The emperor has the intention to destroy your temple. The next day, he will visit in person. You should block him on the way and plead with him; perhaps you can be spared." The monk had always revered the Taoist's magic, so the next morning, they gathered and burned incense, waiting several miles outside the mountain. When the emperor arrived, the monks repeatedly bowed and pleaded. The emperor was surprised and asked, "I had no such intention. Why are you falsely accusing me?" The monks replied, "This is what the Iron Hat Taoist taught us." The emperor was amazed and stopped the plan to destroy the temple.

    Initially, when Xu Wuning, the Duke of Wuning, was a general, the Taoist monk told him, "Your two cheeks are red, and your eyes shine like fire. You will reach the highest rank, but what is regrettable is that you will only attain a middle-aged life." Indeed, he died at the age of fifty-four.

    118

    道人结庐钟山下，梁国公蓝玉携酒访之。道人野服出迎，玉以其轻己，不悦，酒行戏曰：「吾有一语请仙兄属对，云：脚穿芒屦迎宾，足下无礼。」道人指玉所持椰杯复之，曰：「手执椰瓢作盏，尊前不忠。」玉武人，不喻其旨，相与一笑而罢。后玉竟以谋逆伏诛，赤其族。道人居都下数年，一旦，无故自投于大中桥水死。上命求其尸，不获，已而潼关守吏上奏云：「某月日铁冠道人策杖出关。」计之，正其投水之日也。由是讫不复见云。 【 南都儒士毛生说。】

    Explanation

    118

    A Daoist hermit built a cottage at the foot of Zhongshan Mountain. Liangguo Gong Lan Yu brought wine to visit him. The hermit greeted him in his rustic attire. Lan Yu, feeling belittled, was displeased and, during the wine service, playfully said, "I have a word for you to match: 'Wearing straw sandals to welcome guests, Your Feet are impolite.'" The hermit pointed to the coconut shell cup Lan Yu was holding and retorted, "Holding a coconut shell as a cup, In front of the wine, You are disloyal." Lan Yu, a martial man, did not understand the deeper meaning of the hermit's words, and they laughed together before parting. Later, Lan Yu was executed for treason, and his entire family was exterminated. The hermit lived in the capital for several years. One day, without any apparent reason, he jumped into the water at the Dazhong Bridge and drowned. The emperor ordered a search for his body, but it was not found. Soon after, a guard at Tongguan reported, "On a certain day, the Iron-Cap Daoist walked out of the pass with his staff." Calculating the date, it was exactly the day the hermit had jumped into the water. From then on, the hermit was never seen again. [Told by the Confucian scholar Mao Sheng of Nan Du.]

    119

    ○陈子经

    　　四明陈桱子经，尝作通鉴续编，书宋祖陈桥之事曰：「匡胤自立而还。」方属笔之顷，雷忽震其几，子经色不变，因厉声曰：「老天虽击陈桱之臂，亦不改矣。」后三日，子经昼寝，梦为人召去，至一所，门阙壮丽，如王者居。门者奔入告云：「陈先生来矣。」子经进，立庭下。殿上传呼升阶，中坐者冕旒黄袍，面色紫黑，降坐迎之曰：「朕何负于卿，乃比朕于篡耶？」子经具知其宋祖也，谢曰：「死罪，臣诚知以此触忤陛下，然史贵直笔，陛下虽杀我，不可易也。」王者俛首，子经下阶，因惊而寤。洪武中，子经为起居注，坐法死。临刑，上曰：「吾特为宋祖雪愤矣。」 【 此事予旧闻诸先辈 【 此事予旧闻诸先辈　原本阙「予」字，据说库本补。】 ，近见陈永之先生所记云：旧编书奉周主为郑王，子经易「奉」字为「废」，与此不同。】

    Explanation

    119

    Chen Zi Jing

    Chen Jie, a scholar from Sizhou, once compiled the Zongjian Xubian (Chronicle of the Continuation of the Comprehensive Mirror), in which he recorded the events surrounding Emperor Taizu of Song's ascension at Chenqiao, stating: "Kuangyin established himself and returned." While he was in the process of writing, a sudden thunderclap struck his desk. Chen Jie remained calm and, with a stern voice, declared, "Even if Heaven strikes my arm, I will not change." Three days later, Chen Jie fell asleep during the day and dreamed of being summoned by someone to a place with grand and imposing gates, resembling the residence of a king. The gatekeeper rushed in to announce, "Mr. Chen has arrived." Chen Jie entered and stood in the courtyard. The emperor called from the hall, summoning him to ascend the steps. The emperor, seated in the center, wore a crown with jade pendants and a yellow robe, his face dark purple or black. He descended from his seat to greet Chen Jie and said, "What have I done to you? Why do you compare me to a usurper?" Chen Jie realized that the emperor was Emperor Taizu of Song and humbly apologized, "I beg your pardon, I truly know that this offends Your Majesty. However, history values truthful writing. Even if Your Majesty kills me, it cannot be changed." The emperor bowed his head, and Chen Jie descended the steps, waking up in shock. During the reign of the Hongwu Emperor, Chen Jie served as the official recorder of the emperor's daily activities and was executed for a legal offense. At the time of his execution, the emperor said, "I am especially clearing the anger of Emperor Taizu."

    [This story I heard from my predecessors [The original text is missing the character '予' (I), which is said to be added in the library edition]. Recently, I saw it recorded by Mr. Chen Yongzhi, who noted that the old edition referred to the Zhou ruler as the Prince of Zheng, while Chen Jie changed the character '奉' (to honor) to '废' (to depose), which differs from this account.]

    120

    ○罗侍郎

    　　侍郎罗公 【 汝敬】 为人刚直，与杨文贞公同乡郡，偕官于朝，每不满文贞所为，数面斥之，文贞颇不乐。荐令巡抚宁夏，时罗公已年老。至边未几，胡寇大入，方督战，所乘马蹶堕深坑中，不能起，恍惚见红袍者翼而蔽之，寇无所见而去，会有后援得免，遂上章请老而归。

    Explanation

    120

    Luo the Minister

    Minister Luo Rujing was an upright and bold man. He was from the same hometown as Yang Wenzheng and served together in the court. He was often dissatisfied with Yang Wenzheng's actions and repeatedly criticized him face-to-face, which made Yang Wenzheng quite displeased. Yang Wenzheng then recommended Luo Rujing to be the provincial governor of Ningxia, although Luo Rujing was already old. Soon after arriving at the border, the nomadic invaders launched a massive attack. Luo Rujing was directing the battle when the horse he was riding stumbled and fell into a deep pit. He could not get up and vaguely saw a person in red robes shielding him. The invaders saw nothing and left. There was a rear guard that arrived and saved him. Luo Rujing then submitted a petition requesting retirement and returned home.

    121

    ○沈知刚

    　　长洲沈知刚，少从父宦游。一夕，灯下俯几读书，忽有人携其灯疾行而去。知刚惊起逐之，身纔离榻，所坐处壁一堵，拉然而崩，为之眙。视其灯，故在对壁案上，门户皆扃锁，而其人已失矣。盖神物所为云。 【 赵元璧说。】

    　　○关公

    　　长洲顾举人 【 兰】 ，往年会试京师，舍于逆旅，得寒疾甚重。自念去家数千里，羁旅寒困，而病势若此，殊以为忧。见卧旁挂关公像一幅，乃于枕上默祷其庇佑，朦胧间见神来呼之，视其貌彷佛所画者，语之曰：「君无忧，至晚且出汗，即能起矣。」言毕倐然去。及暮，果汗而愈，后归画其像事之。

    Explanation

    121

    沈知刚

    Shen Zhigang of Changzhou, when young, followed his father on official travels. One night, while reading by the light of his lamp, he suddenly saw someone take the lamp and walk quickly away. Shen Zhigang was startled and chased after him. As soon as his body left the bed, the wall where he had been sitting suddenly collapsed, leaving him astonished. He looked at the lamp and saw it still on the desk on the opposite wall, with all doors and windows locked, and the person had disappeared. It must have been done by a divine being. [According to Zhao Yuanbi.]

    关公

    Contribute Lan of Changzhou, a candidate for the imperial examination in the capital many years ago, stayed at an inn and fell seriously ill with a cold. He felt far from home, lonely, and distressed, and his illness was severe, causing him great concern. Seeing a portrait of Guan Yu hanging beside his bed, he silently prayed for his protection. In a daze, he saw Guan Yu come and call him. The figure looked like the one in the painting. Guan Yu told him, "Do not worry; by evening, you will sweat and recover." After speaking, Guan Yu suddenly disappeared. By evening, he indeed sweated and recovered. Later, he drew a picture of the image and worshipped it.

    122

    ○僧时蔚

    　　吴西山圣恩寺僧时蔚，号万峯，温州乐清金氏子，元末名僧长千严高弟也。初学成，请于师出游，师谓曰：「汝逢汝名即住。」至苏，止于邓尉山东麓，曰：「玄墓建大蓝若。」初未尝识字，既超悟禅乘，遂能作书，偈语皆可诵。虽僧服而不去须发，自为赞，有「束发辨头陀，留须表丈夫」之句。洪武辛酉，朝廷闻其名，使征之。使未至之七日，蔚已前知，谓其徒无念曰：「吾与之无缘，汝当应召，吾今去矣。」遂沐浴入湼盘，遗命毋焚尸，越十三日肢体犹温，以瓦缸覆尸而葬。无念入觐，大被宠锡，后住湖广之九峯寺，与蔚埒望焉。

    Explanation

    122

    Monk Wanfeng (僧时蔚)

    Monk Wanfeng of the Shengen Temple in the West Mountain of Wu, also known as Wanfeng, was a son of the Jin family from Yandu, Wenzhou. He was a renowned disciple of the famous monk Changqian Yan during the late Yuan dynasty. After completing his initial studies, he asked his master for permission to travel. The master told him, "When you encounter your name, you should stop." Upon reaching Suzhou, he stopped at the eastern foot of the Dingsui Mountain and said, "Build a large temple at Xuanmu." Initially, he did not know how to read or write, but after achieving a profound insight into Chan Buddhism, he became able to write and compose verses that could be recited. Although he wore monastic robes, he kept his beard and hair, writing a self-praise that included the lines, "Binding my hair to distinguish myself as a monk, keeping a beard to show my manhood." In the 17th year of the Hongwu era (1381), the imperial court heard of his fame and sent an envoy to summon him. Seven days before the envoy arrived, Wanfeng had already foreseen this and told his disciple Wunian, "I have no karmic connection with them; you should go in response to the summons, I will leave now." He then bathed and entered Nirvana, leaving a final instruction not to cremate his body. Thirteen days later, his body was still warm, and he was buried in a clay jar. Wunian went to the imperial court and received great favor and rewards. Later, he resided at the Jiufeng Temple in Huguang, where he was equally esteemed alongside Wanfeng.

    123

    蔚素精堪舆家学，尝言玄墓形势为三龙三凤，胜绝天下，卜葬者多扣之，蔚未尝轻答也。老患痰气，语其徒曰：「吾当服城中沈以潜药，吾与之有缘也。彼在京师，今夕且归矣，宜往速之。」徒如教，至沈氏，则以潜初未归也。返命，仍遣之往，及夜，因寝其家门下待之。二皷，以潜果归，闻之异焉，即往治，疾即瘥。蔚谓曰：「荷君治疾，无以为报，有地于此，请奉以为尊夫人寿域。」因指示竺山后一穴，稍下六尺，云：「是虽微劣，至六十年后，家当大发。」后以潜竟用以葬其母。至成化间，以潜诸孙廛等，皆以富甲其里，布政、杰谕、德焘相继取科第，门户赫奕，距葬时恰及六十年矣。予闻诸以潜末孙注者如此，然「留须」云云，实石室僧语，意蔚非蹈袭，殆是偶合耳。

    Explanation

    123

    Wèi was always skilled in the art of feng shui and often spoke of the terrain of Xuanmu as resembling three dragons and three phoenixes, surpassing all others in the world. Many people consulted him for burial matters, but he never answered lightly. When he grew old and suffered from phlegm and qi issues, he told his disciples, "I should take the medicine of Shen Yiqian from the city; I have a karmic connection with him. He is in the capital and will return tonight; you should go and hurry him." The disciples followed his instructions and went to Shen Yiqian's residence, but he had not yet returned. They reported back, and Wèi sent them again. By night, they slept at the gate of Shen Yiqian's home, waiting for him. At the second drumbeat, Shen Yiqian indeed returned, and Wèi was surprised to hear this. He immediately went to treat Wèi, and his illness improved instantly. Wèi said, "I am grateful for your treatment of my illness, but I have nothing to offer in return. There is a plot of land here; I would like to offer it as a burial site for your respected wife." He then pointed to a site behind Zutu Mountain, slightly lowered by six feet, and said, "Although this site is modest, in sixty years, your family will flourish." Later, Shen Yiqian used it to bury his mother. By the time of the Chenghua period, Shen Yiqian's great-grandsons, Chen, etc., all became the wealthiest in their village, and Bu Zheng, Jie Yu, and De Tao successively passed the imperial examinations. Their family became prominent, and it was exactly sixty years since the burial. I heard this from Shen Yiqian's great-great-grandson, Zhu. However, the words about keeping a beard were actually spoken by a monk from the Stone Room. It seems Wèi did not plagiarize; it was probably a coincidence.

    124

    ○浦应祥

    　　吴人浦应祥，成化丁酉领乡荐，老于礼闱，凡三十有八年，至正德甲戌始就选，得同知高州府。自言初领荐时，尝梦乘肩舆行，而其前有一僧舁之，后数梦皆然。迨得官，自京师挈一僧归吴，道上值险，或涉行潦，輙令扶舆而过。数日，始恍然忆往时所梦僧，正此也。此一小事，兆于三十余年前，人生得丧，岂偶然哉。

    　　○范汝舆

    　　范汝舆，文正公之裔孙也。为府学生，秋试失利还，道经一神祠，乞灵焉。夜即祠下宿，但梦其友婿秦锐盛服坐堂中而已，不解所谓。次举遂捷。故事：举子得解，州府例送捷报牌，其前着举子名第，自府官以下皆列衔具名姓。汝舆第后，偶散步于堂，见楣间所钉牌，中一行曰：「同知秦锐。」乃悟前梦，为之惊叹。

    Explanation

    124

    Final Translation

    Pú Yìngxiáng

    A man from Wuxi named Pú Yìngxiáng, during the Dingyou year of the Chenghua era, was recommended for the provincial examination. He spent thirty-eight years in the metropolitan examination hall without success. It was not until the Jiayou year of the Zhengde era that he was finally selected, obtaining the position of Deputy Governor of Gaozhou Prefecture. He once mentioned that when he was first recommended, he had a dream of riding in a sedan chair, with a monk carrying him in front. This dream repeated several times. After he obtained his official position, he brought a monk back from the capital to Wuxi. On the road, whenever they encountered danger or waded through muddy water, he would always order the monk to carry the sedan chair over. After a few days, he suddenly remembered the monk he had dreamed about before—it was this very monk. This small incident, which predicted his success three decades earlier, shows that the gains and losses of life are not by chance.

    Fàn Rǔyú

    Fàn Rǔyú is a descendant of Fàn Zhòngyǎn, who was posthumously honored as Wénzhèng Gōng. As a student at the local government school, he failed the provincial examination and returned home. On his way, he passed by a temple and prayed for good fortune. That night, he stayed at the temple and dreamed of his friend's son-in-law, Qín Ruì, dressed in fine attire sitting in the main hall. He did not understand the meaning of the dream. On his next attempt, he passed the examination. According to custom, when a candidate passes the provincial examination, the prefecture sends a standard announcement board. The board lists the names and ranks of the successful candidates, starting from the prefectural officials down to the individual names. After Fàn Rǔyú passed, he happened to walk around the hall and saw a board nailed to the door frame. One line on the board read: "Deputy Governor Qín Ruì." He then realized the meaning of his previous dream and was amazed.

    125

    ○产异 【 产异　说库本作「一产五男」。】

    　　丙子秋冬间 【 丙子秋冬间　原本「丙子」作「今年」，据说库本改。】 ，常之武进人张麻妻，一乳五男。数岁前，长洲二都十五图人吴奇妻，一乳四男，皆不育。姨夫徐文甫尝见人担二儿，其腹皮相粘不可劈，状若交合者，云亦出胎时死。

    　　○黄提学

    　　前南畿提学御史黄先生 【 如金】 ，莆田人，弘治甲子举福建乡试第一。前此有邻县儒学一斋仆，祈梦于九仙，欲知是科解首所在，得报云：「乌一黄二，水桶门里，借问黄如金便是。」思本学诸生无此姓名者，必他邑人也，乃之莆田访焉。侵晨，顺途而至一所，有两人立于门。仆揖之曰：「此有黄如金秀才家乎？」曰：「此即是也。」问两人姓名，曰乌一、黄二，皆黄氏仆也。窥门中，则有水桶在焉，遂以梦告。已而先生果占首选。 【 莆田商说。】

    Explanation

    125

    Translation

    Strange Births

    【Strange Births: The library edition reads "one birth of five sons."】

    In the autumn and winter of the year 1526, Zhang Ma's wife from Wujin bore five sons in a single birth. Several years earlier, Wu Qi's wife from Changzhou bore four sons in a single birth, all of whom did not survive. Xu Wenfu, the husband of her aunt, once saw two children being carried, whose bodies were so closely joined that their skin could not be separated, appearing as if they were united in a sexual union. It was said that they had died at birth.

    Mr. Huang, the Censor of Education

    Mr. Huang Rujin, the former censor of education in the southern region, was from Putian. In the year 1494, he passed the provincial examination in Fujian as the top candidate. Prior to this, a servant of a scholar in a neighboring county had a dream in which he sought guidance from the Nine Immortals to determine who would be the top candidate in this year's examination. He was told, "Wu Yi and Huang Er, inside the bucket door, ask if it is Huang Rujin." Thinking that there was no one named Huang Rujin among the students of his school, he concluded that it must be someone from another county and went to Putian to find him. Early in the morning, he came upon a place along the way where two men stood at the door. The servant greeted them and asked, "Is this the home of Scholar Huang Rujin?" They replied, "This is indeed his home." When asked their names, they said Wu Yi and Huang Er, and they were both servants of the Huang family. Looking inside the door, he saw a water bucket, and then he recounted his dream. Soon after, Mr. Huang was indeed selected as the top candidate. 【According to a merchant from Putian.】

    126

    ○江东签

    　　吾苏江东神行祠，在教场之侧，以百签诗决休咎，甚着灵验。记所知者数事。云：
    　　长洲耆儒赵同鲁，年八十一。有疾，卜签得诗云：「前三三与后三三。」是岁同鲁卒，乃九月九日也。或言两三三为九九，亦正合赵寿数。
    　　县桥居民许氏为里长，当解军至湖广五开%。惮远行，祈欲规免，得诗云：「万里鹏程君有分。」既而解至都司，司门有绰楔，其扁曰：「万里鹏程。」许举首见之，始忆神语。
    　　长洲学生周景良，庸鄙不学。秋试年问科名，得诗云：「巍巍独步向云间。」自谓得隽之兆。及试于提学宪臣，乃被黜为松江府吏，而云间实松古郡名也。
    　　府学生陶麟，累举不第，卜以决进退，得诗云：「到头万事总成空。」以为终无成矣。后应贡初试时，编号得「空」字，遂与贡入太学。正德丁卯始领乡荐，其朱卷号亦「空」字。辛未上礼部亦如之，遂擢进士。

    Explanation

    126

    The Shrine of Eastern Jiangnan

    The Shrine of Eastern Jiangnan is located beside the training ground, where 100 bamboo slips inscribed with poems are used for divination to determine auspicious or inauspicious outcomes. It is very famous for its accuracy. Here are a few recorded incidents:

    • Changzhou Elder Scholar Zhao Tonglu, aged eighty-one, fell ill and drew a slip for divination, receiving a poem that read: "Three three before and three three after." That year, Zhao Tonglu passed away on the ninth day of the ninth month. Some said that two three threes make nine nines, which also coincides with Zhao's age.

    • A resident of Xianqiao named Xu served as a village head and was dispatched to Wukang in Hunan Province for military service. Fearing the long journey, he prayed for an exemption and drew a slip for divination, receiving a poem that read: "A ten-thousand-mile journey is your destiny." Later, when he arrived at the military office, there was a signpost at the gate, inscribed with "A ten-thousand-mile journey." Xu looked up and saw it, recalling the words of the divination.

    • Changzhou student Zhou Jingliang, who was mediocre and unlearned, sought fame in the provincial examination and drew a slip for divination, receiving a poem that read: "Soaring alone toward the clouds." He believed this was a sign of success. However, when he took the examination before the educational censor, he was demoted to a clerk in Songjiang Prefecture, as "clouds" actually refers to the ancient name of Songjiang.

    • Prefectural student Tao Lin failed multiple times in the imperial examinations and drew a slip for divination to decide whether to advance or retreat, receiving a poem that read: "In the end, everything turns out to be nothing." He thought he would never succeed. Later, during the initial test for the imperial examination, he received the number "empty" in the registration and was selected for the imperial university. In the year 1517, he passed the provincial recommendation, and his red scroll number was also "empty." In 1521, when he took the examination at the Ministry of Rites, the same number appeared, and he was promoted to the rank of Jinshi (imperial scholar).

    127

    予师毛先生 【 钦】 ，少时眷一妓，情好甚密。妓谋托终身焉，私以一钗遗之，约以为聘资。先生持归，意颇犹豫，潜往谒祷，得诗云：「忆昔兰房分半钗。」其末云：「到底终须事不谐。」先生读首句，为之惊竦下拜，时钗犹在袖也，于是谢绝之。尝读祠记云：「神，秦人，姓石名固。」

    　　○五足牛

    　　丙子岁 【 丙子岁　原本作「今年」，据说库本改。】 ，有僧自京师携一牛至苏，有五足，一在后胯下，短不及地，其蹄类人手，而五指间有皮连络。僧牵于市乞钱，予亲见之。尝闻正统中，吾乡刘原愽先生上京师，其子宗序见道旁人家畜一牛，五足，其一生于领，蹄反向上。以告先生，先生曰：「牛土属，而蹄尤其贱者，今反居上，得无有小人在上，而生变者乎？」后二岁，为己巳，其言果验。

    Explanation

    127

    My teacher, Mr. Mao, was once deeply attached to a courtesan, and their affection was very close. The courtesan planned to entrust her entire life to him and secretly gave him a hairpin, agreeing to use it as a dowry. My teacher took it home, feeling quite hesitant, and secretly went to pray. He received a poem that said: "Remembering the past, we divided a hairpin in the fragrant room." The last line of the poem read: "In the end, the matter would not come to fruition." Upon reading the first line, my teacher was greatly shocked and prostrated himself in worship. At that time, the hairpin was still in his sleeve, and he then refused her. I once read the temple records, which stated: "The deity, a Qin person, surnamed Shi and named Gu."

    　　○Five-Legged Ox

    　　In the year Bingsi [originally written as "this year," but said to be corrected in the library edition], a monk brought a cow from the capital to Suzhou. The cow had five legs, one of which was under the hindquarters, short and did not reach the ground. Its hoof was like a human hand, with skin connecting the five fingers. The monk led it through the market to beg for money, and I personally saw it. I once heard that during the Zhengtong period, my hometown's Mr. Liu Yuanbo went to the capital, and his son Zong Xu saw a cow kept by a family on the side of the road. The cow had five legs, one of which was born on the neck, with the hoof facing upward. He told the master, who said: "The cow is of the earth element, and the hoof is especially lowly. Now it is on top. Is there not a small person in power, causing change?" Two years later, it was the year Ji Si, and his words proved true.

    128

    ○变鬼

    　　南京华严寺僧月堂者，往年以募缘游食至贵州，闻土人言：此中夷俗，有人能为变鬼法。或男子，或妇人，变形为羊、豕、驴、骡之类，囓人至死，吮其血食之。宣慰土官重法禁之，而终不能绝，戒僧云：「卧时善防之。」僧与数人宿寺中，夜深时，闻羊鸣户外，少顷一羊入室，就睡者身连齅之。僧念之，得非向人所云乎？即运禅杖力击其腰下，一羊踣地，遂复本形，乃一M体妇人也。执而絷之，将以闻官，妇人哀叫不已。天明，倩人往报其家，家人齐来寺中，罗拜求免，出白金三百两为僧赎妇命，僧受之，乃释妇使去。他日，僧出郊，见土官导从布野，方执人生瘗之，问旁观者，云：「捉得变鬼人也。」 【 僧自为。】

    Explanation

    128

    ○ Transformation into a Ghost

    A monk named Yue Tang from Huayan Temple in Nanjing traveled to Guizhou for alms and food in the past. He heard the locals say that in this region, there were customs among the non-Han ethnic groups where some people could transform into ghosts. They could change into animals such as sheep, pigs, donkeys, and mules, and would bite people to death, sucking their blood and eating them. The local officials appointed by the central government imposed strict laws to prohibit this practice, but they could not completely eliminate it. They warned the monk, saying, "Be careful when you sleep." One night, the monk and several others stayed at the temple. When it was late, they heard a sheep bleating outside. Shortly after, a sheep entered the room and approached the sleeping person, sniffing at them. The monk thought to himself, "Is this not what the people said?" He immediately swung his Zen staff and struck it below the waist. The sheep fell to the ground and then returned to its original form, revealing a woman with a deformed body. The monk captured and bound her, intending to report her to the authorities. The woman wailed incessantly. The next morning, the monk asked someone to go report to her family. Her family came together to the temple, prostrated themselves, and begged for mercy, offering 300 taels of silver to the monk to redeem the woman's life. The monk accepted the silver and then released the woman, letting her go. One day, the monk went out to the outskirts and saw the local official's entourage spread across the fields. They were just about to execute a person and bury them. The monk asked the bystanders, who said, "We caught the person who could transform into a ghost." 【Written by the monk himself.】

    129

    ○李智

    　　吴中焚尸人亦大有邪术。有李智者，尤精于此。尝操舟出东朱村，见岸上方焚尸，谓同舟者曰：「吾聊戏之。」使一人偃卧，智戟指默诵，咒已，呼其人起坐，则岸上之尸亦坐，使立，则尸亦立，使抱己首，尸亦抱焚尸者之首，旁观人皆惊怖。焚尸者悟曰：「有人作伎俩，欲败吾事耳。」智在舟中忽变色谓诸人曰：「渠不善，尔辈姑避去，吾有以待之。」即趋抱柁而伏。俄闻有声拉然如霹雳，柁为之寸断。智起而喜曰：「免矣。」问其故，云：「本人亦高手，本是为戏，不期便欲相害。若吾术稍劣于彼，适已碎吾首矣。」尝有人从智学，未尽其术而背去。自于他所焚尸，竟日了不焦灼，悟曰：「吾师所为。」赍钱物往拜谢，及还，火须臾便着。 【 都穗说。】

    Explanation

    129

    李智

    People in Wu who burn corpses also possess great magical arts. Among them, there was a man named Li Zhi, who was particularly skilled in this art. Once, he was rowing a boat out of Dongzhucun and saw a corpse being burned on the shore. He told the people in the boat, "I just want to play a trick on them." He had one person lie down, and Li Zhi pointed with a spear and silently recited a spell. After finishing the spell, he called the person to sit up, and the corpse on the shore also sat up. When he made the person stand, the corpse also stood. When he made the person hold their own head, the corpse also held the head of the person burning it. All the onlookers were terrified. The person burning the corpse realized, "Someone is playing tricks, trying to ruin my business." Li Zhi suddenly changed color and told everyone in the boat, "He is not good at it. You all go away for a moment. I have something to deal with." He quickly grabbed the rudder and crouched down. Suddenly, there was a loud sound like thunder, and the rudder was cut into pieces. Li Zhi stood up and said happily, "I'm saved." When asked why, he explained, "The person is also a master. It was just a play, but unexpectedly, he wanted to harm me. If my skills were slightly inferior to his, he would have already smashed my head." There was once a person who studied from Li Zhi but did not fully master his techniques and left. Later, this person burned a corpse elsewhere and the fire did not burn at all throughout the day. The person realized, "This is what my teacher did." He carried money and gifts to thank Li Zhi. When he returned, the fire immediately started. [According to Dousui.]

    130

    ○海岛马人

    　　数年前，有巨艑自海外漂至崇明，中有七人，巡检以为盗执之。七人云：「吾等广中海商，舟入西洋，为风飘至此耳，非盗也。」送上官验视，檄遣还乡。其人自言：在海中时，尝泊一岛，欲登岸取火。忽有异物四五辈，人形而马头，自岛入水而泅 【 自岛入水而泅　原本「泅」作「因」，据说库本改。】 ，以头置船舷，作吁吁声。诸人中或举刀斫其一首，余悉奔去。吾等度其必呼同类来复，亟解维张帆行。未食顷，有马头者百余辈，立水滨 【 立水滨　原本作「入水滨」，据说库本改。】 ，跳踉欲来擒执，而风利舟驶，莫能及。倘少迟，已落其口矣。

    Explanation

    130

    Several years ago, a large ship drifted from the Western Ocean to Chongming County. There were seven people on board, and the patrol officer arrested them, thinking they were thieves. The seven people said, "We are merchants from Guangdong, our boat entered the Western Ocean and was blown here by the wind, we are not thieves." They were taken to the local official for verification and then sent back to their hometown. One of the people said, "When we were at sea, we once anchored at an island and wanted to go ashore to get firewood. Suddenly, several strange creatures appeared, with human bodies and horse heads. They entered the water from the island and swam, placing their heads against the ship's side and making a whistling sound. One of us cut off one of their heads with a knife, and the rest fled. We thought they would call their kind to attack us, so we quickly untied the mooring ropes and set sail. Within the time it takes to eat a meal, over a hundred creatures with horse heads stood at the water's edge, jumping and leaping, trying to catch us. But the wind was favorable and our boat was fast, and they could not catch us. If we had hesitated even a little, we would have been caught by them."

    131

    ○祝氏牧儿

    　　海盐祝主事家有牧羊儿，年十余，素善饭。一日牵羊归，就午食，庖妇故不与以戏之。牧儿去，泣于田间，一道士过，见之问曰：「汝何哭？」告以无饭。道士出怀中黑丸，大如龙眼，授之曰：「食此自当得饱，勿嚼碎。」儿吞之，觉腹中充然。道人戒曰：「无语人也。」遂去。儿暮归不飡，明日亦不饥，绝谷者五六日。庖妇疑其盗米自食也，白于主人。主人召儿将鞭之，儿畏而吐实，主人异之。

    Explanation

    131

    Zhu's Herdsman

    At Zhu's household in Haiyan, there was a herdsman who was around ten years old and was known for his hearty appetite. One day, he led the sheep back and went for lunch. The cook deliberately withheld his meal as a joke. The herdsman left, crying in the fields. A Taoist passed by, saw him, and asked, "Why are you crying?" The herdsman told him he had no food. The Taoist took out a black pill from his robe, as big as a dragon eye, and gave it to him, saying, "If you eat this, you will feel full, but do not chew it." The boy swallowed it and felt his belly become full. The Taoist warned him, "Do not tell anyone," and then left. The boy returned at dusk without eating and did not feel hungry the next day. He went without food for five or six days. The cook suspected that the boy had stolen rice to eat and reported this to the master. The master summoned the boy and was about to whip him. The boy, out of fear, revealed the truth, and the master found it strange.

    132

    明日使他儿与俱，曰：「若复遇道士，一人力挽其衣，一人归报。」二儿到向地，则道士又至矣，语儿曰：「为何漏言。」谢曰：「畏主责耳。」道士以一手支其颔，一手击其顶间，前黑丸自喉跃出，复藏于怀。儿极力挽留，问此何物，曰：「汝知有所谓交梨火枣者乎？此火枣也。」久之，主人闻报而至，将去数百步，道士双足遽陷入土中，稍近，益下，仅露其首，既而首亦不见，土上都无窍穴。惊顾道士，已在隔岸拱手而灭。自是牧儿复食。吾乡戴区人苏盘，时为祝塾师，亲见其事。 【 刘宗廉说。】

    　　○魂魄

    　　高皇帝尝怒一内使洒扫不如法，命引出斩之。被缚至市，犹衣金团背子绿衫 【 犹衣金团背子绿衫　原本「衣」作「布」，据说库本改。】 。市人观之，遥见内侍前有拱手立者一人，状貌衣冠略无少差，甚疑怪之。既而得旨停刑，方解缚，前立者冉冉而逝。疑此为魂魄云。

    　　○刘公望气

    Explanation

    Final Translation

    The next day, he sent his other son along, saying, "If you meet the Taoist again, one of you should try to hold onto his robe, and one should return to report." The two sons arrived at the place, and the Taoist appeared again. He said to the sons, "Why did you reveal this?" They replied, "We feared being blamed by the master." The Taoist supported the boy's chin with one hand and struck his forehead with the other. A black ball jumped out of his throat and returned to his chest. The boy tried to hold onto it, asking, "What is this?" The Taoist said, "Do you know what is called 'interlocking pears and fire dates'? This is a fire date." After a while, the owner heard the report and came. As he was about to leave several hundred steps away, the Taoist's feet suddenly sank into the ground. As he got closer, it sank deeper, only his head was visible, then his head also disappeared, and there were no holes in the ground. Looking in surprise, the Taoist was already on the other side of the river, bowing his hands and vanishing. From then on, the shepherd boy resumed eating. A person from my hometown, Su Pan, who was a teacher of rituals at that time, personally witnessed the event. [Reported by Liu Zonglian.]

    Soul and Spirit

    Emperor Gao once became angry with an eunuch who did not sweep properly and ordered him to be taken out and executed. The eunuch was bound and led to the market, still wearing a gold-embroidered green robe. The people in the market saw a man standing in front of the eunuch, bowing his hands, who looked exactly like the eunuch in appearance and attire, which was very strange. Later, the emperor received an order to stop the execution, and the eunuch was released. The man who had been standing in front of him slowly disappeared. It was suspected that this was the eunuch's soul or spirit.

    鄱阳之役，两军接战方酣。太祖据胡床坐舟端，指挥将士。诚意伯刘公侍侧，忽变色发谩言，引手挤上入舟。上方愕然，俄一飞炮至，击胡床为寸断，上赖而免。战胜之前一日，上疲极，欲引退，公密奏曰：「姑少须之，明日午时，吾气旺矣。」已而果以翼午克捷。

    　　○星变

    　　弘治末，浮梁戴公 【 珊】 、余姚史公 【 琳】 同长内台。史公素善占候，见荧惑犯执法，以语人曰：「司宪之人，其有忧乎？」是岁十二月，戴公卒。或谓史公曰：「公言验矣。」曰：「未也。」前累疏乞归，未得命，寻感疾。越明年，正德纪元正月，竟终于位。荧惑始退舍。

    Explanation

    133

    The Battle of Poyang was in full swing, with both sides deeply engaged in combat. Emperor Zhu Yuanzhang sat on a folding chair at the front of his boat, giving orders to his troops. Liu Bowen, the Marquis of Sincerity, stood by his side. Suddenly, Liu Bowen's face turned red, and he spoke angrily, pulling the emperor into the boat with one hand. The emperor was startled, and just then, a cannon shot came, destroying the folding chair and saving the emperor.

    The day before the victory, the emperor was extremely tired and wanted to withdraw. Liu Bowen secretly advised him, saying, "Wait a little while. Tomorrow at noon, my energy will be strong." Eventually, there was a victory at noon.

    Celestial Phenomena

    At the end of the Hongzhi era, Dai Gong of Fuliang and Shi Gong of Yuyao both served as heads of the internal court. Shi Gong was skilled in divination and observed that Mars was in an unfavorable position. He told others, "Those in charge of justice will have troubles." In the twelfth month of that year, Dai Gong died. Someone said to Shi Gong, "Your words were accurate." Shi Gong replied, "Not yet." He had repeatedly submitted requests to return home, but they were not granted. Soon after, he became ill. The following year, in the first month of the Zhengde era, he died in office. Mars eventually returned to a favorable position.

    134

    ○张宗茂

    　　吾苏玄妙观道士张宗茂有道行，以符咒着灵验。铁瓶巷陈举人 【 汴】 家，有黄鼠豺数十，逐逐成羣，白昼公出，搏食鸡畜，囓坏衣案。占卜云：「是怪汴将讨宗茂符治之，未暇便说。」一日，宗茂晨起诵经，忽有拱立于前者。视之，人身而首则鼠豺也，拜诉曰：「吾辈与陈举人家有夙寃，欲报之。彼来求师，师无豫吾事。」宗茂叱之，忽不见。即诣陈氏，告以所见，为咒水祓除，书符镇之，怪遂绝。宗茂后年老，无疾坐逝，为近时羽流称首。 【 姨夫陈崇仁说。】

    　　○洞庭鸡犬

    　　丁丑年 【 丁丑年　原本作「今年」，据说库本改。】 ，洞庭山民家有黄犬生双角，长寸余。又一家有母鸡，冠尾忽长，遂化为雄，能引吭高鸣。道官薛明净闻其地一巡检说。

    134

    Zhang Zongmao, a Taoist priest at the Xuanmiao Temple in Suzhou, was renowned for his spiritual cultivation and the efficacy of his talismans and spells. In Iron Bottle Lane lived a scholar named Chen Bian, whose home was plagued by dozens of wild dogs and wolves that gathered in groups, emerging in broad daylight to attack and eat chickens and livestock, and gnaw and damage clothes and furniture. Divination revealed that these creatures were a manifestation of a long-standing grudge against Chen Bian, but the curse was not immediately addressed. One morning, while Zhang Zongmao was reciting scriptures, he suddenly saw a creature standing respectfully in front of him. Upon closer inspection, the creature had a human body but the head of a wolf or wild dog. It knelt and reported, "We have a long-standing grudge against the Chen family and wish to exact revenge. He has come to seek your help, but do not interfere with our business." Zhang Zongmao rebuked the creature, and it disappeared. He then visited Chen Bian's home, told him what he had seen, and performed a ritual to purify the house with talismanic water and wrote a talisman to pacify the creatures, which then ceased their attacks. Zhang Zongmao, who later died peacefully without illness, was highly esteemed among contemporary Taoists. [This account was provided by his mother-in-law, Chen Chongren.]

    In the year of Ding Chou (1657), a household in Mount Dongting had a yellow dog that grew horns, each about an inch long. Another household had a hen whose comb and tail suddenly grew longer, transforming it into a rooster capable of crowing loudly. The Taoist official Xue Mingjing heard this story from a local official responsible for maintaining law and order.

    135

    ○飞鱼

    　　沙湖富人丘氏，家有鱼池，近外港。夏月，大雨，水溢，鲤鱼长数尺者，率诸鱼一一飞出港而去 【 率诸鱼一一飞出港而去　原本「一一」作「一二」，据说库本改。】 。至暮，水渐退，鱼复还，巨鲤仍在前，诸鱼从之，飞掷空中，如羣蝶交舞。尝观范蠡养鱼经，中有鱼能飞去之说，观此信然。若去而复还，则尤异也。 【 徐翁玹说。】

    　　○蜂化促织

    　　相城刘浩性好鬬促织。尝侵晨出楼门 【 尝侵晨出楼门　说库本「楼门」作「娄门」。】 ，见水滨一大蜂，以身就泥中展转数四，起集败荷叶上，心怪之。还过其地，见蜂犹在，身已化为促织，头足犹蜂也。持归养之，经日脱去泥壳，则纯变矣。健而善鬬，所当无不胜者。物类之相感化固然。

    ○ Fly Fish

    In Shahu, the wealthy family of the Qiu clan owned a fish pond near an outer harbor. During the summer, a heavy rain caused the water to overflow, and several-foot-long carp, along with other fish, one by one flew out of the harbor and left. By evening, as the water gradually receded, the fish returned, with the large carp still leading the way, followed by the others, flying and leaping through the air like a flock of butterflies dancing. The author once read the Fanyi Jing by Fan Li, which mentions that fish can fly, and indeed, this phenomenon is true. However, the fact that they go and return is even more extraordinary. [According to Mr. Xu Hongxuan.]

    ○ Bee Transformed into Cricket

    Liu Hao of Xiangcheng had a passion for fighting crickets. One morning, he went out through the Loumen gate and saw a large bee rolling around several times in the mud, then gathering on a withered lotus leaf. He found this strange. When he returned to the same spot later, he saw that the bee was still there, but its body had transformed into a cricket, with its head and legs still resembling a bee. He took it home and raised it. After a few days, it shed its muddy shell and completely transformed. It was strong and good at fighting, and it never lost in any battle. The transformation of one creature into another is indeed a natural phenomenon.

    ○ Human Sickness

    During the reign of the Hongzhi Emperor, a woman in Changshu County gave birth to a child with two heads, who died immediately after birth. People competed to come and see, and some gave her money. The poor man hoped to gain more by keeping the child longer, so he hid it. The wet nurse Zhou, an elderly woman, told me that she once attended a childbirth for someone and saw a child with four heads connected by a single neck, which frightened her so much that she killed it. The elderly woman kept the family name secret and would not reveal it.

    ○ Fox of Gǔtíng

    During the reign of the Hongzhi Emperor, a canal ship from the Hangzhou garrison was returning from the capital to Shandong. It was winter, and the river was frozen, so the ship stopped at Ba Li Bay, which was eight li from Gǔtíng Town, hence its name. One evening, a woman with beautiful and alluring attire stood on the shore and called out to the leader of the soldiers, asking for shelter. She said, "I am a local from this town, on my way to my mother's house. It's getting dark, and I can't make it. If you could let me stay, I won't forget to thank you." The soldier refused, but the woman wouldn't leave. As night deepened, she pleaded more urgently, her words filled with sorrow. The soldier unconsciously replied, "Yes," and let her stay at the camp, her sleeping place separated by only a board. In the middle of the night, the woman cried out in pain, her cries were soft and plaintive. The soldier, moved by her cries, got up and made ginger soup for her to drink. He approached her, and she did not shy away. They became intimate, and the soldier considered it a wonderful encounter. At the fifth watch of the night, it started snowing heavily, and the woman said she would return. She said to the soldier, "My home is not far from here. If you are interested, I will come back tonight." The soldier replied, "That would be great."

    ○真武显应

    　　松江富人丁生者，壮年无子，其妾有姙，丁祷于所事真武之神云：「如生男，长成当亲携上太岳烧香，以谢神贶。」已而果得男。长至六岁，丁与妻妾谋将践誓言，皆以子幼道险，欲更须数载。丁以初心不可违，强欲一行，从两仆，携其子而往。甫至，舍于旅邸，其子忽疹，数日竟死。丁悲恸，怨曰：「吾父子至诚，数千里而来，神不赐福亦已矣，而更使得此祸乎！」又数日，痛稍定，乃登山，留儿柩旅邸，嘱邸翁善守之。越三夕，两仆来诣翁，以主命载其棺而去。诘朝丁至，问棺所在，翁具言仆故。丁讶曰：「两仆从我上山，今尚在后，安得有此？」仆至，翁面质之，亦骇愕，疑翁有他故，矢天自明。

    True Martial Manifestation

    A wealthy man named Ding from Songjiang, in his prime, had no son. His concubine was pregnant, and Ding prayed to the deity Zhenwu whom he served, saying, "If a boy is born, when he grows up, I will personally carry him to Mount Tai to burn incense and thank the divine favor." Soon after, a boy was indeed born. When the boy reached six years old, Ding and his wife and concubines planned to fulfill their vow. They all felt that the child was too young and the journey too dangerous, and they wanted to wait a few more years. However, Ding believed that his initial promise could not be broken, so he insisted on going, accompanied by two servants, and took his son with them. As soon as they arrived, they stayed at an inn. The boy suddenly fell ill and died within a few days. Ding was deeply grieved and complained, "My father and son are sincere, traveling thousands of miles, and even if the god does not bestow blessings, but why should we suffer this misfortune!" After several more days, the pain subsided slightly, and he ascended the mountain, leaving the boy's coffin at the inn and instructing the innkeeper to guard it well. After three nights, the two servants came to see the innkeeper, following the master's command, loaded the coffin, and left. The next morning, Ding arrived and asked where the coffin was. The innkeeper explained the servants' story. Ding exclaimed in surprise, "The two servants followed me up the mountain, they are still behind, how could there be such a thing?" When the servants returned, the innkeeper confronted them face-to-face, and they too were surprised and alarmed, suspecting that the innkeeper had another reason, and swore by heaven to clear their names.

    139

    丁大恸曰：「吾违妻妾之言，强以吾儿来。今既死，又并骸骨而失之，吾归何以见家人也。吾有死而已！」既入舟，日常涕泣不食，奄奄殆至灭性。同归者多加宽慰，使进食。抵松，未至家数里，遣一仆先归报。入门，主母出，盛怒诟其夫曰：「汝唯一子，行数千里，忍令他人挈归，于汝心安乎？」且责仆以不谏其主。仆惊不知所对，乃奔告其主，主大怪之，即舍舟趋至家。妻妾交口出骂，问其故，乃言：「旬日前昏时，有船泊岸，二客携儿入门，言吾辈武当烧香遇，而主为事少羁，付此儿先送回耳。」丁大骇，呼儿出看之，疹瘢犹在面，却道前事，皆不信，请同归者证之，始知其非妄。问儿所以生，懵然不知也。 【 右二事鲁百户说。】

    　　○牛祸

    　　丁丑六月 【 丁丑六月　原本作「今年六月」，据说库本改。】 ，巡抚淮扬等处都御史丛兰，奏所管滁州鲍千户家，母牛生一犊，两头八足，两尾共一背，出胎即死。邸报云。

    Ding expressed great grief, saying, "I went against the words of my wife and concubines, forcing my son to come. Now that he is dead, I have also lost his remains. How can I face my family when I return? I will only die!" After boarding the boat, he wept daily and refused to eat, nearly dying from grief. Those who returned with him often comforted him and made him eat. They arrived at Song, not far from home, and sent a servant back to report. Upon entering the house, the mistress of the house came out, angrily scolding her husband, saying, "You have only one son, who traveled thousands of miles, and you allow others to take him back. How can you be at peace with your conscience?" She also blamed the servant for not advising his master. The servant was shocked and did not know what to say, so he ran to tell his master. The master was greatly surprised and immediately left the boat, rushing home. The wife and concubines scolded him together, asking him the reason. He then said, "A few days ago in the evening, a boat docked at the shore, and two guests brought my son inside, saying they met us on a pilgrimage to Wudang Mountain. The master was slightly detained and entrusted this child to be sent back first." Ding was greatly startled, called out to his son to see him, and found the rash and scars still on his face. But when he recounted the previous events, no one believed him. He asked the fellow travelers to confirm it, and they finally realized it was not false. When asked how his son survived, he was completely unaware.

    ○ Cow Disaster

    In the sixth month of Dingchou (which was originally written as "this year's sixth month," but was reportedly changed in the library version), the governor-general of Huai and Yang regions, Cunlan, reported that a cow belonging to Bao Qianguan in Chuzhou gave birth to a calf with two heads, eight legs, and two tails on the same back. The calf died immediately after birth. According to the official gazette.

    ○白乌

    　　大名府元城县一富民，所居庭中甚广阔，植枣树百余本，上有乌巢累数百。弘治甲子，一巢中生白雏，偶坠地，民家收养之。及长，莹洁如雪，循狎可爱。时孝肃皇太后初上仙， 【 时孝肃皇太后初上仙　原本阙「时」字，据说库本补。】 以此为上谅阴纯孝之感也，劝使表献之。朝廷郄不受，还而道死。 【 张参政纲说。】

    　　○楚巫

    　　楚俗好鬼，最多妖巫，变幻不一，人称曰「师公」，敬畏之甚。武冈州有姜聪者尤黠，为城隍庙祝，庙与南渭王府近。王一日脱足缠，为风吹至庙。聪得之，谓其妻曰：「衣食至矣。」杀鸭取其首，裹以足缠，铁钉钉之，置神座下，禁咒之。王登时足痛至废寝食，延羣巫日夜祷祠，终不止。他日，聪托献，亲往问疾，自言能治。一内竖出私财，具牲牢，请聪为王作福，而去其钉足，痛顿瘳，获谢物不赀。

    Translation

    White Crow

    In Yancheng County, Daming Prefecture, there lived a wealthy man whose courtyard was very spacious, with over a hundred jujube trees planted. There were hundreds of nests on these trees. In the year 1494 (Jiazi of the Hongzhi era), a white chick hatched in one of the nests and accidentally fell to the ground. The man's family took it in and raised it. As it grew older, it was as pure and white as snow, gentle and lovable. At the time, Empress Dowager Xiaoshu had recently passed away, and this white crow was seen as a sign of Emperor Jiajing's filial piety during his mourning period. The court was encouraged to present the crow as an offering. However, the court initially refused to accept it, and the crow died on the way back. [According to Zhang Gang, the governor.]

    Shaman from Chu

    The customs of Chu favored the worship of spirits and ghosts, and there were many sorcerers who practiced varied and unpredictable magic. People called these sorcerers "Shigong" (teacher-father) and greatly respected and feared them. In Wugang Prefecture, there was a particularly clever sorcerer named Jiang Cong, who served as a priest at the City God Temple. The temple was close to the Nanwei Prince's mansion. One day, the prince's foot wrap was blown to the temple by the wind. Jiang Cong found it and told his wife, "Our food and clothing are secured." He killed a duck, took its head, wrapped it with the foot wrap, nailed it down, and placed it under the god's seat, performing a spell. The prince immediately experienced severe foot pain that prevented him from sleeping or eating. He invited many sorcerers to pray and make offerings day and night, but the pain did not stop. Later, Jiang Cong claimed to be able to cure the prince and went to inquire about his condition. An eunuch used his own money to prepare sacrifices and invited Jiang Cong to perform a ritual for the prince. Jiang Cong removed the nail from the prince's foot, and the pain immediately disappeared, earning him a large reward.

    141

    又旬余，复依前钉之，王疾如故，又召聪祷而止。自三月至岁且尽，疾时一发，必命聪祷，祷罢辄愈。王心疑之，乃谓聪：「来年将大祭城隍，必厚劳汝。」及是，王故过期不祭，痛辄大作，使人约当以某日祭，则复洒然矣。王烛其奸，召至留之。使校设诱其妻，得三物以献。王亲鞫聪，始犹抵拒，出其物示之，乃具服，狱成，驰驿奏闻，有旨囚妖人送京，至临清毙焉。于时诸巫大抵皆恣横，人家有少酒食，巫经其门，必留享之。或不肯往，便持送其家，不然辄得祸。

    Another ten days later, the ritual was repeated in the same way, but the king's illness remained unchanged. The king then called for Zong to pray, and the illness stopped. From March until nearly the end of the year, the illness would flare up occasionally, and the king would definitely order Zong to pray. After the prayer, the illness would immediately subside. The king began to suspect Zong and told him, "Next year will be a major ceremony for the city god, and I will certainly put you to great effort." However, the king deliberately delayed the ceremony. The pain would suddenly intensify, and he sent someone to arrange a specific date for the ceremony, after which the pain would then suddenly disappear. The king saw through Zong's deceit, summoned him, and detained him. He ordered an officer to set a trap for Zong's wife, who obtained three items to present. The king personally interrogated Zong, who at first resisted. When shown the items, he then fully confessed. The case was concluded, and a fast horse was sent to report to the emperor, who issued an edict ordering the arrest of the witch and sending him to the capital. Zong was killed in Linqing. At that time, most of the witches were generally arrogant and domineering. If a family had a little wine and food, and a witch passed by their door, they would certainly be invited to enjoy it. If they refused to go, the witch would take the food to their home, otherwise, they would suffer misfortune.

    如出而求利，遇巫于道，恳乞一善言，所获必丰，否则多亏败。反唇举目间，皆能为祸福。其党类亦自多疾，互以术相轧。新死卒未能棺殓，则延巫作法，以衣裾承尸气野外散之，经月不秽腐，谓之「寄臭」。来破其法者，径入视，尸臭便作矣。有知者谓：其教中以尸化作一物，如化鲤鱼，置崖间以冰覆之。破法者直用火销却冰，尸自坏臭。唯化作沉香，则诸物莫可害，然火亦能■〈艹执火，上中下〉之。岷王府出丧，柩重不举，益数十夫犹然。呼师公解禳，逡巡即行。

    If one goes out seeking profit, encountering a sorcerer on the road and humbly requesting a good word, one will surely gain much, otherwise suffer great loss. In a moment of anger or a glance, one can bring either good or evil. The group itself is rife with internal strife, and they use their skills to compete against each other. When the newly deceased have not yet been buried, sorcerers are invited to perform rituals, using the hem of clothing to catch the corpse's energy and disperse it in the wild. The corpse remains uncorrupted for months, called 'temporary stench.' Those who come to break the spell, upon entering, the corpse's stench immediately appears. Those who know say: in their teachings, the corpse is transformed into something, like transforming into a carp and placing it on a cliff covered with ice. Those who break the spell simply use fire to melt the ice, and the corpse naturally decays and stinks. Only if transformed into agarwood, nothing can harm it, but fire can still burn it. When the Mian王府 funeral procession began, the coffin was so heavy that even adding dozens more men could not move it. They called upon a shaman to perform rituals, and after a moment, the procession moved forward.

    巫云：「某巫以宿憾，移一山置棺上，适已为扶去矣。」其诡诞可恶如此。自姜聪之败，此辈始为稍稍敛戢云。乡人吴用侍其父教授岷府，数目击其事。时府校有李武者，亦多变幻。用尝试其术，见鹊止屋上，令取之。武默诵咒，鹊旋至其前，徒手得之。武云：「是须邂逅用之则可，若豫畜获禽之念，则终日不能一二也。他物皆类此。」又云：「其术过洞庭湖，则不能大验，亦非乐为是。大抵如闽广所用南法及梓匠厌胜术，以先世传习，故不免为之尔。」吴用者颇善谈怪，后四事并是渠说。

    The witch said, "A certain witch, due to a long-standing grudge, moved a mountain onto a coffin, but it has just been moved away." Such is her deceitful and disgusting nature. After the defeat of Jiang Cong, these types of people began to be somewhat restrained. A local man named Wu Yong served as a teacher in the Min state and often recounted this story. At the time, there was a school official named Li Wu who also performed many transformations. Wu Yong tried his skill and saw a magpie on the roof, commanding it to be fetched. Li Wu silently recited a spell, causing the magpie to fly to him, and then caught it by hand. Li Wu said, "It is necessary to use it by chance; if one has the intention to catch birds beforehand, then one cannot catch even one or two in a day. Other things are all like this." He also said, "His magic does not work well when it crosses Dongting Lake, and he also does not enjoy doing this. It is roughly like the southern methods used in Fujian and Guangdong and the carpentry methods of厌胜术, because it is passed down from previous generations, he cannot help but do it." Wu Yong is quite good at talking about strange things, and the last four events are all his stories.

    ○杨宽

    　　真定之咸宁县学，有斋仆杨宽者，尝因公宴掌酒，见墙角旋风二团，回环不已。宽意旋风中多有鬼神，试沥瓢酒酹之，一风顿息，又酹一瓢亦然。他日宽与同辈四人诣东岳烧香，遇二卒山下，青衣白襕，邀而揖之曰：「我受君惠久矣，未有以报，能同过酒家少饮乎？」宽罔识其人，意必误也，漫应之，同入肆饮罢别去，并不曾询其姓名。同辈问之，宽以不识对，皆笑之。既而登山游观庑下，至一神祠，二塑卒状貌俨如向所见者，相顾大骇。宽自以遇鬼，悒悒不乐。还故处，仍见二卒，谓宽曰：「君毋庸疑我，我非祸君者。颇忆往岁事乎？我二人岳帝座下从者也，奉使贵县，行路饥渴中，得君二瓢之赐，甚惬所愿。昨有事西山，偶获相遇，故以杯酒答谢耳，非有他也。」言讫，瞥然不见。宽归，亲为人说。

    Explanation

    A Tale of Elan

    In the Xianning County School of Zhending, there was a servant named Elan. Once, during an official banquet, he was in charge of serving wine and saw two whirlwinds swirling at the corner of a wall. Elan believed that the whirlwinds contained many spirits and decided to pour some wine from a ladle as an offering. One whirlwind suddenly stopped, and after pouring another ladle of wine, the second whirlwind also ceased.

    One day, Elan and four of his peers went to Mount Tai to burn incense. They encountered two figures at the foot of the mountain, dressed in green and white robes. The figures invited them with a bow and said, "We have been greatly favored by you for a long time and have not yet had the chance to repay you. Would you like to join us for a drink at an inn?" Elan did not recognize them and thought they must be mistaken. He casually agreed and they all went to an inn to drink, then parted ways without inquiring about their names. When his peers asked him about it, Elan replied that he did not know them, and they all laughed.

    Later, they climbed the mountain and visited a shrine. To their astonishment, the statues of two attendants in the shrine looked exactly like the figures they had seen earlier. Elan and his companions were greatly alarmed. Elan felt that he had encountered a ghost and was unhappy. When they returned to their original place, they saw the two figures again. They told Elan, "You need not doubt us; we are not here to harm you. Do you remember the events of the past? We are attendants of the Lord of Mount Tai, on a mission to this prestigious county. In our journey, we were hungry and thirsty, and you gave us two ladles of wine, which greatly satisfied our wishes. Yesterday, we had business in the Western Mountains and coincidentally met you, so we offered you a cup of wine as a token of our gratitude. There is no other reason." After they finished speaking, they suddenly disappeared. Elan returned home and personally told others about the encounter.

    145

    ○方卵猕猴

    　　弘治末，南昌艾公 【 璞】 巡抚江南。苏州属县崇明申报：本县民家有鸡生卵而方者，异而碎之，中有一弥猴，纔大如枣。艾公以告巡江都御史长洲陈公 【 璚】 ，欲同奏于朝。陈公曰：「妖异诚当以闻，然其物怪甚，度已不存矣。万一柄臣喜事者以诏旨进，何以应命？」艾公乃止。吴用见其文移云。

    　　○雀报

    　　镇江卫左所军士范某，妻患瘵疾濒死，遇道人与之药，云：「用雀百头，以药米饲之，至三七日，取其脑服之，当差。然一雀莫减也。」范如数买雀养之，有死者则旋买之以充数。未旬日，范以公差出，妻覩雀叹曰：「以吾一人，残物命至百，甚不仁也。吾宁死，安忍为此。」开笼放之。夫归，怒责其妻，妻亦不悔。已而病差。初，久不产育，是年忽有姙，生一男。男两臂上各有黑瘢，宛如雀形，一飞一俛而啄，羽毛分明，不减刻画。盖冥道以此示放雀报云。

    Explanation

    145

    ○方卵猕猴

    During the late Hongzhi period, Ai Gong from Nanchang served as an imperial commissioner in Jiangnan. In Chongming, a county under Suzhou, there was a report that a household had discovered a square egg, which they found strange and broke. Inside was a creature called a "mihou," only as big as a date. Ai Gong reported this to Chen Gong, the imperial censor from Changzhou, and suggested they both present it to the emperor. Chen Gong replied, "It is indeed necessary to report this strange occurrence, but the creature is very strange, and I suspect it no longer exists. If a powerful minister who likes to take credit for things were to order it presented to the emperor, how could we respond?" Ai Gong then decided not to proceed. Wu Yong saw this document and commented on it.

    ○雀报

    A military officer named Fan from the left company of the Zhenjiang Guard had a wife who was suffering from a wasting disease and was near death. She encountered a Taoist who gave her medicine and said, "Use one hundred sparrows, feed them with medicated rice, and after one hundred days, take their brains and consume them to cure the illness. However, do not reduce the number of sparrows." Fan bought the sparrows as instructed and kept them alive. Whenever any died, he would buy more to keep the count up. After ten days, Fan was sent on a public mission, and his wife, upon seeing the sparrows, sighed, "Because of me, the lives of a hundred creatures have been harmed. How can I bear to do this? I would rather die than continue." She opened the cage and released all the sparrows. When her husband returned, he became angry and scolded her, but she did not regret her actions. Soon after, her illness improved. Initially, she had been unable to bear children for a long time, but that year she unexpectedly became pregnant and gave birth to a son. The boy had black scars on his arms, shaped like sparrows, one flying and one crouching to peck, with feathers that were clearly visible, as if carved. This was apparently a sign from the spirit world, showing her reward for releasing the sparrows.

    ○于梓人

    　　于梓人者，湖广武冈州人。其父尝夜梦梓童神，遂能雕塑神像，极于工致。梓人生七八岁，眉目如画，资性聪警。其州将爱之，因其父艺以梓人名之。 【 湖志作「子仁」，恐误。】 及长，有隽才，且多异术。举洪武乙丑进士，历知登州府。部民有诉其家人伤于虎者，梓人命卒持牒入山捕虎，卒泣不肯行，梓人笞之，更命他两卒曰：「第焚此牒，山中虎即自来。」两卒不得已，入山焚其牒，火方息而虎随至，弭耳帖尾。随行入城，观者如堵。虎至庭下伏不动，梓人厉声叱责，杖之百而舍之，虎复循故道而去。

    Explanation

    146

    A Carpenter Named Yu

    Yu, the carpenter, was from Wugang, a place in the Huguang region. His father once dreamt of the god of carpentry, and as a result, he became skilled in sculpting divine images with great precision. Yu, when he was seven or eight years old, had eyebrows and eyes as beautiful as a painting, and he was naturally intelligent and quick-witted. The prefect of his region admired him and named him "Yu" after his father's skills. [The local records say "Zi Ren," which might be incorrect.] As he grew older, Yu displayed exceptional talent and possessed many unusual abilities. He passed the imperial examination in 1375 during the reign of the Hongwu Emperor and served as the governor of Dengzhou Prefecture. One day, a citizen reported that his family had been injured by a tiger. Yu ordered a soldier to carry a document into the mountains to capture the tiger. The soldier wept and refused to go, so Yu lashed him. He then ordered two other soldiers, saying, "Just burn this document, and the tiger in the mountains will come by itself." The two soldiers, having no choice, went into the mountains and burned the document. As soon as the fire went out, the tiger appeared, with its ears lowered and tail tucked. It followed the soldiers back into the city, where crowds gathered to watch. The tiger lay motionless at the courtyard gate, and Yu sternly scolded it, striking it a hundred times before letting it go. The tiger then returned to its original path and left.

    147

    寻为部民告讦，以为妖术惑众，有诏逮梓人下吏治之，数月瘐死狱中，弃其尸，家人发丧成服。一夜忽闻扣门声，问为谁，答曰：「身是梓人也。」家人惊曰：「鬼也。」曰：「吾实以间逃去，云死者诈也，勿疑。」家人不信，谓鬼衣无缝，验之乃不然，遂内之。梓人不自晦匿，日与故旧游宴。或泛舟不用柁楫，逆水而上以为乐。里人刘氏，其怨家也，执而絷之，白知州伍芳，请奏闻。芳异其事，不许 【 芳异其事　说库本作「芳以异事」。】 。刘遂诣阙告之，朝命法官来州推按，未至，一日忽失梓人所在，但存铁索而已。刘无以自明，竟坐欺罔得重谴，而梓人自是不复见云。梓人自号七十一峯道人，词翰遒逸可观。吴用藏其所制游太山歌一纸，予尝见之。

    Explanation

    147

    Soon after, the local people accused him of using witchcraft to deceive the people, and an imperial decree was issued to arrest the carpenter and bring him to the officials for punishment. After several months, he died of illness in prison, and his body was discarded. His family mourned and wore mourning clothes. One night, they suddenly heard knocking on the door. When they asked who it was, he replied, "I am the carpenter." The family was startled and said, "It's a ghost!" He said, "I actually escaped in the meantime. They said I was dead, but don't doubt it." The family didn't believe him, saying that ghosts' clothes have no seams, but upon checking, it wasn't so. So they let him in. The carpenter did not hide himself and daily socialized with his old friends. Sometimes he would sail a boat without a rudder or oars, going upstream against the current for fun. A local man named Liu, who was his enemy, seized him and tied him up, then reported to the governor Wu Fang, asking for a report to be made to the emperor. Governor Wu Fang found the matter strange and did not allow it. Liu then went to the imperial court to report it. The imperial court sent a judge to the prefecture to investigate, but before the judge arrived, one day the carpenter suddenly disappeared. Only a chain remained. Liu had no way to prove himself and was ultimately punished severely for false accusations. And the carpenter was never seen again. The carpenter called himself the "Seventy-One Peaks Hermit," and his writings were forceful and graceful, worth reading. Wu Yong kept one copy of his poem "Traveling on Mount Tai," and I have seen it before.

    ○老盗

    　　嘉兴金晟，永乐中为刑部主事。时湖广有强盗若干人，械至部。晟鞠之，其渠首年一百二十五岁，面如童子。晟不信，移文验之，果然。问其所以致寿，曰：「少居荆山中，尝遇一人以草炙其脐，云：『令尔多寿。』遂活至此耳。」朝廷以其老，命杖杀之，余皆伏诛。

    Explanation

    The Old Thief

    During the Yongle period, Jin Sheng of Jiaxing served as a middle-ranking official in the Ministry of Punishment. At that time, several bandits from Huguang were brought to the ministry in chains. Sheng interrogated them, and their leader was found to be 125 years old, with a face like that of a child. Sheng did not believe this, so he sent a document to verify it, and indeed it was true. When asked about the reason for his longevity, the leader said, "When I was young, I lived in Jing Mountain, where I once met a person who roasted grass on my navel, saying, 'This will grant you longevity.' Thus, I have lived to this day." The court, considering him old, ordered his execution by beating, and the rest were all punished accordingly.

    　　○异人占星

    　　孝陵在御，多好微行，以察人情之向背。尝以夜出，暂止逆旅，枕石眠草藉上。中夜有两人起共语，上潜听之。一人在庭中，一人在室中。庭中人呼室中人曰：「今夜此翁又出矣。吾视玄象，当在民舍中，头枕石、脚揣藉而卧。」室中人笑曰：「君得无误耶！」上闻而异之，即以首足易位而寝。俄其人亦至庭中，曰：「君果误矣！此翁头枕藉，脚揣石耳。」上听之，不觉汗浃于背，即夕还宫。购求两人不可得，是后微行稍稀。此与汉武帝微行遇书生事相类。

    Explanation

    149

    Chapter 9 of the Gengsi Collection

    Strange People and Star Divination

    The emperor of the Ming dynasty, residing in the Xiaoling Mausoleum, often engaged in secret travels to observe the public sentiment. One night, he ventured out and temporarily stayed at an inn, resting his head on a stone and his feet on a mat. In the middle of the night, two people got up and began to converse. The emperor listened covertly. One person in the courtyard called out to someone in the room: "This old man has come out again tonight. I observed the celestial phenomena and predicted that he would be in a commoner's house, with his head on a stone and his feet on a mat." The person in the room laughed and said, "Could you be mistaken?"

    The emperor was surprised by this and immediately changed his sleeping position, placing his head on the mat and his feet on the stone. Soon after, the person in the courtyard arrived and said, "You were indeed mistaken! This old man has his head on the mat and his feet on the stone." The emperor, upon hearing this, was so frightened that he broke out in a cold sweat and immediately returned to the palace that night. He tried to find the two people but failed. After this incident, his secret travels became less frequent. This event is similar to the story of Emperor Wu of Han, who also encountered a scholar during a secret journey.

    ○金箔张

    　　国初有金箔张者，山西人，自幼多技能。尝以乡人不善金箔，往学于杭，归以授之，用此得名。一日，经河南济源，其神号灵异，人有乞贷帛者，随所须浮出水。张见之曰：「是恶足言神，盖伏机耳。」归即凿池，仿其制为之，已而果然。每客至，翫以为戏。尝遇道人，引之观池，道人曰：「吾亦有小术，君当至吾所观之。」翌日天未明，张见空中两童乘一龙，复控一龙下其家，请张升龙，龙不服，两童鞭之乃得上。须臾至一山，草屋三间，道人坐其中。张再拜请教，道人指庭中曰：「此有丹在，子可取之。」张周视无所见。令再寻之，终无获，道人问曰：「此庭东南角不有物乎？」张对曰：「但见大粪耳。」道人乃叹曰：「子无缘，且当留形住世耳。

    Explanation

    150

    Gold Leaf Zhang

    At the beginning of the dynasty, there was a man named Gold Leaf Zhang, from Shanxi Province. From a young age, he was skilled in many things. Once, because the people in his village were not adept at working with gold leaf, he went to Hangzhou to learn the craft, and upon returning, he taught them, gaining fame for it. One day, while passing through Jiyuan in Henan, he encountered a spirit known for its supernatural powers. People who asked for cloth would see what they needed float out of the water. Zhang saw this and said, "How can this be called a god? It's just a hidden mechanism." Upon returning, he dug a pool and imitated its design, and it worked as expected. Whenever guests came, he would play with it as a game. Once, he met a Taoist priest, who led him to see the pool. The Taoist said, "I also have a small skill. You should come to my place to see it." The next day, before dawn, Zhang saw two children riding a dragon, which then descended to his home. The Taoist asked Zhang to climb the dragon, but the dragon did not obey. The two children whipped it, and Zhang finally climbed on. Soon, they arrived at a mountain with three thatched houses, where the Taoist sat. Zhang bowed twice and asked to be taught. The Taoist pointed to the courtyard and said, "There is elixir here. You can take it." Zhang looked around but saw nothing. He was ordered to search again, but he still found nothing. The Taoist asked, "Isn't there something in the southeast corner of the courtyard?" Zhang replied, "I only saw a large pile of excrement." The Taoist then sighed and said, "You have no karmic connection. You will just have to remain in this form in the world."

    151

    」又曰：「此中甚寂，子欲避名，可移家同住也。」居月余，颇得道人底蕴。一日，偶出散步，少顷回顾，唯空山而已。询之人，乃在大同城外。张归，不以道自名，犹来杭剥金，旦乘驴而至，暮则还家，焂忽数千里。或缚草为龙，跨之而行，归则以挂房檐间。时作戏术以娱人，每适市，人争随求观。孝陵闻之，召至阙下，而责以妖术聚众。张谢曰：「臣非妖术，特戏术耳。」上欲试之，张出袖中小铜瓶，以汤沃之，瓶口出五色云，充满殿庭。上悦，欲尽其术，时正腊月，命开荷花。张请驾至金水河，索干石莲子，乱撒池中，顷刻花开满池，香艳可爱，上亦为唶唶。张索纸剪为一舫，置之水，蹈而登焉，鼓棹放歌，往来花丛中。倐忽转向岸，即失所在，而荷花亦无有矣。亟命四远索之，竟不可得，后莫知其所终。

    151

    The Taoist master said, "This place is very quiet. If you wish to avoid fame, you can move your family to live here together." After living there for more than a month, Zhang gained a deep understanding of the Taoist master's inner essence. One day, he went out for a walk and, after a short while, looked back to find only an empty mountain. He asked someone and learned that he was in the area outside the Great Wall city of Datong. Zhang returned home, not claiming to be a Taoist, but still performing his gold-picking act in Hangzhou. He would ride a donkey to the city in the morning and return home in the evening, instantly traversing thousands of miles. Sometimes, he would tie grass into a dragon and ride it, hanging it on the eaves of his house upon return. He often performed tricks to entertain people, and whenever he visited the market, people would gather to watch. The emperor of the Mausoleum of Taizu heard of him and summoned him to the palace, accusing him of using magic to gather crowds. Zhang replied, "Your servant does not use magic; it is just a trick." The emperor wanted to test him and asked Zhang to produce a small copper bottle from his sleeve. Zhang poured hot water over it, and a five-colored cloud emerged from the bottle's mouth, filling the courtyard. The emperor was pleased and wanted to see all of his tricks. It was then the twelfth month, and the emperor ordered him to make lotus flowers bloom. Zhang asked the emperor to go to the Jinshui River, where he requested dry lotus seeds, scattering them randomly in the pond. In an instant, lotus flowers bloomed across the pond, fragrant, beautiful, and lovable, and the emperor exclaimed in admiration. Zhang then asked for paper and cut it into a boat, placing it in the water. He stepped onto it and boarded, rowing and singing as he wandered among the flower clusters. Suddenly, the boat turned towards the shore, and Zhang immediately disappeared, and the lotus flowers also vanished. The emperor immediately ordered a search in all directions, but ultimately, he could not be found. Later, no one knew his final destination.

    ○盛御医

    　　盛御医 【 寅】 字启东，吴江人。少从隐士王宾学医，永乐中以解户赴京。时上患二肢痹弱，侍医以痿症治之，累年不效。或以寅荐，召至，待命阙下。一内侍微疾，请切脉，辞曰：「未见至尊，安得先及公乎。」内侍服其言，入奏云：「此医人大有分晓。」因道寅语，即传宣入便殿。指上脉叩头曰 【 指上脉叩头曰　原本「叩」作「扣」，据说库本改。】 ：「此风湿也。」上大然之，曰：「吾逐胡出塞，动至经年，为阴寒所侵致此。

    Translation:

    Sheng Yiyi, also known as Yin, with the courtesy name Qidong, was from Wujiang. In his youth, he studied medicine under the reclusive scholar Wang Bin. During the Yongle era, he traveled to the capital as a tax collector. At that time, the emperor suffered from weakness and numbness in his limbs, and the court physicians treated him for a condition called "wasting syndrome," but after many years, there was no improvement. Someone recommended Sheng Yin, who was then summoned and awaited orders at the imperial palace. A eunuch with a minor illness requested that he examine his pulse. Sheng Yin replied, "I have not yet seen the emperor, how can I treat you first?" The eunuch admired his words and reported to the emperor, saying, "This physician has great insight." The emperor then called Sheng Yin to the private hall, where Sheng Yin examined the emperor's pulse and bowed, saying, "This is a case of rheumatism." The emperor agreed, saying, "I pursued the Huns beyond the border, and for many years, I was afflicted by the cold and dampness, which led to this condition."

    吾谓是湿耳，诸医皆误，汝言是也。」药进立效，遂授官。后事仁、宣两朝，皆被眷遇。宣宗尤爱之，尝对御令与同官奕，特赐诗以示宠异。他日，寅晨入御药房，忽头痛昏眩欲绝，羣医束手，莫知何疾。勑募人疗治，有草泽医请见，投药一服，逡巡却愈。上奇之，召问所用何方，对曰：「寅空心入药室，卒中诸药之毒，能和诸药者，甘草也，用是为汤以进耳，非有他术。」上诘寅 【 上诘寅　原本「诘」作「讦」，据说库本改。】 ，果未晨饔而入，乃厚劳其人云。

    　　○奇疾

    　　齐门外临甸寺，有僧年二十余，患蛊疾，五年不瘥而死。僧少而美姿貌，性又淳谨，其师痛惜之，厚加殡，送及荼毘。火方炽，忽爆向一声，僧腹裂，中有一胞，胞破出一人，长数寸，面目肢体眉发无不毕具，美须蔚然垂腹，观者骇异。其师亲为医者陆度说。

    Explanation

    153

    I say it is dampness, all the doctors were wrong, your words are correct. The medicine was administered and immediately effective, and he was then appointed to an office. Later, he served during the reigns of Emperor Renzong and Emperor Xuangzong, and both were favored. Emperor Xuangzong especially loved him, once in the presence of the emperor, he was ordered to play chess with his colleagues, and a special poem was bestowed upon him to show his unique favor. On another day, at dawn, he entered the imperial pharmacy, suddenly suffering from a severe headache and dizziness. All the doctors were at a loss, unable to diagnose the illness. The emperor ordered someone to be sought out for treatment, and a village doctor requested an audience. After administering a dose of medicine, he recovered after a short while. The emperor was surprised, summoned and asked what formula was used. He replied, "At dawn, he entered the pharmacy on an empty stomach, suddenly poisoned by the drugs. The one that can harmonize all drugs is licorice, using this to make a decoction and administer it, there is no other trick." The emperor questioned him, and indeed, he had not eaten breakfast before entering, and then greatly rewarded the person.

    　　○ Odd Disease

    　　At the temple of Lin Dian near the Gate of Qi, there was a monk who was in his twenties and suffered from a disease caused by poisoning. He died after five years without recovery. The monk was young, handsome, and of pure and cautious character. His master deeply regretted his passing and gave him a grand burial, and even burned his remains. As the fire was raging, there was a sudden explosion, and the monk's abdomen split open, revealing a small person inside, about several inches tall, with a complete face, limbs, eyebrows, and hair, and a beautiful beard hanging down to his belly. The onlookers were amazed. His master personally told the physician Lu Du about the incident.

    154

    ○黄村匠人

    　　吴山之西黄村，匠者王某夜归，逢一人，青衣白束腰，如隶卒状。问所之，曰：「欲至黄村。」匠人喜曰：「身亦却归黄村，今相得为伴，甚佳。」便与偕行数里，卒指道旁民家，谓匠曰：「君亦思酒食乎？吾能于彼取之。」匠曰：「善。」卒入门，少选，携一旋酒及一熟鸡来，共坐地上食之。毕，谓匠曰：「君姑留此，我入此家，了少公事也。」匠即取旋纳诸柴积中 【 匠即取旋纳诸柴积中　原本「诸」作「着」，据说库本改。】 ，立伺之。俄见窗里掷出一人，手足束缚，继而卒自窗跃出，负之而去，其行如飞，便闻门内哭声。匠知非人，惊而奔回，明日往验之，乃知其家主翁昨夜死矣。问得无失物乎，乃云：「昨祭五圣，失去一旋酒，一熟鸡。」匠告以夜来所见，不信，探柴积得旋，鸡骨犹满地，始悟其为冥卒也。

    154

    A craftsman from Huangcun village, named Wang, returned home at night. He encountered a person dressed in a blue robe with a white waistband, looking like a servant or soldier. The craftsman asked where he was going, and the person replied, "I want to go to Huangcun village." The craftsman was pleased and said, "I am also returning to Huangcun village; now we have met and can be companions, which is great." They walked together for several miles. The person then pointed to a nearby house and asked the craftsman, "Do you want some food and drink?" The craftsman said, "Yes." The person said, "I can get it from there." In a short while, the person brought a pot of wine and a cooked chicken. They sat together on the ground and ate it. After finishing, the person told the craftsman, "You stay here for a moment; I will go into this house to handle some official business." The craftsman put the pot of wine among the pile of firewood. He stood there waiting. Soon, he saw a person thrown out of the window, with hands and feet bound. Then, the person who had brought the food jumped out of the window, carrying the bound person away. The person moved like the wind, and the craftsman heard crying inside the house. The craftsman realized that the person was not human and ran back in fear. The next day, he went to check and found out that the owner of the house had died the previous night. When he asked if anything was missing, the owner said, "Yesterday, I offered sacrifices to the Five Saints and lost a pot of wine and a cooked chicken." The craftsman told him what he had seen the previous night, but the owner did not believe him. When the craftsman searched through the pile of firewood, he found the pot of wine, and the chicken bones were still scattered on the ground. He then realized that the person was a death messenger from the underworld.

    ○吴恂

    　　乡人吴恂，从其妻之诸母周氏借白金千五百两，而不立契券，实欺之也。既久，遂负不还。周陈于官，为恂行赂不能直而罢。周忿，供城隍神，日祝云：「令彼谋财者红蛆出，白蛆攒。」盖吴俗诅咒语也。已而恂妻得疾，常觉面奇痒，搔之得物如筋，蠕蠕而动，如此日复数四，其色红白不一，而面初无创损也。人以为果报云。 【 右二事子远之氏。】

    　　○北斗经

    　　昆山魏泾清伯，弘治己未病疡，医工误针其足胫，胫肿痛，积久遂不良于行。夜梦白髯老人告曰：「子病若此，亦知诵北斗经乎？」问曰：「诵之何谓？」曰：「不唯愈病，且益寿。」梦觉，意颇不信。诘旦，有道士来问疾，谂之曰：「诵北斗经何功？」曰：「却疾延年。」其言与所梦合，乃悟而持诵，日必三过。久之足瘳，今年及八旬，齿发如少壮，犹日诵经不辍。 【 姊夫姚思慎说。】

    Explanation

    155

    The Townsman Wu Xun

    The townsman Wu Xun borrowed fifteen hundred taels of silver from his wife's maternal aunt, Zhou, without establishing a contract or deed, which was, in fact, a deceit. After a long time, he defaulted on the debt and did not repay it. Zhou reported the matter to the authorities, and on behalf of Wu Xun, bribed officials in an attempt to win the case, but failed to achieve justice. Zhou became angry and offered to the city god, daily praying and saying, "Let those who seek wealth have red worms crawl out and white worms gather around." This was a curse phrase from the Wu region. Subsequently, Wu Xun's wife fell ill, often feeling an unusual itch on her face. When she scratched, she found something like tendons, which moved slowly and wriggled, happening several times a day. The color was not uniform, sometimes red, sometimes white, but her face had no visible wounds. People believed it was a karmic retribution. [The above two stories are from Zi Yuan's family.]

    The Beidou Jing

    During the reign of Emperor Hongzhi in the year Jiwei, Wei Jingqing from Kunshan suffered from a skin disease. A doctor mistakenly pricked his leg, causing it to swell and become painful. After a long time, it became difficult for him to walk. One night, he dreamed of an old man with a white beard who told him, "Your illness is like this, do you know how to recite the Beidou Jing?" Wu Xun asked, "What does reciting it mean?" The old man replied, "It not only cures illness but also prolongs life." After waking from the dream, Wu Xun did not believe it much. The next morning, a Taoist priest came to inquire about his illness. He asked Wu Xun, "What are the benefits of reciting the Beidou Jing?" Wu Xun replied, "It cures illness and prolongs life." The Taoist priest's words matched the dream. Wu Xun then realized and began to recite the Beidou Jing, doing so three times a day. After a long time, his foot healed. This year, he reached eighty years old, and his teeth and hair were like those of a young man. He still recites the scripture daily without stopping. [This is said by my sister's husband, Yao Sichen.]

    ○人瑞

    　　汝宁秀才燕生者，妻一乳三男。吾乡陆锺人杰知光州时，尝以公事适府城，过其家，生呼三男出拜，皆韶秀而形状、衣饰畧无少差。其髻一向左，一向右，一在顶中。生云：「其年皆十二矣，以貌类难别，故剃发为髻以识耳。」他日，生率三子来州谒见，云：「闻此地有一胎三女者，与吾儿同年，欲求为配。」人杰奇之，召见其人，为议而聘焉。

    　　○犬精

    　　弘治中，兖之鱼台县有民家畜一白犬甚驯，其主出行，犬常随之。他日，主商于远方，既去，犬亦不见。经两三日，主辄归，妻问其故，曰：「途中遇盗，财物都尽，幸逃得性命耳。」妻了不疑，周旋阅岁，其真夫归，形状悉同，不可辨。两人各自争真伪，妻及邻里不能明，乃白于县。县令逮两人至，亦无如之何，皆置之狱。县一小卒闻其事，以语其妻，妻曰：「是不难辩，先归者殆犬精也。欲验之，当视其妇胸乳间，有爪伤血纹即是矣。

    人瑞

    Yan Sheng, a scholar from Ruyi, had a wife who gave birth to three sons from one breast. When Lu Zhong Renjie, the governor of Guangzhou, was passing through the county on official business, he stopped by Yan Sheng's home. Yan Sheng called out his three sons to greet him. They were all graceful and handsome, and their appearance and clothing were almost indistinguishable. One had a hair bun on the left side, one on the right side, and one in the middle of his head. Yan Sheng explained, "They are all twelve years old now, and because they look so similar, I had their hair cut into different styles to tell them apart." Later, Yan Sheng brought his three sons to the governor to pay their respects and said, "I heard that there is a woman in this area who gave birth to three daughters at the same time as my sons. I would like to arrange marriages for them." Governor Renjie found this remarkable and arranged a meeting with the woman. He then arranged the marriages.

    犬精

    During the Hongzhi era, a man in Yutai County, Yanzhou, kept a very tame white dog. Whenever the man went out, the dog always accompanied him. One day, the man went to trade in a distant place and left, but the dog disappeared. After a couple of days, the man returned home. His wife asked him what had happened, and he replied, "I met bandits on the road, and they took all my wealth. Fortunately, I managed to escape with my life." His wife did not suspect anything and continued to live with him for a year. Then, his true husband returned, and both men looked exactly the same, making it impossible to tell them apart. The two men argued over who was the real husband, and the wife and neighbors could not determine the truth. They reported the matter to the county magistrate. The magistrate arrested both men and brought them to court, but he had no idea how to proceed and placed both men in jail. A low-ranking soldier heard about the case and told his wife. She said, "It is not difficult to distinguish. The one who returned first is probably the dog spirit. To verify this, you should look at the marks of claw injuries on the breasts of the wife. If there are any, then that is the sign."

    盖犬与人交，常自后以爪按其胸故也。」卒以白令。令召其妇问：「尔家尝有犬乎？」曰：「有白犬，前随夫出矣。」裸而视其胸，有血纹甚多，令知为怪，密使人以血洒其伪夫，即成犬形，立扑杀之。令从容问卒：「汝计善矣，何从得之？」谢曰：「吾妻所教也。」令谕之曰：「汝妻不与犬通，何缘知此？汝归第密察之。」卒归，看妻亦有纹，比此妇尤多，以令语责之。妻穷吐实，乃知亦与一犬通故也。妻惭自缢死。吾乡陈都御史 【 璚】 ，时奉使彼中，得其案牍。 【 周郊说。】

    　　○雷谴道士

    　　玄妙观李道士，早岁颇精于焚修，晚更怠忽。尝上青祠，乘醉戏书「天尊」为「夫尊」，「大帝」为「犬帝」。一日，被雷震死，背上朱书二行可辨，云：「夫尊可恕，犬帝难容。」事在天顺成化间。 【 陈崇仁说。】

    ○曾状元

    　　泰和曾状元 【 彦】 老于举场，成化戊戌，年且六十，乃魁天下。是科，殿试馆阁诸公阅卷竟日，未得超拔之作。最后眉州万公 【 安】 得曾公卷，亟赏叹，以示众，众传观皆钦服，谓文宜第一，特未见其貌。故事：将赐第前一日，集诸举士于礼部阁老堂中，呼名阅其仪观。及是呼至曾公，文康属目，觉其秀伟，尤异于众，喜谓诸公曰：「得人矣。」魁选遂定。迨胪傅出 【 迨胪传出　原本作「迨胪得出」，据说库本改。】 ，则貌寝多髯，与前不类，文康为之愕然。退取其卷读之 【 退取其卷读之　原本「卷」作「策」，据说库本改。】 ，亦平平无奇语，以示诸公，皆然，乃大惊叹，以为有神助云。 【 长州郑长史之子泰说。盖状元尝受业于长史也。】
