    Zeng Ziyuan

    Zeng Ziyuan from Tahe was old in the examination hall. In the year 1478 (Chenghua Wuxu), he was almost sixty years old when he finally became the top scholar in the world. During this examination, the officials in the palace examination hall spent the entire day reading the exam papers but did not find any outstanding works. Finally, Wan An from Meizhou obtained Zeng Ziyuan's paper and quickly praised and admired it, showing it to everyone. Everyone who saw it was impressed and admired, saying that the text should be ranked first, but they had not yet seen his appearance. According to the old custom, the day before the results were announced, all the candidates were gathered in the hall of the cabinet of the Ministry of Rites, where their names were called and their appearance was examined. When Mr. Wen Kang looked at Zeng Ziyuan closely, he found him to be tall and handsome, especially different from others. Happily, he said to the officials, "We have found the right person." When the announcement was made, Zeng Ziyuan had an unattractive appearance with many whiskers, which was different from before. Mr. Wen Kang was surprised. He took Zeng Ziyuan's paper and read it, which was also quite ordinary without any remarkable statements. He showed it to the officials, and they all agreed. Then they greatly admired and exclaimed, thinking that it was helped by a divine force. This story was told by Zhang Tai, the son of a magistrate from Changzhou, because the top scholar had studied under the magistrate before.

    ○腾冲龙

    　　正德某年 【 正德某年　原本阙「某」字，据说库本补。】 ，云南腾冲龙卫地震。其初，日数十度，渐至十余度，后至一二度，凡半年乃止。有一山倾为平地，一村坊居民数十家，皆陷没入土中，余以震压死者不可胜数。民无宁居，皆即空旷处构庐舍以自庇。举人汪城者，家人尽宿后圃，夜半有龙见于圃中八仙桌上，头角尾爪悉具，其色白，若粉所画，扪之鳞甲刺手，但不觉其蠢动耳。居数日，来观者众，汪氏恐为家祸，取狗血涂之，乃灭。 【 长洲丁训导说。】

    Explanation

    159

    ○腾冲龙

    During a certain year of the Zhengde era (the exact year is unknown), an earthquake struck the Dragon Guard in Tengchong, Yunnan. Initially, the ground moved several dozen degrees per day, gradually reducing to several dozen degrees, and later to one or two degrees, lasting for half a year before it ceased. A mountain collapsed into a plain, and dozens of households in a village were all buried underground. The number of people who died from the earthquake was too numerous to count. The people had no safe place to live, so they built temporary shelters in open areas to protect themselves. A scholar named Wang Cheng had all his family members stay in the garden behind the house. At midnight, a dragon appeared on an eight-legged table in the garden, with head, horns, tail, and claws all present. Its color was white, as if painted with powder, and touching its scales felt like they were stinging the hand, but it did not feel like it was moving. After several days, many people came to see it. The Wang family was afraid it would bring disaster to their home, so they took dog blood and smeared it on the dragon, and it disappeared. [Told by a schoolmaster from Changzhou.]

    ○陨石

    　　成化中，星陨于山东莒城县马长史家门中。初堕地，其光煜煜，而星体腐软，特如粉浆。马家人以杖抵之，没杖成穴，久而渐坚，乃作一石。 【 嘉兴焦通判说。】

    　　○尤弘远

    　　乡人尤弘远居东城，其邻庄氏有女奴与相悦，私交信问，愿托终身，后得嫁为远妾。远妻妬悍，日虐之，又为诸厌胜法，咒诅于神，欲使速死。居无何，妾果病卒。又岁余而妻病，久不瘥，厌厌床褥，家人倦于侍，乃呼一里妪使相伴宿。及夜，见一女子红裳绿衫，冉冉行至远妻床前，视之乃其妾也。指妻身谇曰 【 指妻身谇曰　原本阙「谇」字，据说库本补。】 ：「我命未合死，尔多为咒诅，令我夭殁，情理惨虐。我今控诉已得理于岳司，必追汝抵命。明日晚间，令汝腰痛，定去矣！」言讫而灭。妪平日往来尤氏，熟识妾貌，其衣乃殓时所服也。闻语甚恐，不能寐，天明即去。

    160

    Meteorite

    During the Chenghua era, a meteorite fell into the courtyard of Ma Changshi's house in Juzhou County, Shandong Province. When it first hit the ground, it glowed brightly, and the meteorite was rotten and soft, like powdered soup. The family members used a stick to touch it, and the stick sank into a hole, indicating how soft it was. Over time, it gradually hardened and became a stone. [Reported by Jiaxing's Judge Jiao.]

    You Hongyuan

    A villager named You Hongyuan lived in the eastern part of the town. His neighbor, the Zhu family, had a female servant who was fond of him. They secretly communicated and agreed to marry, and she eventually became You Hongyuan's concubine. His wife was jealous and cruel, mistreating her daily and using various cursing methods to invoke the gods, hoping to hasten her death. Not long after, the concubine indeed fell ill and died. A year later, the wife also fell ill and remained bedridden for a long time, becoming listless and weak. Her family members grew tired of taking care of her and called a village woman to stay with her overnight. At night, a woman in a red skirt and green shirt appeared, slowly walking to You Hongyuan's wife's bedside. Upon seeing her, the wife recognized her as her former concubine. The concubine pointed at her and said, "My fate was not meant to die, but you cursed me so much that I died young, which is cruel and unjust. I have appealed to the judicial authority and received justice. I will definitely come back for you tonight, and you will suffer from waist pain, and you will definitely die!" After speaking, she disappeared. The village woman often visited the You household and recognized the concubine's appearance. The clothes she wore were those used for her funeral. Hearing this, the village woman was very frightened, could not sleep, and left at dawn.

    又两日来问讯，则远妻果以次日之暮死，死时呼腰痛。妪乃具言所见。远闻之，心念妾寃，而其妻往日所许誓愿，及文书之类甚多，必为己累，甚忧之。素奉道，乃日持诵玉皇经凡数百部。谋建法事，择主行者，祷于所事真武，以环珓卜之，连举数人皆名流，不许，最后举玄妙观沈道士，乃得之。因大建水陆道场数昼夜，备极诚洁，欲以谢前过。后远得病，昏迷中见隶卒持帖来勾摄。远随而行，路皆昏黑，到一大门阙下，扁曰：「岳府。」入门，隶捽远跪于庭 【 隶捽远跪于庭　原本「捽」作「卒」，据说库本改。】 ，殿上王者叱问：「尔妻攀诉尔同为咒诅，致妾非命，尔知罪乎？」远叩头谢非己过。

    161

    Two more days passed, and when news came, it was confirmed that Far's wife had indeed died the previous night, crying out in pain from her waist. The old woman then detailed what she had seen. Upon hearing this, Far felt sympathy for the concubine's injustice, but he was also worried about his wife's previous vows and written promises, which were numerous and would certainly be a burden to him. He had always practiced Daoism and thus began to recite the Jade Emperor Sutra daily, hundreds of times. He planned to conduct religious rites, choosing the person to lead the ceremonies, and prayed to the True Warrior (Zhenwu) using the yuánjiào for divination. Several famous people were consecutively named, but none were chosen; finally, the Daoist Master Shen from the Xuanmiao Temple was selected. As a result, large-scale water and land Buddhist ceremonies were conducted for several days and nights, with utmost sincerity and purity, in order to atone for past mistakes. Later, Far fell ill and, in a state of confusion, saw bailiffs holding a summons to take him away. Far followed them, and the path was dark and gloomy, leading to a grand gate where a sign read, "The Court of the Lord of the Mountains." Upon entering, the bailiffs seized Far and made him kneel in the courtyard. The king on the throne shouted and questioned, "Your wife accused you of being involved in curses, leading to her untimely death. Do you know of your guilt?" Far bowed his head and apologized, saying it was not his fault.

    王者呼左右押尤弘远妻妾来证之，卒奉命去。少选押至，皆囚首桎梏，跪阶下。王使对辩，往复甚苦。久之，妻辞屈，妾亦具言罪不在夫。王者震怒，叱其妻曰：「尔为人正室，生既妬虐，强渎鬼神；死复诬诳，妄干官府，尔罪容可逭乎？」便令卒押送酆都。仍释妾囚，判送受生案。王呼远曰：「尔虽不知情，然此妇人所为咒诅，文书甚多，如何破除？」远未及答，王案旁一绿衣判官白王曰：「高真处已有文书来，与准折过矣。」王令吏检看，乃启一櫉，櫉中文书丛沓，吏抽一卷呈王，王览之，俾授远。远惶惧中不暇细读，但见朱字数行在纸尾。王曰：「文移酆都当云呈，今乃云咨，误矣。

    162

    The king summoned his attendants to bring Yu Hongyuan's wife and concubines to testify. They obeyed the command and left. Shortly after, they arrived, all shackled and bound, kneeling at the foot of the steps. The king ordered a debate, which was very difficult. After a long time, the wife's arguments were refuted, and the concubine clearly stated that the blame did not lie with the husband. The king was greatly angered and scolded his wife, saying, "You are the principal wife; you were jealous and cruel, and you forcibly invoked the spirits while alive; after death, you lied again and falsely interfered with the officials. Can your guilt be pardoned?" He immediately ordered the soldiers to escort her to Fengdu. He still released the concubine, sentencing her to the case of rebirth. The king called Yu, saying, "Although you were unaware, this woman's actions and curses are documented in many documents. How can they be resolved?" Yu had not yet answered when a green-robed judge standing next to the king's desk said to the king, "Documents have arrived from the high realm, and they have been settled." The king ordered the officials to inspect, and they opened a box, which contained documents in piles. An official drew out a scroll and presented it to the king, who read it and ordered it to be given to Yu. In a state of fear, Yu did not have time to read it carefully, but only saw several lines of red words at the end of the paper. The king said, "Documents sent to Fengdu should say 'present,' but now it says 'consult.' It is wrong."

Lingguan looked at Wang and said, 「This is also a minor mistake and not worth questioning.」 Wang nodded in agreement. Lingguan kicked Far's back with his foot and said, 「Go away.」 Far was then released and managed to escape. They said, 「Return, you should go to the Five Pestilence Office.」 Far said, 「I do not know what the Five Pestilence Officials are, but I have only heard of the primordial qi.」 He then detailed the reason for the high-ranking deity's pardon of sins. One of the monks said, 「But do you know that following the Dao and forgetting about Buddhism is a problem? The consequences here are also not trivial. You have now returned home, you should urgently invite six highly virtuous monks for longevity, recite six volumes of the Lotus Sutra and dedicate the merit, only then can you eliminate past sins.」 They ordered him to be released, and he was able to live. He had been dead for more than a day. He immediately invited six monks, all over seventy years old, to recite the required number of sutras. To this day, every first day of the lunar month, he regularly recites scriptures and confesses sins, even when very busy. 【 Provided by Deng Kai.】

    ○猫王

    　　福建布政使朱彰，交趾人，而寓于苏。景泰初，谪为陕西庄浪驿丞。有西蕃使臣入贡一猫，道经于驿，彰馆之，使译问猫何异而上供。使臣书示云：「欲知其异，今夕请试之。」其猫盛罩于铁笼，以铁笼两重，纳着空屋内。明日起视，有数十鼠伏笼外尽死。使臣云：「此猫所在，虽数里外鼠皆来伏死。」盖猫之王也。 【 谢训导瑞说。】

    Explanation

    164

    The King of Cats

    Zhu Zhang, the Provincial Governor of Fujian, was originally from Jiaozhi but lived in Suzhou. In the early years of the Jingtai era, he was demoted to the position of Yancheng in Zanglang, Shaanxi. An envoy from the Western regions presented a cat as tribute, passing through the postal station where Zhu provided hospitality. The envoy wrote a message asking what was special about the cat and why it was offered as tribute. The envoy suggested, "To know its uniqueness, let us test it tonight." The cat was placed in a heavy iron cage with two layers, which was then put inside an empty house. The next morning, Zhu found that dozens of rats had gathered outside the cage and all had died. The envoy remarked, "This cat is so powerful that rats from several miles away come and die at its feet." Indeed, it was the king of cats. [Recorded by Xie Rui, the Instructor.]

    165

    ○昭陵银兔

    　　陕西九鬷山，唐太宗昭陵在焉。尝有醴泉县村民取薪于山，见白兔突起草中，异而逐之。兔跃入巨穴，民不觉失足亦坠焉。乃入隧道中，颇觉黯黑，其旁累铜缸十数，皆盛油，设关捩流注。最下一缸中宿火，其窍有碍，油不下，火荧荧欲灭。民为通之，火复明。向所逐兔，宛然在旁，乃银铸者，上有刻字云：「拨灯火，赐银兔一个。」民视四周积金银珠贝，瑰丽万状，再拜请曰：「小人贫，所赐不足以赡，愿更益之。」于是恣意所取，怀挟将出而路迷，跬步莫辨，便舍之，乃复有门豁然。遂携兔而出，隧门随闭，仅有微罅。民归，邻居恶少年闻之者，竞到陵所，迹其罅掘之，杳不可穷。事觉，皆被逮系，民亦几坐谴云。

    Explanation

    165

    The Silver Rabbit of Zhaoling

    On the Nine-Zong Mountain in Shaanxi, lies the tomb of Emperor Taizong of Tang, known as Zhaoling. Once, a villager from Lique County went to the mountain to fetch firewood and saw a white rabbit suddenly appear from the grass, which was unusual, so he chased it. The rabbit jumped into a large hole, and the villager, unaware, also fell in. He then found himself in a tunnel, which was quite dark, with dozens of copper pots stacked on the side, all filled with oil and set up with mechanisms for oil flow. The bottom pot had a lingering fire, but the hole was blocked, so the oil could not flow down, and the fire was flickering and about to go out. The villager cleared the blockage, and the fire reignited. The rabbit he had chased was actually a silver rabbit, with an inscription on it saying, "Clear the fire, and you will be granted a silver rabbit." The villager saw a vast accumulation of gold, silver, pearls, and shells, all beautifully arranged, and he bowed twice and requested, "I am poor, and the gift is not enough to sustain me, I wish for more." He then took whatever he wanted, carrying it out, but became lost, unable to distinguish even a step, so he abandoned it, and then a new exit suddenly opened up. He carried the rabbit out, and the tunnel door closed behind him, leaving only a tiny crack. When he returned home, his neighbors, hearing about it, rushed to the tomb, following the crack and digging, but the cave was deep and endless. The matter was discovered, and everyone involved was arrested, with the villager almost being punished.

    166

    ○梁泽

    　　三原县按察分司素多怪，居者辄死，使官莫敢入。士子梁泽以气自负，常谓诸友：「吾能宿此。」诸友出钱与赌之，泽许诺。以夜入，坐堂上。三鼓月色明朗，闻庑间有人切切私语，若相推而前者，久之不至。泽便厉声云：「何不速来？」俄有三人列跪庭下，稍前者一青衣，次一黄衣 【 次一黄衣　原本「一」作「亦」，据说库本改。】 ，一白衣，貌色不可辨识。泽骂曰：「老魅敢数害人。」青衣答曰：「非敢然也，乃见者自怖死耳。」泽曰：「汝何为者？」青衣曰：「我笔也。

    Explanation

    166

    The Inspection Office in Sanyuan County was always plagued by strange occurrences, and those who lived there died, so officials dared not enter. Scholar Liang Ze, proud of his spirit, often told his friends, "I can stay here." His friends bet money on it, and Liang agreed. At night, he entered and sat in the main hall. At the third drumbeat, the moonlight was bright, and he heard someone whispering in the eaves, as if pushing each other forward, but they did not come. Liang then shouted loudly, "Why not come quickly?" Soon, three people knelt in a row in the courtyard, the one slightly ahead dressed in green, the next in yellow, and one in white, their appearance and color could not be identified. Liang scolded, "Old demon, dare to harm many people." The one in green replied, "We are not daring to do so; it is those who see who are scared to death." Liang asked, "What are you?" The one in green said, "I am a pen."

    」问：「居何在？」曰：「在仪门屋上第三瓦沟中。」问黄衣，低回未言。青衣代答曰：「彼金钗也，在庭中槐树下。」问白衣，曰：「我剑也，在堂东柱础下。」泽曰：「汝等今来为欲相苦耶？」皆曰：「不敢。」共献一纸，曰：「此公一生履历也，今报公，令前知。」泽受而麾之曰：「去。」三物各投所言处，一时都灭。泽便卧。达曙，诸友忖谓必死，来见之，惊。泽为说向所见，未信，去，将人操锸来，按次求之，尽得三物。出其纸，如故楮币，都无一字，及夕映视之，迹了然。从是廨中永无害怖。泽后登第为御史，成化间巡按山东，以监试事诖误谪官。卒如其纸上语。

    The person asked, "Where are you staying?" and replied, "In the third tile groove on the roof of the gatehouse." When asked about the person in yellow clothing, he hesitated and did not speak. The person in green clothing answered on his behalf, saying, "That is the golden hairpin, under the locust tree in the courtyard." When asked about the person in white clothing, he said, "That is my sword, under the base of the pillar on the east side of the hall." Zé asked, "Are you here to cause us trouble?" They all replied, "We dare not." They jointly presented a piece of paper and said, "This is the biography of this person; now we are informing you, so that you may know in advance." Zé received it and waved his hand, saying, "Go away." The three items were each thrown to the places they mentioned and all disappeared at once. Zé then lay down. Until dawn, his friends thought he would surely die. They came to see him and were surprised. Zé told them about what he had seen, but they did not believe him. They left and brought people with shovels. They searched for them in turn and found all three items. They took out the paper, which was like old money, with no words on it. By evening, when they looked at it under the light, the traces were clearly visible. From then on, the office was free from harm and fear. Later, Zé passed the imperial examinations and became an imperial censor. During the Chenghua period, he was sent to inspect Shandong. He was demoted for an error in supervising the examinations. In the end, it happened just as written on the paper.

    ○黑厮

    　　黑厮者，陕西按察司隶也。洪武中，有按察使适当朝觐诣京，籍其从者名，黑厮豫焉。俄一夕病死，使将择代者，更造其籍。是夕，恍见黑厮跪白曰：「籍无庸改也，小人虽死，尚能事公。所患潼关难过，公但于关外大呼吾名，即出矣。」许之。比行，所经驿传，百需皆备，诘之则云：「适有隶报公将至，乃令治具尔。」问其状，曰：「肥短而黑。」使心知其黑厮也。出关，呼其名，讫便闻鬼语云：「某已出关矣。」自陕护至淮安，谢不肯行，曰：「都城隍严，某不敢入京师，当止此以候公。

    168

    Black Slave

    Black Slave was a servant or laborer under the Shaanxi Censorate. During the reign of Emperor Hongwu, there was an official who was due to pay homage to the emperor in the capital. He registered the names of his attendants, and Black Slave was among them. Suddenly, one night, Black Slave fell ill and died. The official was about to choose a replacement and remake the registry. That night, he suddenly saw Black Slave kneeling and saying, "There is no need to change the registry. Even though I am dead, I can still serve you. The difficulty lies in crossing the Tongguan Pass. Just shout my name loudly outside the pass, and I will come out." The official agreed to this. As they traveled, all the relay stations along the way had all necessities prepared. When asked about this, they said, "Just now, a servant reported that you were coming, so we were ordered to prepare everything." The official asked about his appearance and was told, "He was fat, short, and black." The official realized that it was Black Slave. After crossing the pass, he shouted Black Slave's name, and soon a ghostly voice said, "I have already crossed the pass." Black Slave accompanied the official from Shaanxi to Huai'an, but then refused to continue, saying, "The city god of the capital is strict, and I dare not enter the capital. I will stop here to wait for you."

    169

    」使入朝，以事下吏。久之，黑厮遂降于居民，言：「吾黑厮大王也，当血食此土。」乡民翕然信之，为立庙，凭巫言祸福甚验，祷谢无虚日，巫积所施予至数百金。岁余，使事白，复官。将渡江，黑厮下教于巫曰：「某日某官将至，具宴犒。而所有金悉归之，不者吾且罪汝。」巫不得已，往迎焉，以金献。前一日，使已见黑厮来白己曰：「公谨无泄吾名，惧不为福。」巫至，始受其献。巫不解神意，数问焉，不答。巫随行数百里，固请之，乃以实告。巫愠，归以语乡人，相率投词都城隍诉之，毁其庙，灵响遂绝。

    The official was sent to court, and the matter was handed over to officials. After a long time, the Black Chief submitted to the residents, saying, "I, the Black Chief, will receive sacrifices here." The villagers unanimously believed him and built a temple for him. They relied on the witch's predictions of good and bad fortune, which were very accurate. Prayers and thanks were offered every day without fail, and the witch accumulated what was given up to several hundred gold pieces. After a year, the matter was cleared up, and he was restored to office. As he was about to cross the river, the Black Chief gave instructions to the witch, saying, "On a certain day, a certain official will arrive. Prepare a feast and offer rewards. Hand over everything, otherwise, I will punish you." The witch had no choice but to go to meet him, offering the gold. The day before, the official had already seen the Black Chief come to tell him, "Be careful not to reveal my name, fear that it will not bring good fortune." The witch went back to tell the villagers, and they went together to the city隍 to lodge a complaint. The temple was destroyed, and the spiritual response ceased.

    ○蝎魔

    　　西安有蝎魔寺，塑大蝎于栋间。相传国初有女子，素不慧，病死复生，遂明敏，以文史知名。时有布政适丧俪，客以女为言，遂娶之。月余日，布政方视事，有所需 【 有所需　原本作「有所须」，据说库本改。】 ，使阍人入私廨取之，呼夫人不应，但见老蝎大如车轮，卧于榻。阍惊而出，以白焉，不信，叱为妖妄。阍请曰：「他日相公下堂 【 他日相公下堂　原本作「他日相公望」，据说库本改。】 ，愿无謦欬，密掩之，必可见也。

    170

    The Temple of the Scorpion Demon

    In Xi'an, there is a temple known as the Temple of the Scorpion Demon, where a large scorpion statue is placed between the beams. It is said that at the beginning of the dynasty, there was a woman who was usually not wise. She died of an illness but came back to life, and then she became bright and quick-witted, becoming famous for her knowledge of literature and history. At that time, a high-ranking official had just lost his wife, and a guest mentioned the woman, leading to the official marrying her. After a month, while the official was handling affairs, he needed something and sent a servant to the private office to fetch it. When he called for his wife, there was no response. Instead, he saw an old scorpion as big as a carriage wheel lying on the bed. The servant was shocked and came out to report it, but the official did not believe it and scolded it as a lie. The servant pleaded, saying, "On another day when the official descends the hall, I hope you don't make a sound, cover it discreetly, and it will surely be seen."

    171

    」如其言，果见老蝎伏榻上，展转间，又成好女子矣。虽抵讳，而词意颇羞涩，已而忽失所在。是夕人定，乃出拜灯下，曰：「身本蝎魔，所以夤缘见公者，非敢为幻惑，欲有求耳。公能不终拒，乃敢输情。」许之，乃曰：「昔为魔，得罪冥道，赖观音大士救拔，免其死。因假女尸为人，幸获侍左右，觊公建一兰若，以报大士之德耳。今丑迹已彰，幸公哀怜。」布政颔之，女子遂隐。他日，乃命所司建寺，至今存焉。 【 右四事张训导说。张，陕西干州人。】

    Explanation

    171

    As he spoke, indeed, an old scorpion was seen lying on the bed, and in the course of a moment, it transformed into a beautiful woman. Though she hesitated and spoke with a shy demeanor, she suddenly vanished. That night, when all was quiet, she emerged and bowed before the light, saying, "I am originally a scorpion demon. I came to see you through my connections, not to deceive or bewitch you, but to make a request. If you do not completely reject me, I dare to reveal my true feelings." He agreed, and she said, "In the past, I was a demon and offended the underworld, but I was saved by the Great Bodhisattva Guanyin, who spared my life. Because of this, I took on the form of a woman and was fortunate enough to serve you. I hoped you would build a temple to repay the virtue of the Great Bodhisattva. Now that my shameful deed has been revealed, I hope for your compassion." The provincial governor nodded in agreement, and the woman disappeared. On another day, he ordered the officials to build the temple, which still stands to this day. [This story was told by Zhang Xun Dao. Zhang was from Gan Prefecture, Shaanxi Province.]

    ○胡弘

    　　宁波儒士胡弘，字任之。少时受术于江右日者张生，力学勤苦不厌。正统初游杭遇老翁，自称汴人，深于易理。弘从之游，尽得其秘，由此以卜筮名。景泰初，从张都御史 【 楷】 征闽寇邓茂七 【 征闽寇邓茂七　原本阙「邓茂七」三字，据说库本补。】 ，在军中，所言多奇中。后至苏，士大夫多从问休咎。儒士杜琼年暮，数失子，筮得鼎初爻云：「子爻逢旺，当有二男。」赵御史 【 忠】 筮得坤之师，云：「当发策决科，司风宪，至某年月日罢官，且生子。」祝参政 【 灏】 筮得比二五爻动云：「君臣庆会，必居黄门近侍，转任大藩。」后皆验。杨尚书 【 翥】 筮得复之六二，言：「公至中年，方有奇遇。若官三品，寿九十；官二品，则差减四五年。有子亦沾禄。

    Explanation

    172

    Hu Hong, a Confucian scholar from Ningbo with the courtesy name Renzhi, learned the art of divination from Zhang Sheng, a fortune-teller from Jiangxi, in his youth. He studied diligently and worked hard without tiring. In the early years of Zhengtong, he traveled to Hangzhou and met an old man who called himself a native of Bian and was deeply knowledgeable about the principles of the Yi (Book of Changes). Hu Hong followed him and eventually mastered all his secrets, thus becoming famous for his divination skills. In the early years of Jingtai, he followed Zhang, a censor-general, to campaign against the rebel Deng Maoseven in Fujian. In the army, his predictions were often remarkably accurate. Later he went to Suzhou, where many scholars and officials sought his advice on good or bad omens. The Confucian scholar Du Qiong, in his old age, had lost several children. When he cast the divination, he got the first line of the Ding hexagram, which said: "The child line is strong; there will be two sons." Zhao, the censor, cast the divination and got the Shī line of the Kūn hexagram, which said: "You will pass the imperial examination, serve in the censorate, be dismissed from office on a certain date, and have a son." Zhu, the provincial official, cast the divination and got the second and fifth lines of the Bǐ hexagram moving, which said: "A celebration between ruler and minister; you will surely serve as a close attendant in the Yellow Gate and later be transferred to a major province." All these predictions came true. Yang, the minister, cast the divination and got the sixth line of the Fù hexagram, which said: "You will have a remarkable encounter by mid-life. If you hold a third-rank position, you will live to ninety; if a second-rank position, you will live four or five years less. Your son will also receive an official salary."

    173

    」未几，果以潜邸旧恩，累进大宗伯，卒年八十五。子亦以荫授吴县主簿。如此千百皆中。尤善相字，尝遇二士于途，将赴乡试，问得失。弘云：「二君一当中，一有服阻。」皆不以为然。已而一丧父，不得入试，一领荐。或问之，弘曰：「丧父者问时，适有人汲水而过。水与立，『泣』字也，故知其当有哭泣之戚。领荐者问时，偶有人立于旁，成『位』字，故知其必中。」又有士人应试，书「串」字问之。弘云：「君不唯中举，兼擢进士。『串』字者，二中也。」别一士闻其语，亦书「串」字以问 【 亦书串字以问　原本「书串」作「串书」，据说库本改。】 ，弘云：「君且勿言科名，当忧疾病。」其后二人一连捷，一得重疾。弘云：「前问者出于偶尔，后问者从而效之，则有心矣。『串』下加『心』，故应得患也。」其术大抵如此。

    Explanation

    173

    Not long after, he was indeed promoted to the position of Grand Minister of Rites, due to his former favor when the emperor was still a prince. He died at the age of eighty-five. His son was also granted the position of magistrate of Wuxian County through hereditary privilege. In countless cases, the predictions were accurate. He was especially skilled at divination through characters. Once, he encountered two scholars on the road who were about to take the provincial examination and asked him about their fortunes. He said, "One of the two will pass, while the other will be hindered by mourning." Neither of them believed him. Soon after, one of them lost his father and could not take the examination, while the other was recommended. Someone asked him about this, and he said, "When the one who lost his father asked, there happened to be someone drawing water and passing by. The water and the standing figure formed the character '泣' (to weep), so I knew that he would have the sorrow of mourning. When the one who was recommended asked, there happened to be someone standing beside him, forming the character '位' (position), so I knew that he would pass." There was also a scholar who was taking the examination and wrote the character "串" to ask him about his fortunes. He said, "You will not only pass the examination but will also be selected as a Jinshi. The character '串' means 'two passes.'" Another scholar heard this and also wrote the character "串" to ask. He said, "Do not speak of success in the examination; you should be concerned about illness." Later, one of them passed the examination in consecutive stages, while the other suffered from a serious illness. He said, "The first question was asked out of curiosity, while the second was asked deliberately, and thus the result was different. Adding the character '心' (heart) to '串' means that you should be concerned about illness." His methods were largely like this.

    174

    ○瑞莲

    　　正统戊午，吴县学池中，莲一茎三花。巡抚周文襄公见之曰：「行有当之者。」明年而施修撰 【 盘】 以县学生状元及第。成化辛卯，苏州府学池中，莲亦一茎二花。明春有甘露降于学之桃树上，越两月而吴文定公 【 宽】 为状元。又吴人旧传云：「穹窿石移，状元来归。」弘治丙辰，状元为今朱学士 【 希周】 。前一岁，城西穹窿山风雨中，有大石自移，时学士公犹为诸生云。

    Explanation

    174

    Prosperous Lotus

    In the year 1438 of the Zhengtong era, in the pool of the Confucian school in Wuxian, a single lotus stem bore three flowers. Zhou Dunyi, the governor of the region, observed this and remarked, "There will be someone who deserves it." The following year, Shí Pán, a student of the Confucian school, passed the imperial examination as the top scholar, fulfilling Zhou's prediction.

    In the year 1481 of the Chenghua era, in the pool of the Confucian school in Suzhou, a single lotus stem bore two flowers. That same year, sweet dew descended upon a peach tree in the school, and in the following year, Wú Kuān, a scholar, passed the imperial examination as the top scholar.

    It was also said that a stone from Qionglong Mountain moved mysteriously, and it was predicted that the状元 would return. In the year 1506 of the Hongzhi era, Zhū Xīzhōu, a student of the Confucian school, passed the imperial examination as the top scholar. The previous year, during a storm, a large stone moved on its own in Qionglong Mountain, and at that time, Zhū Xīzhōu was still a student in the Confucian school.

    ○人妖公案

    　　都察院为以男装女魇魅行奸异常事。该直隶真定府晋州奏：犯人桑冲，供系山西太原府石州李家湾文水东都军籍李大刚侄，自幼卖与榆次县人桑茂为义男。成化元年，访得大同府山阴县已故民人谷才以男装女，随处教人女子生活，暗行奸宿，一十八年不曾事发。冲要得仿效，到大同南关住人王长家寻见谷才，投拜为师。将眉脸绞剃，分作三柳，戴上■〈髟上狄下〉髻，妆作妇人身首。就彼学会女工，描剪花样，扣绣鞋顶，合包造饭等项，相谢回家。比有本县北家山任茂、张虎，谷城县张端大，马站村王大喜，文水县任昉、孙成、孙原前来见冲，学会前情。

    Explanation

    175

    Case of the Human Demon

    The Censorate reported an extraordinary case involving a man disguised as a woman. The official report from the Jinzhou Prefecture of Zhending, Zhili, stated: The accused, Sang Chong, confessed to being the nephew of Li Dagang, a military officer from Dongdu, Wenshui, and was adopted by San Mao from Yuci County as a stepson. From a young age, he was sold to San Mao. In the first year of the Chenghua era, he discovered that Gu Cai, a deceased resident of Shan County, Datong Prefecture, had disguised himself as a woman and taught women's ways of life everywhere, secretly engaging in sexual acts for eighteen years without being exposed. Chong wanted to imitate him and went to Wang Chang's home in the south gate of Datong to find Gu Cai, who formally became his teacher. He had his eyebrows and face shaved, parted his hair into three sections, wore a specific hairstyle, and dressed as a woman. There, he learned women's crafts, designing and cutting patterns, sewing the tops of shoes, preparing meals, and other tasks, then thanked and returned home. Later, people from Beijia Mountain, Ren Mao and Zhang Hu, Zhang Dada from Gucheng County, Wang Daxi from Majian Village, and Ren Fang, Sun Cheng, and Sun Yuan from Wenshui County came to see Chong and learned the previous situation.

    176

    冲与各人言说：「恁们到各处人家，出入小心，若有事发，休攀出我来。」当就各散去讫。成化三年三月内，冲离家到今十年，别无生理，在外专一图奸。经历大同、平阳、太原、真定、保定、顺天、顺德、河间、济南、东昌等府朔州、永年、大谷等，共四十五府州县，及乡村镇店七十八处。到处用心打听良家出色女子，设计假称逃走乞食妇人，先到傍住贫小人家投作工。一二日，使其传说，引进教作女工，遇晚同歇，诳言作戏，哄说喜允，默与奸宿。若有秉正不从者，候至更深，使小法子。将随身带着鸡子一个，去青，桃 【 卒】 七个 【 鸡子一个去青桃卒七个柳卒七个　说库本「青」作「清」，「卒」均作「辛」。

    Explanation

    176

    Chong told everyone: "Be cautious when entering and leaving each household. If anything happens, don't implicate me." They then dispersed and completed their tasks. In the third month of the third year of the Chenghua era, Chong had been away from home for ten years, with no other means of livelihood, and had been dedicated to plotting evil. He had traveled through Datong, Pingyang, Taiyuan, Zhending, Baoding, Shuntian, Shunde, Huan, Jinan, and Dongchang prefectures, as well as Shuozhou, Yongnian, and Dagou states, a total of 45 prefectures, states, and counties, and 78 villages, towns, and markets. Everywhere, he carefully inquired about well-bred, beautiful women, devising a plan to pretend to be a runaway beggar woman, first going to poor small households to work. After one or two days, he had them spread the word and introduce her as a seamstress, meeting at night to rest together, telling lies and pretending to play, coaxing them to agree, and secretly committing adultery. If there was someone who was upright and refused, he would wait until very late and use a trick, taking a chicken egg with him, removing the green, and using seven peaches (or other items). In one version of the text, "青" is written as "清" and "卒" is written as "辛."

    177

    】 ，俱烧灰，新针一个，铁搥捣烂，烧酒一口，合成迷药，喷于女子身上。默念昏迷咒，使其女子手脚不动，口不能言，行奸毕，又念解昏咒。女子方醒，但有刚直怒骂者，冲再三陪情，女子含忍。或住三朝五日，恐人识出，又行那移别处求奸。似此得计十年，奸通良家女子一百八十二人，一向不曾事发。成化十三年七月十三日酉时分，前到真定府晋州地名聂村生员高宣家，诈称是赵州民人张林妾，为夫打骂逃走前来投宿。本人仍留在南房内宿歇。至起更时分，有高宣婿赵文举潜入房内求奸。冲将伊推打，被赵文举将冲捽倒在炕按住，用手揣无胸乳，摸有肾囊，将冲捉送晋州。审供前情是实。

    Explanation

    177

    In this way, for ten years, he committed adultery with 182 virtuous women, never once being discovered. On the 13th day of the 7th month in the 13th year of the Chenghua era, at the hour of the rooster, he arrived at the home of a scholar named Gao Xuan in the village of Nie in Jinzhou, Zhen Ding Prefecture, claiming to be the concubine of Zhang Lin from Zhao Prefecture, having fled from her husband's beatings and seeking shelter. The person remained in the southern room for lodging. Until the first watch of the night, Gao Xuan's son-in-law Zhao Wenju secretly entered the room to commit adultery. The person pushed and beat him, and was grabbed by Zhao Wenju and thrown down onto the kang (heating platform) and held down. Zhao Wenju felt for breasts but found none, and felt for testicles and found them, and the person was captured and sent to Jinzhou. The interrogation confirmed the previous statements were true.

    参照本犯立心异人，有类十恶，律无该载。除将本犯并奸宿良家女子姓名开单，连人牢固押法司收问外，乞勅法司将本犯问拟重罪等因。具本奏，奉圣旨：「都察院看了来说。钦此。」钦遵。臣等看得桑冲所犯，死有余辜，其所供任茂等俱各习学前术，四散奸淫，欲将桑冲问拟死罪。仍行各处巡按御史，挨拿任茂等解京，一体问罪，以警将来。及前项妇女，俱被桑冲以术迷乱，其奸非出本心，又干碍人众，亦合免其查究。成化十三年十一月二十日掌院事太子少保兼左都御史王等具题。二十二日于奉天门奏。奉圣旨：「是。这厮情犯丑恶，有伤风化，便凌迟了，不必覆奏。任茂等七名，务要上紧挨究，得获解来。钦此。」 【 右得之友人家旧抄公牍中。】

    　　升遐之兆

    178

    Referring to the criminal's intent being extraordinary, similar to the ten grave offenses, and not covered by the law, except for listing the names of the criminal and the women he had intercourse with, and arresting them firmly and taking them to the judicial authorities for questioning, we request that the judicial authorities be instructed to sentence the criminal to a severe punishment. A memorial was presented, and in accordance with the imperial edict: "The Censorate has reviewed and reported." As the emperor has decreed. In accordance with the decree. We have examined the case of Sang Chong, who deserves death and more. As he confessed, Ren Mao and others were all skilled in the occult arts, engaging in promiscuous sexual acts. We intend to sentence Sang Chong to death. And we instruct the circuit censors in various regions to apprehend Ren Mao and others and bring them to the capital, punishing them uniformly, to warn future generations. As for the women involved, they were all bewitched by Sang Chong, and their promiscuity was not of their own volition, and involves many people, so they should also be exempted from further investigation. On the 20th day of the 11th month of the 13th year of the Chenghua era, the Grand Secretary and Left Vice-President of the Censorate, Wang, and others presented a memorial. On the 22nd, they presented it at the Hall of Supreme Harmony. In accordance with the imperial edict: "Correct. This person's crime is truly vile, harmful to public morals, and should be subjected to the death penalty by slicing, no need for further reporting. Ren Mao and others, seven in number, must be apprehended with urgency, and brought to the capital." As the emperor has decreed. [Taken from an old copy of a public document found in a friend's home.]

    Chapter: The Omen of Ascension

    In the seventeenth year of the Hongzhi era, a commoner in Suzhou's Zhu Zhu Lane (also known as Drilling Turtle Lane) died of illness. Upon arriving in the underworld, he met the Lord of Hell. The records were inspected, and it was said, "Your lifespan has not yet ended." He was then allowed to return. The palaces, utensils, and attire in the underworld were all like those in the human world, but it was strange that the officials and servants were all dressed in mourning attire. He privately asked about this, and they replied, "The emperor in the mortal world has passed away, so we are in mourning." The commoner returned to life and privately told his relatives about the experience. In the following May, the emperor abdicated. According to the Xuan Guai Lu, during the late Yuanhe period, the Inspector of Gao'an, Xin Gongping, encountered officials of the underworld welcoming the emperor. He accompanied them into the main hall, where he saw the emperor ascend into a carriage, escorted by soldiers and horses. Several months later, there were tears of mourning. Today, what this commoner saw also occurred after half a year, and the events were roughly the same.

    180

    ○诚意伯

    　　诚意公佐命之功，追踪文成，而时罕传记。至其学所师承，亦无能言之者。 【 或云师九江黄楚望，更考之。】 予乡人顾楩知青田县，与刘翁游，为诚意之末孙，能通其家学。为楩言：诚意未遇时，知青田山有灵异，日手一编，面山而坐，目不暂释。经岁，忽崖上豁开二扉，公亟掷书趋入，闻有呵之者曰：「此中毒恶，不可入也。」公不顾，极力排而进。其中日色明朗，有石室方丈，壁上见七大字云：「此石为刘基所破。」公喜，引巨石推之，应手折裂，得一石函，中有古钞兵书四卷，怀之出，纔转足而壁合如故。归诵之，甚习，然犹未得其肯棨。乃多游深山崇剎，以访异人。

    Explanation

    180

    Final Translation

    Chengyi, the Marquis of Loyalty

    The meritorious service of Chengyi, the Marquis of Loyalty, follows in the footsteps of Wen Cheng, yet his achievements are rarely recorded. As for the source of his learning and the teachers he followed, no one can speak of them. [Some say he studied under Huang Chuyang of Jiujiang; further investigation is needed.] My fellow townsman, Gu Pian, who knew Qingtian County, traveled with Old Master Liu and is a descendant of Chengyi. He understands the family learning. He told me: When Chengyi had not yet achieved fame, he knew that Qingtian Mountain had supernatural phenomena. He would hold a book in his hand, sit facing the mountain, and never take his eyes off it. After a year, suddenly two doors opened on the cliff. He quickly threw down his book and rushed inside, hearing someone warn him, "This place is poisonous and evil, do not enter." But he paid no heed and pushed forward with great effort. Inside, the sunlight was bright, and there was a small stone room. On the wall, he saw seven large characters: "This stone was broken by Liu Ji." He was delighted and pulled a large stone to push it, breaking it with a single touch. He found a stone box containing four ancient military treatises, which he carried out. As soon as he turned his foot, the wall closed again as it was. Upon returning, he recited the texts and became very familiar with them, but still did not fully understand their essence. Thus, he frequently visited deep mountains and grand temples to seek out extraordinary individuals.

    181

    久之，入一山寺，见老道士凭几读书，知其隐者，拜之请教，道士不顾。公力恳之，道士举所读书以授曰：「读此旬日能背诵，则可；不能，姑去。」书厚二寸，公一夕记其半，道士惊叹曰：「子天才也。」遂得其学。后佐高皇帝，尝对御言及道士。上令驿召至阙，年且八十，而容色甚少。命与诚意及张铁冠择建宫之地，初各不相闻，既而皆为图以进，尺寸若一。上欲留之，不可，遂放还山，不知所终。又言公疾革时，语其子云：「吾家封爵当中绝，然至五世后，应得武职。从兹可传继矣。」至孙荐袭爵，后果被革。弘治初诏录公后为处州指挥使，正五世矣。时嫡孙以罪系狱，有司脱桎梏而冠服之，人以为奇遇。 【 顾楩为子远说。】

    Explanation

    181

    After a long time, he entered a mountain temple and saw an old Taoist sitting by a table reading a book. Recognizing him as a hermit, he bowed and asked for instruction, but the Taoist ignored him. The official pleaded earnestly, and the Taoist handed him the book he was reading and said, "If you can recite this in ten days, then you may proceed; if not, leave." The book was two inches thick, and the official memorized half of it in one night. The Taoist exclaimed, "You are a genius!" Thus, the official obtained the Taoist's teachings. Later, he assisted Emperor Gao. Once, he mentioned the Taoist to the emperor. The emperor ordered him to be summoned by imperial decree to the capital. The Taoist was nearly eighty years old but appeared very youthful. The emperor ordered him to choose with Cheng Yi and Zhang Tianguan the site for the imperial palace. Initially, they did not communicate with each other, but later they all submitted plans, and the measurements were identical. The emperor wanted to keep him, but it was not possible, so he was released to return to the mountain, and his final fate is unknown. The Taoist also said that when the official was gravely ill, he told his son, "Our family's title of nobility will be cut off, but after five generations, we should obtain a military position. From this point, it can be passed down." When the official's grandson succeeded to the title, it was eventually abolished. In the early years of the Hongzhi era, the emperor ordered that the descendants of the official be appointed as the commander of Chuzhou, exactly five generations later. At that time, the legitimate grandson was imprisoned for a crime, and the officials removed his shackles and dressed him in official robes, which people considered a rare opportunity. [Gu Pin told this story to his son Yuan.]

    182

    ○上梁日时

    　　诚意公尝过吴门，中夜闻邪许声，以问左右，曰：「人家上梁也。」又问其家贫富及屋之豊俭，曰：「贫家，数楹屋耳。」公叹曰：「择日人术精乃尔。」又曰：「惜哉，其不久也。」左右问故，公曰：「此日此时，上梁最吉，家当大发，然必巨室乃可。若贫家骤富，必复更置此屋，旺气一去，其衰可待也。」其后此家生计日裕 【 其后此家生计日裕　原本无「此」字，据说库本补。】 ，不数载，藏镪百万，果撤屋广之。未久，遂贫落如故。

    Explanation

    182

    The Auspicious Day and Time for Raising the Main Beam

    Once, the Venerable Master passed through Wu Gate and, in the middle of the night, heard the sounds of "Ya He" (a traditional chant used during the beam-raising ceremony). He asked those around him, and they replied, "A household is raising the main beam." He then inquired about the family's wealth and the size of their house, and they answered, "It is a poor family with just a few rooms." The Master sighed and said, "The skill of selecting the day and time for such an event is truly refined." He added, "Alas, it will not last long." When those around him asked why, the Master explained, "On this day and at this time, raising the main beam is the most auspicious, and the household will prosper greatly. However, this prosperity will only occur if the household is large and wealthy. If a poor family suddenly becomes wealthy, they will likely rebuild the house. Once the good fortune leaves, the decline is inevitable." Indeed, the household's financial situation gradually improved over time, and within a few years, they accumulated a million units of currency. They then demolished and expanded the house. Soon after, they returned to their previous state of poverty.

    183

    ○义象行

    　　洪武中，林膳部 【 子羽】 尝作义象行曰：「有象有象来天都，大江欲渡心次且。诱之既渡献天子，拜跪不与众象俱。象奴劝之拜，怒鼻触象奴。赐酒不肯饮。哺之亦不餔。屹然十日受饥渴，侻首垂泪愤且吁。天子命杀之，众官束手莫敢屠。侍卫传宣呼壮士，披甲各执丈二殳。象战久不克，兵捷象乃殂。忆昔君皇每巡幸，象当法驾行天衢，珊瑚错落明天珠，被服美锦红氍毹。紫泥函封载玉玺，万乐争拥羣龙趋。玉玺归沙漠，龙亦归鼎湖。所以老象心，南来誓死骨为枯。嗟尔食禄人，空负七尺躯。高高白玉堂，赫赫黄金符，伊昔轩冕今泥涂。嗟尔食禄人，不若饭豆刍。象何洁，尔何污。天子垂衣治万世，俾全象德行天诛。呜呼，象兮古所无，呜呼，象兮古所无！」

    Explanation

    183

    Translation

    A Poem of the Righteous Elephant

In the era of Hongwu, Lin Ziyu, the Minister of Rites, once composed this poem:

There was an elephant, an elephant, who came to the imperial capital, hesitating by the great river.
Lured across, it was presented to the Son of Heaven, but it did not kneel and bow like the other elephants.
The elephant handler urged it to kneel, but it angrily struck him with its trunk.
When offered wine, it refused to drink. When fed, it refused to eat.
For ten days, it stood firm, enduring hunger and thirst, shaking its head, shedding tears, and expressing anger and sorrow.
The emperor commanded it to be killed, but the officials were helpless and dared not slaughter it.
The guards summoned brave warriors, who donned armor and wielded long spears.
The battle with the elephant lasted a long time without success, but the soldiers eventually triumphed, and the elephant fell.
Recalling the emperor's frequent tours, the elephant had always been part of the ceremonial procession, adorned with coral and pearls, dressed in beautiful brocade and red felt.
The imperial seal was carried in a purple clay box, and the grand music followed the emperor.
The seal returned to the desert, and the dragon returned to the Lake of the Dead.
Thus, the old elephant's heart, coming from the south, vowed to die and become a skeleton.
Alas, you who feed on the emperor's bounty, are useless despite your seven-foot-tall bodies. Once high-ranking officials in white jade halls, now reduced to lowly status.
Alas, you who feed on the emperor's bounty, are no better than the simple food given to animals.
How pure the elephant, how corrupt you.
The emperor governs the world with ease and authority, allowing the elephant to die while preserving its noble character.
Alas, such an elephant was never seen before!
    184

    ○张潮

    　　苏学生张潮惟信，戊寅十二月二十八日得寒疾死，年止四十二。其女痛父之殁，号恸陨绝，良久复苏。云：见父服朱袍，张黄盖，后二人青袍青盖，皆乘肩舆，从者数十人，呵殿而行。女望见父在舆中，呼问所之，曰：「吾今为衢州知府，以正旦到任，故急行耳。」女垂涕问曰：「父今做官，母女孤零无依，何不挈之俱行也？」潮亦泫然，曰：「未也，汝母寿应至七十五，至期吾当自来领取。吾在彼，左右乏人，对门暑袜铺王家女子颇淑慧，吾欲取之。」又指示女曰：「二公乃同知通判，一昆山人姓张，一太仓人姓王，皆秀才也。与吾同选复同僚，今俱赴任耳。」言讫驰去。时王氏女正得疾甚重，未几果死。予亲友有与张潮善者往吊，闻女言如此。

    Explanation

    Zhang Cao Wei Xin

    Zhang Cao Wei Xin, a scholar from Suzhou, died of a cold illness on the twenty-eighth day of the twelfth month in the year of Wu Yin, at the age of forty-two. His daughter, grieving her father's death, cried out in anguish and collapsed, only to revive after a long time. She reported seeing her father dressed in a red robe and holding a yellow canopy, followed by two others in green robes and canopies, all riding sedan chairs, with many attendants accompanying them as they proceeded with shouts and commands. The daughter, seeing her father in the sedan chair, called out to ask where he was going. He replied, "I am now the governor of Quzhou, and I am rushing to take office on New Year's Day." The daughter, with tears in her eyes, asked, "Father, now that you are in office, mother and I are left alone and without support. Why didn't you take her along with you?" Zhang Cao also wept, saying, "Not yet. Your mother is destined to live to seventy-five, and at that time, I will come to take her myself. I am there, but I lack attendants. The woman from the Wang family who runs the sock shop next door is kind and wise, and I wish to marry her." He then pointed to two men and said, "These two are joint governors or deputy magistrates. One is from Kunshan, surnamed Zhang, and the other is from Taicang, surnamed Wang. They are all scholars. We were selected together and became colleagues, and now we are all taking office." After saying this, he sped away. At that time, the Wang family girl was also very ill, and not long after, she died. One of my friends, who was close to Zhang Cao, went to offer condolences and heard the daughter speak thus.

    ○王贯

    　　王贯字一之 【 王贯字一之　说库本「一之」作「一言」。】 ，故蜀人，系籍锦衣卫，居京师。举成化丁未进士，知□□县，到任年余，有廉能称。一日，忽语其妻徐氏曰：「吾当为此地城隍，行且与尔别矣。」妻愕然曰：「君病狂耶？」贯曰：「不然，昨梦帝遣使衔命来，吾以家累多，宦业未成力辞，不得允，势必须去，期在明夕耳。」又呼其子永年嘱之曰：「好事若母，力为善人。」及明夕漏下十数刻，冠带升堂，召吏使鸣鼓，集僚属。

    Explanation

    185

    Wang Guan, courtesy name Yizhi, was originally from Sichuan but had his household registered with the Jinyiwei and resided in the capital. He passed the imperial examination in the Dingwei year of the Chenghua era and served as the magistrate of □□ County. After a year in office, he was known for his integrity and ability. One day, he suddenly told his wife Xu that, "I will become the City God of this place and will soon have to part from you." His wife was startled and asked, "Are you insane?" Wang replied, "No, last night I dreamed that the Emperor sent a messenger with a command. I excused myself because of my many family responsibilities and unfinished career, but it was not allowed, so I must go. The deadline is tomorrow night." He then called his son Yongnian and instructed him, "Be good to your mother and strive to be a virtuous person." By the next night, after several hours had passed, he dressed in formal attire, ascended the hall, summoned the officials to beat the drum, and gathered the officials.

    186

    吏白：「深夜非时。」贯不听。鼓竟，同官毕集，贯从容曰：「予得与诸公同事，幸甚。今受帝命为城隍，不复得相周旋，荷诸公爱厚，敢以妻子为托，顾薄俸足以为装，但少赐周全，令得归故里足矣。」同官方怪愕，贯起向之再拜曰：「予今非狂也，今即行矣。」语讫，还内沐浴，公服端坐，呼妻子与诀，了无惨慽容。俄而自称头眩，遂瞑目而逝。及明，颜色如生，同官为殓殡，护其妻子还京师。 【 医士陈希恩，贯妻甥也，因说张潮事及此。】

    　　○斗神救灾

    　　常熟县奚浦钱氏，大族也。正德丙寅，其族连居数房皆被焚，火凡三夕始绝。煨烬中有小楼三楹，巍然独存，乃所谓小四房者。姑妇二人寡居，同处楼中，方火炽时，烟焰四逼，二人窘布无措。素事斗神，但扣头求救。须臾，见朱衣者七人立檐下，举袖麾之，火应手而散，七人忽不见。姑妇拜起，则四面几无一椽留矣。 【 庞金说。】

    Explanation

    186

    The official reported, "It is late at night and not the proper time." But Guan did not listen. After the drumming was finished, all the officials gathered. Guan calmly said, "I am fortunate to work with all of you. Today, I have been appointed as the City God by the emperor, and I will no longer be able to interact with you. I deeply appreciate your kindness and dare to entrust my wife and children to you. The small salary is enough for preparation, but please provide some assistance so that I may return to my hometown." The officials were just startled. Guan stood up and bowed twice, saying, "I am not crazy now; I will leave immediately." After saying this, he soon claimed to have a headache and then closed his eyes and passed away. By morning, his appearance was still lifelike. The officials protected his wife and children and returned them to the capital. [The physician Chen Xien, Guan's sister's son, recounted this story.]

    The Worship of the Fighting God to Save from Disaster

    The Qian family in Xipi Village, Changshu County, was a large clan. In the third year of the Zhengde era (1506), several branches of the family were burned down in succession, and the fire lasted for three nights before it was extinguished. Among the ruins, a small pavilion with three rooms stood alone, known as the "Small Fourth Branch." A widow and her daughter-in-law lived together in the pavilion. When the fire was at its fiercest, smoke and flames surrounded them, and the two women were in a desperate situation with no means to escape. They had always worshipped the Fighting God, so they knelt down and prayed for help. Soon, they saw seven figures in red clothes standing under the eaves, raising their sleeves to disperse the fire. The seven figures suddenly disappeared. The widow and her daughter-in-law stood up and bowed, only to find that there was not a single roof beam left on all sides. [Pang Jin recounted this story.]

    ○张氏子入冥

    　　御史张西铭希载，云南人。有季弟年十二三得疾死，而尸不冷，家人未忍殓，三日开目复活。母询其所以，答云：「病中忽忽不自省了，但觉二吏夹持我行通衢间，人烟市肆，不异人世。到一公廨，制甚卑下，吾父及伯父并立于门，见我呼问所以来，答云：『适在家为二吏引至此。』二父且喜且悲，询家人安否，及生计甚悉，我一一答之。父曰：『儿勿忧，汝命未尽，到前司当得放还。』且示戒云：『前路人与汝汤水，却不可食，食便不得归矣。』吾敬诺。吏引向一司，主者未出，庭中吏卒头面皆诡异可怖。

    The Son of the Zhang Family Enters the Underworld

    Grand Censor Zhang Ximing Xizai, a native of Yunnan, had a youngest brother who was twelve or thirteen years old and died of an illness, but his body did not turn cold, and the family did not dare to bury him; three days later, he opened his eyes and came back to life. The mother asked him why this had happened, and he replied: "While I was sick, I felt dazed and unaware of myself. I only felt that two officials held me tightly as I walked in the main thoroughfare, where there were people, houses, markets, and shops, just like in the world of the living. I arrived at a government office, whose appearance was very lowly, and my father and uncle stood together at the door. They saw me and called out, asking why I had come. I replied: 'I was just now at home when two officials led me here.' My father and uncle were both happy and sad, and they asked about the safety of the family and their livelihood in great detail. I answered them one by one. My father said: 'Do not worry, son. Your life is not yet finished. When you get to the previous office, you will be able to be released back.' He also gave a warning, saying: 'The people ahead will give you soup or water, but do not eat it. If you eat it, you will not be able to return.' I respectfully agreed. The official led me toward one office, but the head of the office had not come out, and the heads and faces of the officials and soldiers in the courtyard were all strange and frightening."

    188

    吾见案上有一卷书，题曰注死簿，揭视之，首一行曰：『某日府学生周某午时死，府吏朱某戌时死。』又欲视其次，二吏见之呵曰：『小儿那得看此。』以手掩之。已而主者出，呼问姓名，检簿看毕，叱曰：『非也，姓同名异，所追误矣。』命吏送还，仍到向处，二父犹在，喜谓我曰：『从此去，可速达家。』遂循而归，不觉便活耳。」母闻其言不甚信，遣人阴察儿所言二人。至其日，周生者晨自学舍归，及门中风，至午死。朱生晚间犹无恙，至昏时而镇守内臣过其地，朱正辖夫役，以人数不足死杖下，时刻不爽。始大异之。时希载从宦于外，母贻书令市褐纱五百疋，制僧服为儿忏悔。希载道吴江以托盛医官买之，为盛具说如此。 【 顾说。】

    Explanation

    188

    I saw a book titled "Register of Death Notes" on the table. I lifted and looked at it, and the first line said: "On a certain day, the scholar Zhou died at noon, and the official Zhu died at戌 (戌 is a time unit in ancient Chinese, roughly equivalent to 7-9 PM)." I wanted to see the next entry, but two officials saw me and shouted, "How could a child see this?" They covered the book with their hands. Later, the master came out, called and asked for names, checked the register and finished looking. He said, "No, the surnames are the same but the names are different; the pursuit was mistaken." He ordered the officials to send me back. I returned to the original place, where the two fathers were still there. They happily told me, "From here, you can quickly reach home." So I followed the path and returned home, not realizing I was alive.

    My mother did not fully believe what I said and sent someone to secretly investigate the two people I mentioned. On that day, the scholar Zhou returned from school in the morning and caught a cold upon reaching the gate. He died at noon. Zhu was fine in the evening, but in the evening, a palace guard passed by his place. Zhu was overseeing the laborers, and because the number of people was insufficient, he was beaten to death. The timing was exact. Only then did I realize the strangeness of it.

    At that time, Xi Zai was serving abroad. My mother sent a letter instructing him to buy 500 pieces of dark silk to make monastic robes for my son's repentance. Xi Zai went to Wujiang and entrusted a famous physician to buy them, and told him everything in detail. [This story is told by Gu.]

    ○杨少卿

    　　长兴杨复，幼有敏才。为士子时，迎提学于关外，未至，伺于土地堂中。戏取■〈王丕〉珓祝曰：「提学即至，当赐胜兆。」一掷而珓落于梁上，不可取。即以垩书神像背云：「发武陵驿摆站。」是夜，神见梦于提学云：「公所辖士黥吾背，发为驿夫，幸公一言免之。」明日以诘诸生，复愧谢，叱令洗去。是夕，又梦神来谢，因问：「此生一少年，神何畏之如此？」神曰：「此人他日大理少卿也。」复后登第，累官果至棘寺。在任不久，即乞致仕还乡。未至家，先遍辞亲友曰：「吾某日且逝矣。」至期，端坐而卒。复平生刚鲠自守 【 复平生刚鲠自守　原本「鲠」作「鯾」，据说库本改。】 ，为乡邦推重云。

    Yang Shaohua of Changxing

    Yang Fu, from Changxing, was a young man with exceptional talent. When he was a student, he went to meet the provincial examiner outside the pass, but before the examiner arrived, he waited in the land temple. In jest, he took a divination tool and wished, saying, "When the examiner arrives, may I receive a favorable sign." He threw the divination tool, and it fell onto the beam, making it impossible to retrieve. He then wrote on the back of the deity's image with lime, saying, "Send me to the Wu Ling post station." That night, the deity appeared in a dream to the provincial examiner, saying, "The officials under your jurisdiction branded my back and made me a post station worker. Please speak up and release me." The next day, the examiner questioned the students, and Yang Fu felt ashamed and apologized, ordering him to wash it off. That night, the deity appeared again in a dream to thank him, and asked, "This young man, why do you fear him so much?" The deity replied, "This person will one day become a Deputy Minister of Justice." Yang Fu later passed the imperial examination and gradually rose to become a high-ranking official in the Yushi Tai (Supervisory Court). He served for a short time and then requested retirement to return to his hometown. Before reaching home, he first bid farewell to his relatives and friends, saying, "I will die on a certain day." On that day, he sat upright and died. Throughout his life, Yang Fu was always upright and principled, and he was highly respected by his hometown.

    ○张孟介

    　　湖州张廉孟介，以都御史镇云南。尝巡边徼，夜宿军营。人定后，自携灯出游，顾一美妇人在旁，张惊愕，遽以灯授之，妇亦不辞，执灯侍侧。既讫，麾令前行，妇亦如命。入帐，欲观书以自持而无书，偶得大明律读之，至五鼓不一转盻。妇不能惑，掷灯而隐，竟不知何怪。

    Zhang Mengjie

    Zhang Mengjie, a high-ranking official from Huzhou, served as the Governor-General in Yunnan. Once, he went on an inspection tour to the border regions and stayed overnight in a military camp. After midnight, he took a lamp with him and went for a walk. Suddenly, he noticed a beautiful woman standing beside him. Zhang was startled and quickly handed the lamp to her. The woman did not hesitate and took the lamp, standing by his side. After a while, he gestured for her to go ahead, and she complied. He then entered the tent, intending to read a book to distract himself, but found no books. By chance, he came across the Great Ming Code and began to read it, so intently that he did not even blink until dawn. The woman could not seduce him, so she threw the lamp away and disappeared, leaving him still unsure of what kind of spirit she was.

    ○严尚书

    　　严震直，字子敏，湖之骥村人，有宠高皇朝，累官户部尚书。后奉使安南，死于途，归葬郭外。他日，有舟过其墓侧，遇一老公附舟，云：「欲至骥村。」及到严氏宅前，谓舟人曰：「吾入内，使家人以钱畀汝。」乃登岸，一足践于水，濡其靴。既入，久而不出，因扣其家曰：「适有老公附舟，入门，今安在？」讶曰：「无之。」顾地上有足迹，循之，乃入家庙中，视严公像，一足靴果湿，方知是神归也。 【 右三事湖州柳如嵩说。】

    　　○木妖

    　　予所居临顿里中百姓金氏，有旧杨木肉杌，已七八年物。己卯四月 【 己卯四月　原本作「今年四月」，据说库本改。】 ，忽生枝条十余，青色，粗踰食着。又桃花坞徐铁匠家木杌亦生枝条，畧与金氏同，近木妖也。

    Explanation

    191

    Translation

    严尚书

    严震直，字子敏，是湖之骥村人，深得高皇朝的宠信，官至户部尚书。后来奉命出使安南，途中不幸去世，归葬于城外。某日，有一艘船经过他的墓旁，遇到一位老者登船，说：“我要去骥村。”船到严氏宅前，老者对船夫说：“我进去，让家人给你钱。”于是登岸，一脚踩入水中，弄湿了靴子。进入宅中后，许久不见出来，船夫便敲门询问：“刚才有一位老者登船，进门后现在在哪里？”家人惊讶地说：“没有啊。”船夫看到地上有脚印，循着脚印，发现老者进入了家庙，看到严公的雕像，发现一只靴子果然湿了，这才明白老者是严公的神魂归来。【以上三事由湖州的柳如嵩讲述。】

    木妖

    我居住的临顿里有一位百姓金氏，家中有一张旧的杨木肉杌，已有七八年的历史。己卯四月，这张肉杌突然长出了十多根枝条，青色，粗得超过食物。又听说桃花坞徐铁匠家的木杌也长出了枝条，与金氏家的情况相似，可能是木妖作祟。

    192

    ○唐■〈王巳〉

    　　吴县吏唐■〈王巳〉，嘉定江湾镇人，年十八，习吏事。尝送客入城，归倦甚，隐几而卧。忽冥然如梦，见两皂衣牵马来曰：「昆山某官邀君饮。」■〈王巳〉便上马，驰出嘉定北门，入昆山南门，迤逦沿坏城而行 【 迤逦沿坏城而行　原本无「坏」字，据说库本补。】 。忽复有二人出，持牒叱曰：「吾山王遣来，追违限者，汝不得复乘马。」即捽■〈王巳〉至地，出袖中绠，系其颈，行抵山王庙门下入报。内传呼召入，跪于庭。神衣黄袍，插金花，侍卫甚众，谓■〈王巳〉曰：「知汝有吏才，特召来为我掌四殿八厢公牍。」指阶上竹笥十六示之曰：「此皆文案也。」山王为昆城妖神，■〈王巳〉素知，自念一承职，永不得生矣。

    Explanation

    192

    Tang Wengsi, a clerk from Wuxian County, was from the town of Jiangwan in Jiading. At eighteen years old, he had been studying official duties. Once, after escorting a guest into the city, he returned feeling very tired and leaned against a table to fall asleep. Suddenly, as if in a dream, he saw two figures in black clothing leading a horse and said, "An official from Kunshan invites you to drink." Tang Wengsi immediately mounted the horse and galloped out through the north gate of Jiading, entering the south gate of Kunshan, winding along a ruined city wall. Suddenly, two more people appeared, holding a document and shouting, "We are sent by the Mountain God to pursue those who have missed their deadlines. You may no longer ride a horse." They seized Tang Wengsi to the ground, pulled out a rope from their sleeves, tied it around his neck, and led him to the gate of the Mountain God's temple to report. Inside, they called out to summon him, and he knelt in the courtyard. The deity was dressed in a yellow robe, adorned with golden flowers, and was surrounded by many attendants. The deity told Tang Wengsi, "I know you have talent as a clerk and have specially summoned you to manage the official documents of the four halls and eight pavilions." Pointing to sixteen bamboo containers on the steps, the deity said, "These are all the documents." The Mountain God is a local deity of Kunshan, and Tang Wengsi had always known about this. He thought to himself that once he accepted this position, he would never be able to return to life.

    193

    因力辞曰：「某素不谙吏事，亦不识一字，惟大王哀免。」再三强之，固不从。神怒，叱左右加刑，五毒备极，痛苦不堪，而■〈王巳〉执词愈坚。神无如之何，乃令行刑者提置庑下，而别书牒，令人持去追其县某人来云。约半日，追至一人，神复以前语语之，此人忻然拜命。神喜，即为易冠服，领十六笥退入司中。神呼前两人送■〈王巳〉付土地祠，令转达东岳还魂。至祠，土神冠佩出受牒，自遣部下两人送诣岳祠。既到，停门外，入投牒未出，■〈王巳〉望之，见岳帝冠冕赭袍，据案治事。侍立皆紫衣纱帽者，不知几百，而庭下往来扰扰，又数百人。■〈王巳〉自念：「吾方足痛，恐入门不堪诸人践踏。」踌躇间，忽门内有人出呼曰：「郎君何为在此？」视之，乃唐氏故仆也。

    Explanation

    193

    He refused with great effort, saying, "I have never been familiar with administrative matters, nor do I know a single character. Only Your Majesty, please have mercy and forgive me." Despite repeated urging, he still refused. The deity became angry and scolded the attendants to inflict punishment, using all five types of punishments to the utmost, causing unbearable pain. Yet, ■〈王巳〉 remained steadfast in his refusal. The deity could do nothing about it and then ordered the executioner to take him and place him under the eaves. The deity wrote a separate document and had someone take it to summon a certain person from the county to come. After about half a day, the summoned person arrived. The deity repeated the previous words to him, and this person gladly accepted the order. The deity was pleased and immediately changed his headdress and clothing, leading him with sixteen chests and withdrawing into the office. The deity called the two people forward to hand over ■〈王巳〉 to the land temple, ordering them to convey him to the Eastern Peak for revival. Upon arriving at the temple, the god of the land, wearing a headdress and ornaments, came out to receive the document and sent two of his subordinates to escort him to the temple of the Eastern Peak. Having arrived, he stopped outside the gate, entered to deliver the document but did not emerge. ■〈王巳〉 looked inside and saw the emperor of the Eastern Peak, wearing a headdress and a brown robe, sitting at the table to handle affairs. Those standing in attendance were all wearing purple robes and gauze hats, numbering in the hundreds, and there were another several hundred people bustling in the courtyard. ■〈王巳〉 thought to himself, "My feet are still sore, and I fear that entering will not withstand the trampling of many people." While hesitating, suddenly someone came out from inside the door and called, "Young master, why are you here?" Looking at him, it was an old servant of the Tang family.

    194

    ■〈王巳〉具说前事，仆曰：「郎君当复生，吾今送归。」■〈王巳〉告以足痛，仆曰：「当觅一舟相载也。」扶■〈王巳〉至岸下一空舟，无头尾，仅有腹，掖登之，缩脚而卧。仆立舟上，不见其鼓棹而舟自动。祠下去家约四十里，顷刻已至，又掖而升岸，回顾，失仆及舟所在。入门，为门限所蹶，惺然而寤，以手扪四壁不可出，已知在棺中也。乃以足蹴其板，家人闻而骇之，亟揭棺盖视，■〈王巳〉已活，距死时四十七日矣。欲扶出之，惫不可起，破棺后一板，始得出。灌以姜汁，气息纔属，而双目昏暗，手足皆伤，厌厌未有生意。方谋迎医，忽有全真道士过门乞斋，闻之，谓其父曰：「吾能治之，但须先炙其胸穴 【 但须先炙其胸穴　原本「胸穴」作「胸曰」，据说库本改。

    Explanation

    194

    ■〈王巳〉 recounted the previous events, and the servant said, "The young man will come back to life, and I will now send him back." ■〈王巳〉 reported his foot pain, and the servant said, "I will find a boat to ferry you." The servant helped ■〈王巳〉 to a boat below the shore, an unusual vessel with no bow or stern, only a hull. They helped him onto it, and he curled up his feet and lay down. The servant stood on the boat, not seeing him row, but the boat moved on its own. From the temple to home was about forty miles, but they arrived in a moment. They helped him back to the shore, and looking back, they lost sight of the servant and the boat. Entering the house, he was knocked over by the door threshold, and he awoke with a start. Feeling the walls, he realized he was in a coffin. He kicked the board with his feet, and the family, startled, quickly lifted the coffin lid. ■〈王巳〉 was already alive, having been dead for forty-seven days. They wanted to help him out, but he was too exhausted to stand. They broke the coffin after a board, and finally, he was freed. They poured ginger juice into him, and his breath was just barely connected. His eyes were dim, and his hands and feet were all injured, showing no signs of life. They planned to bring in a doctor, when suddenly a Daoist priest passed by the door asking for alms. Hearing this, the priest said to his father, "I can treat him, but I must first apply heat to his chest acupoint."

    】 ，若知痛，乃可生也。」父喜引入，■〈艹执火，上中下〉艾炙之。火方燃 【 火方燃　原本「火」作「久」，据说库本改。】 ，遽呼痛，道人曰：「生矣。」然犹不能言。道人出囊中紫药一锭，形制如墨，令研碎以米汁调其半灌之，留半以待昏时服，药尽则能言而行矣。家人如教，治具以待。道人不食，止啖水果数颗及酒三杯而已。抵暮告去，去未久，家人觅所藏药已失之，于是交相尤恨，以为必无生理。诘旦，道人至，告以故，笑曰：「不足惜也。」复出半锭与之，正昨所失者，家人愚，不以为异，赠以十金，道人笑曰：「我方外士，安用金为？」又以布二十疋，曰：「且留之，明日来取。」遂去，竟不复至。■〈王巳〉得生，备述冥中事如此。 【 ■〈王巳〉自为子远说。】

    Explanation

    195

    "If one knows pain, then one can live," the Taoist said. The father, overjoyed, brought the child in and the Taoist performed moxibustion on him. As the fire was just lit, the child immediately cried out in pain. The Taoist said, "He's alive." However, the child still could not speak. The Taoist took out a purple pill from his bag, shaped like ink, and instructed them to grind it into powder and mix half of it with rice water to administer it. The other half was to be saved for consumption at dusk. When the medicine was finished, the child would be able to speak and walk. The family followed the Taoist's instructions and prepared everything as directed. The Taoist did not eat, only consuming a few pieces of fruit and three cups of wine. As dusk approached, he announced that he was leaving. Soon after he departed, the family discovered that the hidden medicine had disappeared. They blamed each other, believing that there was no hope for the child. The next morning, the Taoist returned, and the family told him what had happened. He laughed and said, "It's not worth worrying about." He then produced another half pill, which was exactly the one that had been lost. The family, in their ignorance, did not find this strange, and they gave him ten taels of gold. The Taoist laughed and said, "I am a hermit, what use do I have for gold?" He then gave them twenty bolts of cloth, saying, "Keep it for now, I will come back for it tomorrow." He left, and never returned. ■〈王巳〉 was saved from death, and later detailedly described the events in the afterlife.

    ○张都宪

    　　都御史张公 【 泰】 ，肃宁人，少时貌极丑。尝得危疾，梦其父以罪被逮，当论死，己白于官，请以身代。官听之，即械赴市中就刑，挥刀霍然头落，其魂遂入冥司。见阎君，曰：「此人无罪，应得受生。判生山东民家为男子。」遣吏卒押送。见一大鸡前导，己随而行，其年盖属酉云。至其家，妇适坐蓐，遂投胎而生。既浴，置炕上，家人环视，或指之曰：「好一小儿。」俄身渐长大。又曰：「何讵如许？」遂蹶然而觉，乃长眠榻上，冥然经日矣。旦起，家人视之，皆惊而不识，丰颐伟貌，迥异曩时。公具言所梦，益相怪骇，久之，稍稍察其声音举止与旧不殊，乃信之。公后举进士，历任至今官。 【 顾秀才桧说。】

    Explanation

    196

    ○ Zhang the Grand Censor

    Grand Censor Zhang Gong [Tai], a native of Sucheng, was extremely ugly in his youth. He once fell gravely ill and dreamed that his father was arrested for a crime and was sentenced to death. In the dream, he petitioned the officials, offering himself in place of his father. The officials agreed, and he was shackled and led to the marketplace to face execution. The sword swung, and his head fell off instantly. His soul then entered the underworld, where he met the Judge of Hell. The Judge said, "This man is innocent and should be reborn. He shall be born as a boy in a commoner's family in Shandong." Officials were sent to escort him, with a large rooster leading the way. He followed and eventually arrived at the family's home, where the woman was just giving birth. He was reborn into the world. After bathing, he was placed on a kang. Family members gathered around to look at him, and someone pointed at him and said, "What a good little boy." Soon, his body grew bigger. Another person said, "How could it be like this?" He suddenly woke up and lay in a deep sleep on the bed, remaining unconscious for a whole day. In the morning, when he woke up, his family members were all surprised and did not recognize him. He had a full face and a majestic appearance, greatly different from before. He told everyone about his dream, and they were even more amazed and frightened. After a while, they gradually noticed that his voice and behavior were not much different from before, and then believed him. Later, he passed the imperial examination to become a Jinshi and served in various positions up to his current rank. [As told by the scholar Gu Hui.]

    ○辟疟镜

    　　吴县三都陈氏祖传古镜一具，径八九寸。凡患疟者执而自照，必见一物附于背，其状蓬首黧面，胡涂不可辨。一举镜而此物如惊，奄忽失去，病实时愈。盖疟鬼畏见其形而遁也。世以为宝。至弘治中，兄弟分财，剖镜，各得其半，再以照疟，不复见鬼矣。 【 医者周帷中说。】

    　　○臂龙

    　　旧说大江金山寺有行者，素佻■〈亻达〉。尝昼寝，同袍者戏画一龙于其臂，头角麟鬣，状颇逼真。行者觉而见之 【 行者觉而见之　原本「行」下无「者」字，据说库本补，下文同。】 ，戏曰：「吾寝而臂出龙，岂非天授乎？当黥之以成其异。」乃以针刺而加墨焉。积数月，墨色渐紫，又数月，其纹稍稍隐起，约高一黍米。每风雨之夕，此龙蜿蜒如动，一臂为之摇摇不安，行者病之。他日，澡于江，江水为之开豁数丈，此臂腾掉上下，如非己有者。

    Explanation

    197

    Translation

    Fever-Repelling Mirror

    The Chen family of San Du in Wuxian passed down an ancient mirror, measuring about eight or nine inches in diameter. Anyone suffering from malaria who holds and gazes into the mirror will see an object attached to their back. The object has a wild and unkempt appearance, with a dark and indistinct face. When the mirror is raised, the object seems to be startled and suddenly vanishes, and the illness is immediately cured. It is said that the malaria ghost fears seeing its own form and flees. The mirror is considered a treasure. During the Hongzhi period, when the brothers divided their inheritance, they split the mirror, each getting half. When they used the halves to cure malaria, they no longer saw the ghost. [Reported by the physician Zhou Weizhong.]

    Dragon on the Arm

    According to an old saying, there was a monk at the Jinshan Temple on the Yangtze River who was carefree and unrestrained. One day, while he was sleeping during the day, a fellow monk drew a dragon on his arm as a joke. The monk woke up and saw it. He said playfully, "I slept and a dragon appeared on my arm. Is this not a gift from heaven? I should brand it to make it unique." He then pricked the area with a needle and added ink. After several months, the ink color gradually turned purple. After another few months, the pattern slightly raised, about the height of a grain of millet. Every time there was a storm, the dragon seemed to wriggle as if moving, causing the arm to shake and feel uneasy. The monk was troubled by this. One day, while bathing in the river, the water parted for several zhang, and the arm flapped up and down as if it were not his own.

    198

    行者益以为神，时时潜没水中，见鼋、鼍、鱼、鳖历历在目。一旦自念曰：「金山盘距江心，其下宜有根着，盍探之。」乃下投，穷至江底，见山根大仅数抱，若一柱擎其山焉。因运臂撼之，山为摇卼不止，屋宇皆动。僧怖，以为地震，焚香祝三宝，食顷而定。行者登山，知而窃笑之，旬日乃为同袍道其实，因具言臂龙之神。同袍惊以白长老，长老曰：「此妖人也。」潜诣镇江告官，请煞之，官谓诬罔，不为理。僧惧其为己累也 【 僧惧其为己累也　原本「惧」作「擢」，据说库本改。】 ，醉行者而缢之。行者既亡，龙亦顿逝，讫无灵焉。

    198

    The traveler grew even more revered, often disappearing into the water where he could see turtles, alligators, fish, and crabs clearly before his eyes. One day, he thought to himself, "Mount Jin lies in the middle of the river, and beneath it should have a foundation; why not explore it?" He then dived down and reached the bottom of the river, where he saw the mountain's base was only as wide as several embraces, as if supported by a single pillar. He swung his arm and shook it, causing the mountain to shake violently and the buildings to move. The monk was frightened, thinking it was an earthquake, and burned incense to pray to the Three Jewels. After a meal's time, the situation settled. The traveler climbed the mountain, knowing the truth and secretly laughing at it. After ten days, he told his fellow monks the truth, explaining the divinity of the dragon's arm. The fellow monks were shocked and reported to the elder monk, who said, "This is a demon." The elder monk secretly went to Zhenjiang to report to the authorities, asking them to kill it. The officials dismissed it as a false accusation and did not handle it. The monk feared the traveler would be a burden on him, so he intoxicated and strangled him. After the traveler's death, the dragon suddenly disappeared, and there was no more magic.

    ○九尾龟

    　　海宁百姓王屠与其子出行，遇渔父持巨龟，径可尺余，买归系着柱下，将■〈羔上火下〉之。邻居有江右商人见之，告其邸翁，请以千钱赎焉。翁怪其厚，商曰：「此九尾龟，神物也，欲买放去。君从臾成此，功德一半，是君领取。」因偕往验之。商踏龟背，其尾之两旁露小尾各四，便持钱乞王，王不肯，遂烹作■〈羔上火下〉，父子共啖。是夕，大水自海中来，平地高三尺许，床榻尽浮，十余刻始退。及明午，翁怪王屠父子不起，坏户入视之，但见衣衾在床，父子都不知去向。人或云：害神龟，为水府摄去杀却也。 【 吴人仇宁客彼中，亲见其事。】

    Explanation

    199

    Translation:

    In Hai Ning, a commoner named Wang Tu and his son went out for a walk when they encountered a fisherman carrying a large turtle with a diameter of over a foot. They bought the turtle and tied it to a pillar, intending to roast it. A merchant from Jiangxi, who lived nearby, saw the turtle and told the shopkeeper, asking to buy it for a thousand coins. The shopkeeper was surprised by the high price, and the merchant explained, "This is a nine-tailed turtle, a divine creature. I wish to buy it and release it. If you help me, you will receive half the merit; this is your share." They went together to verify the claim. The merchant stepped onto the turtle's back, and on either side of its tail, four smaller tails were revealed. He then gave the money to Wang Tu, but Wang Tu refused, so they roasted the turtle instead. Father and son ate it together. That night, a sudden flood came from the sea, rising three feet above the ground. All the beds and tables floated, and after more than ten hours, the water receded. By midday the next day, the shopkeeper was surprised that Wang Tu and his son had not risen, so he broke down the door to check on them. He only found their clothes on the bed, but father and son were nowhere to be seen. Some people said that because they had harmed the divine turtle, it was taken away by the water god and killed. [Chou Ning, a guest from Wu, personally witnessed the event.]

    ○鄱阳水神 【 鄱阳水神　纪录汇编本「鄱」作「番」，据说库本改。】

    　　余姚戚澜，字文湍，景泰二年进士，授翰林编修。丁艰服阕上京，渡钱塘江，风涛大作。有绛纱灯数百对，照江水通明，丈夫九人，帕首袴鞾，带剑乘白马，飞驰水面如平地。舟人大恐，戚公曰：「毋惧，吾知之矣。」推窗看之，九人皆下马跪，公问曰：「若辈非桑石将军九弟兄耶？」应曰：「然。」曰：「去，吾喻矣。」皆散。公命舟人返棹，曰：「有事，吾当还。」遂归。抵家，谓家人曰：「某日吾将逝矣。」及期沐浴朝服坐，向九人率甲士来迎，行践屋瓦，瓦皆碎，戈矛旌帜，晃耀填拥。

    The Water Deity of Poyang Lake

    Qi Lan, from Yuyao, whose courtesy name was Wentai, passed the imperial examination in the second year of the Jingtai era and was appointed as an editor in the Hanlin Academy. After completing the mourning period for his parent and returning to the capital, he crossed the Qiantang River when a great storm arose. Hundreds of pairs of red silk lanterns illuminated the river water brightly, and nine men, wearing turbans, trousers, and boots, carrying swords, and riding white horses, flew across the water as if it were flat ground. The boatmen were greatly frightened, but Qi Gong said, "Do not be afraid, I know what is happening." He pushed open the window to look and saw that the nine men had all dismounted and were kneeling. He asked, "Are you not the nine brothers of General Sang Shi?" They replied, "Yes." He said, "Go, I understand now." They all dispersed. Qi Gong ordered the boatmen to turn back, saying, "If there is something, I will return." He then returned home. Upon arriving, he told his family, "On a certain day, I will pass away." On that day, he bathed, dressed formally, and sat down. The nine men led by armored soldiers came to greet him, walking and stepping on the roof tiles, which all broke, with their weapons and banners shining and crowded together.

    201

    有顷， 【 有顷　纪录汇编本作「有项」，据说库本改。】 公卒后，车骑腾踔，前后若有所呵卫者，隐隐入空而灭。后琼山丘文庄公夫人入京，舟过鄱阳湖，夜梦朱衣贵人来见曰：「吾仲深故人戚澜也，见为水神。昨奉天符，应覆数百艘舟，夫人慎毋渡。」觉而舟子方解维欲行，夫人亟止之。瞬息大风，舟行者皆溺。明日夫人乃渡。至京以告文庄，文庄感其意，缄文祭之。戚公之乡人项生侍公渡江，亲见其与九神语，又尝得见丘公祭文。 【 又尝得见丘公祭文　纪录汇编本无「见」字，据说库本补。】

    In a short while, 【有顷　纪录汇编本作「有项」，据说库本改。】 after the public figure passed away, chariots and riders galloped about, as if there were someone guarding in front and behind, disappearing into the void. Later, the wife of Mr. Qi, a distinguished official from Qiongshan, entered the capital by boat, passing over Poyang Lake. At night, she dreamed of a noble person wearing red clothes who appeared and said, "I am Qi Lan, an old friend of Zhong Shen, and I am now a water deity. Yesterday, I received a heavenly command to protect hundreds of boats. Lady, be cautious and do not cross." Upon waking, the boatman was just about to untie the mooring and set off, but the lady quickly stopped him. In an instant, a strong wind arose, and all those on the boat drowned. The next day, the lady crossed the lake. Upon arriving in the capital, she informed Mr. Qi, who was deeply moved by her experience and sealed a memorial to honor him. A fellow villager named Xiang served Mr. Qi in crossing the river and personally witnessed him conversing with nine deities. 【又尝得见丘公祭文　纪录汇编本无「见」字，据说库本补。】

    ○椶三舍人

    　　椶三舍人者，椶缆也。太祖御舟师败陈友谅于鄱阳湖，死者数十万。返还，委椶缆于湖，寃魂凭之，遂能为妖。舟人必祭，否则有覆溺之患。

    　　○马少师

    　　钧州马少师文升，景泰辛未进士，至弘治末，位冢宰，前后历仕五十余年，虽年及耄而精力不衰，后致仕去，正德壬申薨于家。其日，日将晡时，公里人有事从城外归者，道逢公乘肩舆，侍从甚众，自舆中向其人拱手，问所之，曰：「庄上去。」其人归到公门，闻哭声，乃知已捐馆矣。计相见之顷，正其气绝时也。 【 公乡人韩训导说。】

    Explanation

    202

    The Hemp Rope Official

    The Hemp Rope Official, also known as the Hemp Rope, was a bundle of hemp rope. During the reign of the founding emperor, Zhu Yuanzhang, he led a naval force to defeat Chen Youliang in Poyang Lake, resulting in the deaths of tens of thousands. Upon returning, he discarded the hemp rope in the lake. The spirits of the dead attached themselves to it and became capable of causing mischief. Boatmen must perform rituals to appease these spirits; otherwise, they face the danger of capsizing or drowning.

    The Venerable Official Ma

    Ma Wen Sheng, a Venerable Official from Junzhou, passed the imperial examination in the year Xin Wei of the Jingtai era. By the end of the Hongzhi era, he held the position of Grand Councillor and had served for over fifty years. Despite being old, his energy and vigor did not diminish. He later retired and died at home in the year Ren Shen of the Zhengde era. On that day, near dusk, a man from the area was returning from an errand outside the city when he met Ma Wen Sheng riding in a sedan chair, accompanied by many attendants. Ma Wen Sheng bowed from the sedan chair towards the man and asked where he was going. The man replied, "To the village." Upon returning to the city gate, the man heard the sound of crying and realized that Ma Wen Sheng had already passed away. The time of their meeting coincided with the moment Ma Wen Sheng died. [This account was provided by a local official named Han.]
